Current Affairs Commentary

Italian-Abyssinian Relations Intensify Again 30

— Heng

Since Germany announced its rearmament, the European situation has suddenly become serious, causing Italy, which was actively preparing for war against Abyssinia, to slightly shift its attention to Europe. As a result, Italian-Abyssinian relations eased. However, in recent days, due to the results of the Stresa Conference and the establishment of the Franco-Russian agreement, the crisis in Europe has subsided somewhat. Thus, Italy's attitude toward Abyssinia has taken on a bold and decisive air. Italian authorities stated that the Italian government can no longer tolerate the situation in Abyssinia, that Abyssinia is not a country of the same race or religion, and that Italy has a need to clarify the overall situation in Abyssinia. At the same time, Mussolini ordered Italian troops to prepare for war. Judging from his intentions, he seems determined to launch a decisive attack on Abyssinia.

Historically, the countries with interests in Abyssinia have been the United States, France, and Italy. In the late 19th century, Africa was divided among them, but Abyssinia remained independent due to its geographical advantages. At that time, Britain feared that the territory would fall into French hands, so it encouraged Italy to seize it. This aroused French suspicion, and France actively sought Abyssinia's friendship, training its troops and supplying it with arms. Abyssinia's ability to defeat the Italian invasion in 1896 was due to French assistance. After that, Italy's ambition toward Abyssinia was somewhat restrained. However, Britain's desire to control Lake Tsana in Abyssinia, to control the source of the Egyptian Nile, remained undiminished. Therefore, in 1902, it threatened the Abyssinian king to conclude the Anglo-Abyssinian Treaty, obtaining the right to build a dam on Lake Tsana. At the same time, it continued to incite the Italians to attack Abyssinia, hoping to profit from it. However, France at this time always regarded maintaining the territorial integrity of Abyssinia as its mission, and always sought to obstruct the actions of Britain and Italy. For example, the Tripartite Agreement on Abyssinia among Britain, France, and Italy, initiated by France in 1906, was a joint commitment to protect Abyssinia's territorial integrity. Abyssinia's accession to the League of Nations in 1923 was also due to French introduction. In 1925, Chamberlain of Britain attempted to reach an understanding with Mussolini to divide spheres of influence, but failed due to French opposition. Therefore, since the 19th century, the country most concerned about Abyssinia's territorial integrity has been France. As for Britain, although it has no territorial ambitions in Abyssinia, it cannot be without demands for controlling the source of the upper Nile. It is human nature to resent when one's demands are not met, and one may even be happy to use the power of others to satisfy one's own desires. This is why the British often tolerate Italy's plans for Abyssinia.

Given the complex relationship among the three countries regarding Abyssinia, Italy's current actions against Abyssinia would be difficult to carry out without the understanding or tacit consent of Britain and France. The understanding of France is especially essential. Since last summer, due to Germany's rapid expansion in Austria, the contradictions between France and Italy have gradually disappeared. And this spring, the Franco-Italian Rome Agreement was established. Considering that France, in this agreement, allowed the Italians to participate in the management of the railway from the Abyssinian capital directly to French Somaliland, it can be seen that France has actually abandoned its policy of assisting Abyssinia against Italy. This railway is operated solely by France and is the only route for Abyssinia to communicate with the outside world. Abyssinia's foreign trade and the import of arms depend on this route for communication. Now that the Italians can participate in the management of this route, they will be able to deal a great blow to Abyssinia in terms of arms inspection. France has already made its intention not to assist Abyssinia clear by granting this power to the Italians. Furthermore, Abyssinia's repeated appeals to the League of Nations have never been placed on the agenda of the Executive Council. France has great influence in the League of Nations. If it wanted to provide assistance, how difficult would it be? Now it turns a blind eye. What does it mean by that? Also, in fact, France wants Italy to support its various plans to stabilize the European situation, and wants Italy not to assist Austria-Hungary in making things difficult for the Little Entente. It must make great concessions to Italy. This is why it cannot but acquiesce in Mussolini's actions against Abyssinia.

That Italy's current actions against Abyssinia have obtained the unofficial understanding of Britain and France has become an open secret. However, it is still difficult to predict whether Mussolini is determined to use force against Abyssinia. First, the territorial integrity of Abyssinia is recognized by the Anglo-Franco-Italian Tripartite Agreement of 1906. Second, Abyssinia is currently a member of the League of Nations. Britain and France now want to fully maintain and strengthen the League of Nations. How can they permanently sit idly by while Abyssinia is being invaded? Furthermore, what about the Italo-Abyssinian arbitration treaty of 1928? How can they abandon it and ignore it? Third, according to Chamberlain's suggestion to Mussolini in 1925, Italy was only allowed to build a transverse railway in Abyssinia. Beyond this, Britain may not allow it. Moreover, Abyssinia is located in a high plateau with towering mountains and rugged terrain. It is easy to defend and difficult to attack. This has always been the case. In addition, the Abyssinians are brave and warlike. Although the Italians have sophisticated weapons, they cannot be without caution. Therefore, it is speculated that Mussolini may not intend to annex Abyssinia. He just wants to demonstrate force against Abyssinia and coerce it into submission. In recent years, due to the unclear Italo-Abyssinian border, the Italians have nibbled away at Abyssinian territory. In order to maintain these occupied territories, they must adopt a very tough attitude. Moreover, in preparation for a second world war, Italy must actively arouse the war sentiment of its people. The current Italo-Abyssinian dispute is an excellent source of material for cultivating this sentiment. Mussolini, with his penetrating vision, would not easily let go of this great opportunity to encourage national war sentiment.

Abyssinia Completes Mobilization Plan; Tensions High in East Africa; Britain and France, with Interests at Stake, Cannot Remain Silent; Will Jointly Intervene in Italy's Actions 31

(London) Today's news: The British and French governments are currently considering jointly requesting Italian Prime Minister Mussolini not to engage in combat in East Africa. The note may also indicate that Italy's actions are likely to provoke impeachment by the League of Nations' Executive Council. At the same time, news from East Africa suggests that a large-scale war between Italy and Abyssinia seems imminent. According to dispatches from the Abyssinian capital, a national mobilization plan has been completed. If Italy's military preparations do not stop, this plan will be implemented soon. (12th National Dispatch)

(Paris) This newspaper is paying extraordinary attention to the increasingly tense Italo-Abyssinian relations. Because Italy and Abyssinia are both members of the League of Nations, if they resort to arms again, it will inevitably deal another blow to the already declining prestige of the League of Nations. Although officials remain silent on the development of this situation, various newspapers have devoted special space to publishing news from Abyssinia, Rome, and London. It was previously reported that the British and French governments will jointly intervene in Rome's actions to make it accept the arbitration methods suggested by the League of Nations. This news has been confirmed by the "Echo de Paris," which said that Britain opposes Italy's desire to resolve this dispute outside the League of Nations. The London correspondent of "Echo de Paris" also said that the British government firmly believes that Italy has decided to seize the provinces of Harar and Ogaden from Abyssinia. Once this happens, not only will the connection between the port of Djibouti in French Somaliland and the hinterland be severed by Italy, but also the source of the upper Nile River will be controlled by Italy. Therefore, the correspondent believes that the British government will not approve of this. (11th National Dispatch)

(London) The British and French governments will, in the near future, make friendly representations to the Italian government to prevent the conflict between Italy and Abyssinia from becoming increasingly entangled. As for the Abyssinian government, Britain and France will not hesitate to make similar representations. The Abyssinian Emperor has recently sent a note to the Italian government, requesting that the Italo-Abyssinian dispute be submitted to arbitration as soon as possible. The purpose of Britain and France's representations to Italy is to urge Italian Prime Minister Mussolini to make the Abyssinian note produce results. In principle, the submission of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute to arbitration has already been accepted by both Italy and Abyssinia. What London hopes is that Italy will find a way to establish a mixed arbitration committee as soon as possible, so that the Italo-Abyssinian dispute can be eased, and Italy can devote its full strength to resolving the various problems in Europe. (16th Havas Dispatch)

(London) The policies adopted by Italy towards Abyssinia have aroused concern at home and abroad. The "Observer" of London commented that it is impossible to know for sure what the Italian public's mood is like, as the news is divergent. Some believe that many soldiers in the Italian troops sent to Africa have deserted. However, people in Italy say that morale is very high, and more than 30,000 people have voluntarily enlisted in the Italian army. It is only necessary to draw 3% of the total number that can be mobilized in the country to conquer Abyssinia. As for military expenses, the funds for public works can be used, so there is no need to worry about a shortage. After the European War, the Treaty of Versailles entrusted some places to be ruled by the countries of Britain, France, Belgium, Australia, Japan, New Zealand, and South Africa, but Italy did not get anything. This is a difficult matter. (12th Havas Dispatch)

(Rome) After Gong, the Abyssinian police chief of Jijiga, led his subordinates to attack the Italian consulate in November last year, Italy lodged a protest and obtained a solution. Abyssinia also agreed to submit the police chief and others to the court for punishment. Now the Abyssinian government has suddenly released them. Italy believes that Abyssinia lacks sincerity, which is now evident. In addition, it has been confirmed that German reserve officer Stephen is now selling German Junkers aircraft in Abyssinia. (11th Havas Dispatch)

US Navy Conducts Major Maneuvers in the Pacific; Aircraft Carriers Display Power 32

(New York) The Pacific naval maneuvers have begun. Aircraft carriers Langley, Saratoga, Lexington, and Ranger form a team led by Vice Admiral Butler, coordinating with the naval fleet in attacking the Aleutian Islands. The Lexington and Saratoga have higher speeds than battleships, reaching 33 knots per hour. Each carries 33,000 tons and 100 aircraft. Together with Langley (11,500 tons) and Ranger (13,500 tons), they carry 270 aircraft and launch a fierce attack on the enemy. Their power is considerable. (11th Havas Dispatch)

(Honolulu) The US Navy is preparing for aviation exercises. 450 aircraft will depart from various aircraft carriers and fly in formation. 45 seaplanes are conducting secret maneuvers in the Pacific. Naval authorities decline to comment. (11th Havas Dispatch)

Japanese Aviator Attempts Trans-Eurasian Flight; Arrives Safely in Peting from London Yesterday; Takes Route Via India, Siam, Hong Kong, Shanghai, and Reaches Tokyo 33

(London) A British-made aircraft, piloted by Japanese aviator Anno, took off from Heston Aerodrome at 8:20 this morning, intending to set a new solo flight record from London to Tokyo. Many people were at the scene to see him off, including many Japanese. His first stop is Peting, and he will pass through Vienna, Belgrade, Ankara, Baghdad, Karachi, Calcutta, Yangon, Hong Kong, and Shanghai before reaching Tokyo. It is also heard that this flight also aims to establish a new route between Britain and Japan with fewer dangers. This aircraft is a newly built British Hawk aircraft, named "碧海 (Hekikai, Azure Sea)" by Mrs. Matsudaira, the wife of the Japanese ambassador.

(Peting) Japanese aviator Anno, who flew from London to Tokyo, has arrived here, two hours and twenty-one minutes after his departure from England. However, the fuselage was slightly damaged upon landing, and the engine also needs minor repairs. He is expected to continue his flight on Monday. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

Upgrade of Diplomatic Missions to be Realized; Arima Returns Next Month; Hirota Actively Renews Diplomatic Relations with China; Plans to Send Powerful Personnel to China for Inspection 34

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota believes that Sino-Japanese relations have improved, so he decided to order Ambassador Arima to take office as soon as possible and convey the Japanese government's policy. Guangdong Inspection Group Leaves France; Nothing In Paris Inspection Was Not Open to Public View; Completely Contrary to Rumors Fabricated by Certain Parties 35

(Paris) The military inspection group sent by the Guangdong Provincial Government of China, led by Lin Shiqing, commander of the Guangdong Provincial Security Forces, and Du Yiqian, principal of the Guangzhou Military Academy, came to France last month to conduct inspections. Old Seiyukai Faction of Japan Organizes New Party Movement; Internal Shakeup Begins within Seiyukai 37

(Tokyo) Although the Japanese government has been able to organize a cabinet deliberation council and investigation bureau, the executives of the Seiyukai are still taking a non-cooperative attitude, except for the two elders Mizuno and Mochizuki, who violated the party's resolution to participate in its organization. If this continues for a long time, the government will inevitably be oppressed by the majority party Seiyukai when the Diet convenes. Therefore, there is now a discussion within the government to form a new party, that is, to organize a new Seiyukai Alliance with the Kenseikai President Adachi Kenzō, the Tokonami Takeji faction, and Finance Minister Takahashi and others, who were formerly related to the Seiyukai, and to make it its actual work, so that the Tokonami faction and other members who are dissatisfied with the current executives of the Seiyukai will instigate within the party to split it. After that, the trend in the political world will be most interesting with the new party movement. (12th China United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Tokonami faction and the old Seiyukai faction, etc., have decided to launch a movement to establish a new party due to the internal shakeup of the Seiyukai. In form, they will meet at the Hibiya Tao Tao Pavilion on the 14th in the name of a current affairs discussion meeting to discuss future countermeasures. Yesterday, on the 11th, a notice was sent out, inviting more than 80 members, and various movements have already begun. However, the movements of the Minseitō and the Kokumin Dōmei, regarding the destruction of the Seiyukai's form of national unity and the organization of a new party, plan to wait for the public's fair judgment before deciding on a method, because there are many who advocate this self-respecting argument, and they may not be eager to establish a new party and withdraw from the party in large numbers at present. However, Watanabe Go, Kishida Masaji, and others from the Mochizuki faction, and Ito Kaizaburo and others from the Akita faction, are jointly opposed to the left-wing figures of the President faction such as Mukai Iwo, Kuramoto Yōichi, and Namba Kiyoto, and are expected to express their determination to leave the party in the middle of this month. However, the Tokonami remnants and the Hokkaido Federation will take a relatively self-respecting attitude and will not leave the party immediately, but will wait for the establishment of the new party. However, it is not known whether a small number of people will leave the party in the near future. (12th Rengo Dispatch)

Japanese Textile Mills Decide to Reduce Operations 38

(Osaka) The Spinning Federation held a reduction-in-operations committee at the Cotton Industry Hall yesterday to discuss everything. Because the major mills' argument against reduction and the small and medium-sized mills' argument for expansion were at odds, no decision was made. Then, after Chairman Kawabe's decision, the following was decided at 9 p.m.: Production adjustment from July 1 to October 31, increasing one day and night in July and August in addition to the current reduction rate, and increasing 6% from September 1 to the end of October in addition to the current rate. However, this resolution will be implemented only if it is approved by three-quarters of the total number of companies and three-quarters of the total number of spindles in the Federation. This reduction rate is equivalent to a 20% stoppage rate in July and August, and a 22.2% rate in September and October. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

Russian Heavy Industry Conference; Committee Submits Report; Production Volume Greatly Increases 39

(Moscow) The first conference of the Soviet Heavy Industry Committee has opened, chaired by Ordzhonikidze, Chairman of the Heavy Industry Committee. Leaders of various companies and directors of various factories and scientific research institutions attended. The meeting first discussed the balance of the Soviet heavy industry in 1934. According to the report, due to the great improvement in technology, the increase in labor productivity, the reduction in production costs, and the emergence of new industries in the enterprises under the jurisdiction of the Soviet Heavy Industry Committee, the total balance as of January 1, 1935, was about 56 billion rubles (46.678 billion rubles on January 1, 1934). On January 1, 1924, the total balance of the entire Soviet industry (including heavy industry, light industry, timber, food, and other industries) was 4.661 billion rubles. The active results of the industry under the jurisdiction of the Heavy Industry Committee in the previous year were even greater in the increase in total production than in the increase in balance. The production station increased by 28.6%, while the balance increased by 19.3%. This point shows that the Soviet enterprises have made progress in the utilization of the value of machinery and materials. The balance of each part of the heavy industry shows the non-parallel development of the Soviet Union's extremely heavy industry. (11th TASS Dispatch)

Sixth Day of the British King's Accession Anniversary; Grand Celebration in London; Tens of Thousands of Children from the Suburbs Add to the Festivities; The People Compete to See the King's Majesty, Like a Tiding; As Many As Five Hundred People Faint and Fall to the Ground 40

(London) On the last day of the British King's Accession Week, London, Edinburgh, Belfast, and Cardiff all had very lively celebrations. The King sent his sons to the provincial capitals as his representatives. Therefore, the Prince of Wales went to Cardiff, the Duke of York and his Duchess went to Edinburgh, and the Duke of Gloucester went to Belfast. There were extremely enthusiastic expressions of support for the King and the royal family everywhere. Each prince spoke in the provincial capitals, all mentioning the King's concern for the pain of unemployment. The highlight of the London celebrations was the large gathering of tens of thousands of schoolchildren. Thousands of children, led carefully by nannies and teachers, went to the stands on Constitution Hill. The area was designated by the King specifically for children's seating, so that they could see the King's majesty and so on. The London City Council, the Public Works Bureau, the police department, and the railways and streetcars pre-planned ways to transport the children, striving for their comfort. After the children entered the stands, they were entertained by military bands and wireless broadcasts. From Hyde Park Corner to Marble Arch, the whole route was full of children, numbering no less than 15,000. When the King and others drove past, the children cheered continuously. The King and others enjoyed it. At night, the crowds outside the palace cheered for the King and Queen, who appeared on the balcony under the illumination of electric lights for the public to admire. They waved to the crowd for seven minutes. However, there were so many people coming and going outside the palace, estimated to be more than 250,000. When the King and others appeared, they squeezed each other, causing some to fall to the ground and others to faint. Therefore, the King announced that he would no longer appear on the balcony. After this week, the palace will stop burning colored lights, but many shops and private residences in London and the provinces will continue to celebrate with lights. (11th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) At night, the King and Queen appeared on the palace balcony in response to the cheers of the people. At that time, the people competed to see them, like a tidal wave, causing more than 500 people to faint, and many were pushed to the ground. They were treated by temporary emergency medical stations set up next to the Victoria Memorial. Those who were more serious, including a woman with two broken ribs, were sent to the hospital. There were many people visiting the streets with lively lights, especially St. James's Park. The electric lights there were dazzling, and the flowers and trees were even more beautiful. Trafalgar Square became an open-air ballroom at midnight, with the crowd singing and dancing, led by a man standing on the head of a stone lion. They gradually dispersed after being driven away by the police. (11th Reuters Dispatch)

(New York) American famous humorist and movie star Rogers broadcast on the radio today, inviting the British King and Queen to visit the United States. Then he said to the British audience, the King and others may wish to visit this country. You should urge the Prince of Wales to persuade them. The Prince is a good person. Even if they don't come, we should let us know whether there is an opportunity to unite with you in accordance with the Canadian method. We seem to have obtained more freedom than we can handle. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

LADDICK'S DISCOURSE ON THE FRANCO-SOVIET MUTUAL ASSISTANCE PACT 43

(Moscow) Renowned Soviet political commentator LADDICK, in an article in IZVESTIA, stated that the Franco-Soviet pact is of utmost importance, not only as a weapon of peace but also because a capitalist country has unprecedentedly decided to conclude a mutual assistance pact with the first proletarian state that has achieved victory.

LADDICK mentioned documents from the late 19th century, specifically the negotiations between the French Republic and Imperial Russia for an alliance 44 years prior, pointing out the situation of Imperial Russia at the time. He said, "At that time, Russia had to order 500,000 rifles from France because Russia itself could not produce them. Simultaneously, due to the poverty of the national treasury, it had to borrow from another country to repay debts. Russia at that time could not attain an equal position in diplomatic negotiations."

LADDICK continued, "Today's Soviet Union has established industry and agriculture through the strength of its workers and peasants. In this industrialized and collectivized country, the Little Red Army's armaments are all supplied by domestic industry. This army will surely be able to defend its country against any number of enemies. The Soviet government's conclusion of a mutual assistance pact is not because it cannot obtain foreign aid or defend its country on its own but to demonstrate to those who love military adventures that any country wishing to consolidate peace must engage in collective self-defense actions to deal with them. The Soviet government is different from other countries; it has absolutely no aggressive intentions, nor does it wish to exclude any country. Precisely for this reason, the importance of the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance pact is increasingly strengthened and not diminished." (TASS dispatch of the 11th)

(Paris) "CAPITAL JOURNAL" recently published a commentary analyzing the relationship of the Franco-Soviet mutual assistance treaty to Britain, stating that "If Germany were to attack the Soviet Union, and France were to provide assistance to the Soviet Union in accordance with the mutual assistance treaty, would Britain then have an obligation to assist Germany in accordance with the Locarno Treaty? If we interpret the terms of the treaty, the Locarno Treaty does not actually have this kind of constraint, because France's assistance to the Soviet Union is based on the provisions of Article 16 and Article 15, Section 7 of the League of Nations Covenant. The Locarno Treaty itself already stipulates that sanctions actions stipulated by the League of Nations Covenant cannot be regarded as aggression against the territory of another country. Therefore, Britain would have no obligation to assist Germany," (Havas dispatch of the 12th)

GERMAN PARTY TROOPS CROSS INTO FRENCH TERRITORY; ONE OFFICER ARRESTED 44

(Metz, France) Yesterday, a squad of uniformed German National Socialist Party troops crossed the border into France near Merlbach and had lunch at a coffee shop. A French guerrilla soldier arrested one officer, and the rest fled back to Germany. (Havas dispatch of the 11th)

FRANCO-POLISH TALKS CONCLUDE SUCCESSFULLY; MAINTENANCE OF OLD ALLIANCE; NO CONFLICT WITH FRANCO-RUSSIAN AGREEMENT; OBTAINED POLISH UNDERSTANDING THROUGH SINCERE EXPLANATION; LAVAL DEPARTS WARSAW FOR MOSCOW 45

SUPPORT FOR COLLECTIVE SECURITY SYSTEM

(Berlin) The Berlin Stock Exchange Report stated that "French Foreign Minister Laval declared to Polish Foreign Minister Beck that the collective security system is considered necessary by both France and Russia, and Poland should decide whether or not to agree. Beck immediately expressed his agreement. In addition, Laval did not express opposition to Poland maintaining friendly relations with Germany. Laval's trip to Warsaw did not change the general situation on the surface, but Poland has realized that the French government still treats Poland as an allied country, and Poland's position is actually equal to that of the Soviet Union." The National Socialist Party's organ, the People's Observer, stated, "Poland will continue to actively operate in Eastern Europe, because France and Russia are attempting to establish a security system, and Poland cannot remain indifferent, lest the country's current foreign policy be affected." FRANCO-POLISH RELATIONS ARE EASING

Warsaw According to information obtained by our correspondent, the foreign ministers of France and Poland have continued their talks without interruption since yesterday. Relations between the two countries have indeed returned to a state of easing. French Foreign Minister Laval has proven to Colonel Beck that the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact does not conflict with the German-Polish Non-Aggression Treaty, the Russian-Polish Non-Aggression Treaty, and the Franco-Polish Alliance. He also stated that Germany has always expressed its participation in consultative and non-aggression collective pacts, and France is now preparing to promote the establishment of this pact. Poland does not intend to reject this proposal, but on the condition that the country's special interests in the Baltic Sea coast are not despised. Poland also agreed to participate in the negotiations for the Danube River Non-Interference in Internal Affairs Pact and will take advantage of the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting (on the 20th of this month) to go to Geneva to participate in preparatory talks. At that time, Laval will conduct negotiations with representatives from related countries, especially the Little Entente countries, so that the Rome Conference can be successfully concluded. In addition, Laval and Beck also discussed a number of issues related to economic relations between the two countries, such as the treatment that Polish workers can enjoy in France, which is one aspect. (Havas dispatch of the 11th)

EXCHANGE OF SPEECHES BY THE TWO FOREIGN MINISTERS

Warsaw The French Embassy recently hosted a banquet for French Foreign Minister Laval. Laval gave a speech on the spot, stating, "There is no instability or ambiguity in the relationship between France and Poland. Mutual cooperation between the two countries is necessary for the creation of European peace, especially even more so now than in the past. During my talks with Foreign Minister Beck, I proposed guaranteeing that the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact does not conflict with the existing agreements between France and Poland (referring to the alliance) and the existing agreements between Poland and its neighbors (referring to the German-Polish and Polish-Russian non-aggression treaties). Colonel Beck replied, "France and Poland have the same goal, which is to maintain world peace. This goal should be backed by several factors, and Franco-Polish friendship is one of these factors." Beck concluded that the significance of the French Foreign Minister's visit goes far beyond ordinary diplomatic etiquette. (Havas dispatch of the 11th)

MINISTRY OF INDUSTRY DENIES PLANS TO FORM INTERNATIONAL TRADE COMMITTEE 50

(Nanjing) It is rumored that the Ministry of Industry, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs are planning to form an International Trade Committee to study balancing international trade. According to officials in charge of the Ministry of Industry, this is not true. The so-called balancing of international trade means that the value of imports and exports is equal, in other words, reducing the trade deficit. However, in reality, the content is extremely complex. The important points are the expansion of domestic production and the flexibility of tariff policies, which are all integral to the issue and cannot be effectively achieved by organizing a Balanced Trade Committee. The Ministry of Industry is currently directing the International Trade Bureau in Shanghai to conduct basic work on international trade issues. (Special dispatch of the 12th)

Tianjin-Pukou Railway: Employee Traffics Narcotics - Case Cracked in Jinan 77

Jinan Dispatch: The Jinan Station Investigation Team of the First Route of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway recently received a confidential report stating that Hu Yanyu, a luggage clerk of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, was privately carrying a large quantity of narcotics from Tianjin to Jinan for sale. He was on the 75th train, which was scheduled to arrive in Jinan at around 11:00 AM. Niu Zhensan, the investigation officer of the team, immediately notified the station the previous night (the 10th) at around 11:00 PM before the 75th train entered the station, requesting the station to dispatch the deputy station master and the section chief of the railway police department, as well as investigators from the team, ten soldiers with pistols, and Tianjin-Pukou Railway police to wait at the station in preparation for inspection. At 11:40 PM, the train entered the station. Niu Zhensan and others immediately went to the luggage car and strictly guarded both doors. Together with the deputy station master of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway and the railway police, they began the inspection. In addition to the luggage clerk Hu Yanyu, there were also Kang De, a dismissed Tianjin-Pukou Railway worker, and Tian Shuifa, a dismissed tea server, who were secretly transporting goods on the train. The car contained Hu Yanyu's leather suitcases and fresh goods, shoes, children's toys, and other items. The investigation team, together with the railway personnel, opened all the items and conducted a thorough inspection. Hu Yanyu, seeing the large number of soldiers and police and realizing the seriousness of the situation, immediately changed his expression, panicking and at a loss. The suspicion of the investigators grew, and the search became more stringent. As expected, 380 packets of heroin were found in Hu's suitcase. The narcotics were confiscated, and the suspect was arrested. Kang De and Tian Yongfa, who were on the same train, were also considered highly suspicious and were arrested as well. At around 1:00 AM this morning (the 11th), they were escorted to the military law department of the headquarters for interrogation. After receiving the case, the military law department, led by military judge Zhang Tieqiao, conducted a rigorous interrogation at around 9:00 AM this morning. Hu Yanyu was interrogated first. According to his confession, "I am 36 years old, from Yixian County, Hebei Province. I have been working at the Tianjin-Pukou Railway since 1919 and am currently a luggage clerk. I bought raw heroin twice in Tianjin last month, totaling 300 yuan. This time, I bought three and a half, weighing twelve taels, worth 200 yuan. The total value of the three purchases is about 500 yuan, of which 150 yuan belongs to Liu Baoqing and 300 yuan to Zhang himself. Kang De and Tian Yongfa do not own any of the heroin. The fresh goods, shoes, and other items are what they were selling. What I have confessed is the truth." Next, Kang De was interrogated. According to his confession, "I am 60 years old, from Shanhaiguan, and currently reside in Tianjin. I used to work on the railway but was dismissed. Because I know many people on the railway, I travel back and forth with the train to sell goods. This time, I bought some ice cream cones and children's toys from Tianjin to sell. I have never carried raw heroin. As for Mr. Hu's heroin, I know nothing about it. What I have confessed is the truth." Tian Yongfa also confessed, "I am 24 years old, from Shenxian County, Hebei Province. I used to work as a tea server on the railway but no longer do. Now, I follow the train to sell some fresh goods to earn some money. As for the heroin, I really don't know anything about it. What I have confessed is the truth." (11th)

Page 7

Important Communist Bandit Leaders Qu Qiubai and Others Captured in Western Fujian, Along with Female Bandits Zhou Yuelin and Zhang Liang; Deng Zihui Escapes, He Shuheng Killed, Xiang Ying Reportedly Captured in Xingguo, Jiangxi 78

Xiamen Dispatch: Among the top Communist Party leaders, Qu Qiubai, the General Secretary of the pseudo-Central Party Headquarters, whose position was second only to Mao Zedong, a pseudo-Central Executive Committee member, and Chairman of the Education People's Committee of the pseudo-Central Soviet Government, was recently discovered to have been captured by the 14th Security Regiment at Lutan, five miles west of Shuikou, at the intersection of Changting and Shanghang. At the same time, Zhang Liang, the wife of pseudo-Central Government Vice Chairman Xiang Ying, and Zhou Yuelin, the wife of Liang Baitai, the pseudo-Central Government Minister of Internal Affairs and a pseudo-Central Committee member and Minister of Women's Affairs, were also captured. Zhong Shaokui, the commander of the 14th Regiment, escorted the two female bandits, Zhou and Zhang, to the Longyan Second District Pacification Headquarters for interrogation on the 7th. The following is a record of the capture of the Qu bandit and others:

When the Red bandits abandoned western Jiangxi and fled, Qu Qiubai was seriously ill, and Zhang Liang was pregnant and unable to follow. Both remained in Tangwu, Huichang. Later, due to the National Army's search and suppression, they could not establish a foothold. Therefore, the pseudo-Fujian Military Region (now eliminated) dispatched a company of pseudo-special agents to escort them back to the so-called rear area of Yongding and Longyan. In addition to Qu, Zhou, and Zhang, there were Deng Zihui, Chairman of the pseudo-Central Finance People's Committee, He Shuheng, a member of the pseudo-Central Executive Committee, another person from Yongding, a party of six, and the pseudo-special agent company. When they reached Lutan, five miles from Shuikou at the intersection of Ting and Hang, they crossed the river and advanced. The Zhong Regiment was originally stationed in Wuping County and the western district of Shanghang County, and happened to be patrolling near Shuikou. They received a report from the villagers that bandits were passing through. They led their troops to suppress and surround the bandits, seizing many guns, killing several bandits, and capturing several bandits. At that time, Zhang Liang falsely claimed to be Zhou Yulian, the wife of a mushroom merchant, who had been kidnapped and extorted by the Red bandits. Qu falsely claimed to be Lin Qixiang, a hospital doctor, and Zhou falsely claimed to be Chen Xiuying, a female nurse at the hospital. This happened at the end of March, and Dun Chu did not know that these three were the top bandits. Coincidentally, there was a conscript in the regiment who had been captured in the northern district of Wuping and had surrendered. One day, during the interrogation of Qu and others, the conscript happened to pass by the hall and was asked if he recognized the prisoners. The soldier had been to Ruijin. After being asked, he nodded and withdrew to another room, informing that one of the women was Zhang Liang. Zhong became very attentive to this. He interrogated Qu and others again, but Zhang still denied it. The soldier came out to confront her, and she finally confessed. However, Zhang still did not reveal Qu and Zhou. Later, the 36th Division of Changting obtained information from the captured Chairman of the pseudo-Zhaozheng County Soviet that Qu and others had been captured. At the same time, the Second District Pacification Department received a telegram from Tao, the commander of the 8th Division, stating that a captured bandit had confessed that Qu Qiubai and others had been captured by the National Army at Shuikou. They telegraphed Commander Zhong to investigate and reply. The captured bandit confessed that the special agent company escorted Qu and others, and each person had a Mauser pistol with them. And those seized that day were indeed Mauser pistols, so it was believed that Qu should have been captured. Song, the commander of the 36th Division, telegraphed to have Qu escorted to Changting so that the captured bandits could identify him. After Zhang confessed that she was Zhang Liang, the Zhong Regiment Headquarters treated Zhang and Zhou very favorably. Later, Zhou Yuelin, grateful for the preferential treatment, confessed everything. Only then did they know that the person named Lin Zuxiang was indeed Qu Qiubai. Therefore, Zhang and Zhou were escorted to Longyan, and sedans and horses were prepared for them to ride. After arriving in Longyan, the two female prisoners were interrogated by the military law department of the Second District Pacification Headquarters on the night of the 7th, and they confessed in detail. Only then did they learn that He Shuheng was killed on the spot, Deng Zihui had escaped, Deng was from Longyan, was more agile, and was familiar with the Hakka dialect of Longyan and Yongding, so he was able to slip through the net. Zhou and Zhang are currently detained in the cavalry company of the 10th Division in Longyan. Qu Qiubai will be escorted from Changting to Longyan. Qu was the leader of the pro-Russian faction of the Communist Party. After Chen Duxiu was expelled, Qu took his place as the Secretary of the pseudo-Central Party Headquarters and was known as the "Russian expert." The following are the confessions of Zhou and Zhang regarding their work in the Communist Party and their capture with Qu:

Zhou Yuelin Confesses

My surname is Zhou, my name is Yuelin. After being captured this time, I used the false name Chen Xiuying. I am 28 years old this year, from Ningbo, Zhejiang. I am the wife of Liang Baitai, the pseudo-Minister of Internal Affairs. When I was over ten years old, I was a female worker at the Dakang Yarn Factory opened by the Japanese in Shanghai. The May Thirtieth Massacre occurred in 1925, and all the factories went on strike. At that time, Li Lisan presided over the General Labor Union, and the workers of all factories were mostly under his command. In June of the same year, I was introduced to the Communist Party and assigned to work in the Second Office of the Labor Union. In 1926, the General Labor Union sent me and Gu Chengzhang and others to Russia. All travel expenses were provided by them. My level was very poor, so I stayed in Vladivostok to attend a primary Soviet school. What I learned was all basic subjects, such as arithmetic, Chinese, and Russian alphabet. Coincidentally, Liang Baitai was working in the Soviet Party Department in Vladivostok. I met and married him. Liang Baitai was sent to law school. In the winter of 1929, I went to Moscow alone, intending to enter a school if possible, otherwise I would return to Vladivostok. When I arrived in Moscow, I found the Chinese delegation and was introduced to the Lenin Academy for accommodation. At that time, there were no enrollments yet, and I had to wait until the summer of the following year to enter the school. The following year (1930), I officially entered the accelerated program of the Lenin Academy. The accelerated program was divided into Chinese, German, French, English, and other classes. I lived in a room with an English girl, a German girl, and an African girl. The English and African girls entered the English class, the German girl entered the German class, and I entered the Chinese class. The subjects I learned were deeper, including politics, economics, and society. Because of my weak health, I went to southern Russia to recuperate. Liang Baitai telegraphed from Vladivostok, instructing me to return to China with him. We stayed at the Zhejiang Hotel in Shanghai. The pseudo-Central Committee sent a liaison officer to the hotel to contact Liang to work in the bandit area. I asked to go with him and was allowed, but I suddenly fell ill, so Liang went first. A month later, after I recovered, I went from Shanghai to Hong Kong, via Shantou and Dabu, to the bandit area. It happened to be the first Soviet Congress, and Liang and I attended as observers. The pseudo-Central Committee, considering that Liang had studied law, ordered him to work in the pseudo-Ministry of Justice. Zhang Guotao, the pseudo-Minister of Justice, was not in Ruijin, so Liang was actually responsible for the ministry's affairs. Liang proposed that I be a Central Labor Inspector and also the Director of the Women's Improvement Committee, but both positions were empty shells with nothing to do. Later, Qin Bangxian and Zhang Wentian came from Shanghai and believed that the Women's Improvement Committee had no organization. At the same time, the pseudo-government did not yet have a Women's Department, so they established one and I became the Minister. The responsibility of the Women's Department was to inspect the results of women's movements in various places and review their reports. I was inherently not suited for this kind of work, and Liang also thought it was inappropriate. Coincidentally, Dean Fu of the National Hospital had a violent temper and did not care about the patients' opinions, so I was appointed Dean. At the Second Soviet Congress, I was elected as a member of the pseudo-Central Executive Committee, a member of the Presidium, and also a member of the Workers' and Peasants' Inspection Committee, but all of the above were only nominal, and there was actually no work to do. All kinds of powers were in the hands of Zhu, Mao, Xiang, and Zhang. Last October, the pseudo-Red China Daily suddenly published an editorial stating that the Fourth Front Army of Yu, E, and Wan, led by Xu Xiangqian, had entered Sichuan, and we should also respond, which aroused suspicion among many people. I worked in the hospital and knew nothing about the westward flight plan. Liang Baitai also did not know. When the bandits fled westward, it was called organizing a field army. Half a month after the field army set off, Xiang Ying suddenly issued a notice ordering the dissolution of the National Hospital and the return of the patients. At this time, Liang Baitai and Xiang Ying were in the same place. Liang told me, "Your body is not well, and you can't walk. You can pretend to be a member of the masses and hide." So he took a letter of introduction from the Organization Department and went to Tangwu Fujian Provincial Soviet. In Tangwu, I saw Chairman Liao (name unknown). He sent me to Jin Fang to live in the home of a Mr. Xie. The township Soviet received an order from the provincial Soviet to give me a dan of grain husks every two months. The first time, I was given four dan. Mr. Xie also did not know who I was, but only knew that I was a refugee. Life was extremely difficult, with no oil or salt to eat. The Fujian Provincial Soviet, because Jin Fang was oppressed by the National Army, instructed me to go to Tangwu to decide what to do. In the Tangwu Provincial Soviet, I met Qu Qiubai, He Shuheng, Deng Zihui, Zhang Liang, and another person from Yongding. The provincial Soviet wanted the six of us to go to Yongding to work with the masses, so as not to have nowhere to settle down. There were five soldiers with box cannons escorting us. At the end of March, we were discovered near Shuikou in Wuping and captured. I and Qu Qiubai and Zhang Liang were captured, Deng Zihui and others escaped, their whereabouts unknown. After arriving at the 14th Security Regiment, I heard the soldiers say that an old man was injured and refused to leave, so he was shot and killed. That old man was He Shuheng. Only then did I know that He had been killed. I gave the name Chen Xiuying at the regiment headquarters. After repeated inquiries, I was grateful for the preferential treatment, so I revealed the truth and was escorted to Longyan with Zhang Liang. Qu Qiubai was escorted to Tingzhou. I have not heard from Liang Bailiu since we separated. I still have two sons in Russia, one named Yisuoka and one named Weilin, now eight and seven years old. They were sent to a nursery as soon as they were born and raised. I have never communicated with them since I returned to China, and I don't know what they look like now. As for the letter of repentance, I will write and submit it separately."

Zhang Liang Confesses

My surname is Zhang, my name is Liang, my original name is Zhang Lianyu. I am from Luoshan, Sichuan, and I am 30 years old this year. When I was young, I married Guo Jian as my wife. Guo Jian's alias is Maoliang. He is from Jiading, Sichuan, and runs a salt well as a business. His family is quite wealthy. In 1925, Guo and I went to Shanghai. Guo wanted to find work, and I entered Qinyie Women's Normal School to study, but my level was low, and I could not pass the exam. So I entered the school as a tutor, working and studying part-time. Guo soon returned to Sichuan and did not come to Shanghai. I had no money to use, so I looked for my fellow villagers Zhang Zidou and Liu Jing. Zhang introduced me to work in his Zhonghua Industrial Factory. The May Thirtieth Massacre occurred, and the factories went on strike for three days. After the resumption of work, the labor union was established, and I joined the labor union. Guo Luzhen, a female graduate of Peking University, asked me if I wanted to study. I answered that I was willing. In 1926, the labor union sent me to Moscow to enter Oriental University. Because my level was too shallow, I only entered the literacy class to study Chinese. Soon after, I fell ill and returned to Shanghai to recuperate in 1927. At this time, my relationship with the Party had been interrupted. I had to find a fellow villager's home to recuperate. Soon after, the Zhabei riot occurred. After the failure, I found the Zhabei District Committee again and rejoined the Party. This was in June. I was sent to Wuhan to work in the labor union as an inspector. After the split between the Kuomintang and the Communist Party, I returned to Shanghai and made a living by stringing pearl flowers. Three months later, I met an acquaintance and re-established contact with the Party. Ms. Wang Yazhang, who was originally the Minister of Women Workers of the Wuhan General Labor Union, introduced me to Xiang Ying. Soon after, we got married. Xiang was working in the Labor Union Federation. Soon after, Xiang was sent to the Soviet Union. I went back to work in the factory. Because I was pregnant, I rented a place in the General Labor Union with a subsidy of seven yuan per month. In 1929, Xiang returned from Russia, and I gave birth to a girl. The subsidy was increased by five yuan per month. Xiang was still working in the Labor Union Federation. In 1930, Xiang came to the bandit area. I was still in Shanghai. In 1932, I entered the bandit area via Hong Kong and Dabu, and I was assigned to be a labor inspector. At this time, I was pregnant again and could not work. So I went to the Party school to study for a month and a half. After leaving the school, I translated ordinary telegrams for the pseudo-Central Committee. In March 1932, I gave birth to a boy. Xiang Ying and I often quarreled. Xiang never talked to me about anything. He often said, "Do I have to tell my wife everything?" Last October, after the field army set off, the Central Government Rear Office was established, with Xiang as the director. There was a standing committee in the office, with Xiang, Deng Zihui, He Shuheng, Liang Baitai, and others as members. Qu Qiubai had severe lung disease and could not work and suffered from headaches. The office was first in Meikeng and later moved to Gaoweinao. I was pregnant and suffered greatly from the travel. The one-year-old boy I gave birth to last year died from illness due to traveling in the wind and snow. On January 10 this year, Xiang Ying told me to pretend to be a member of the masses and hide. I asked him where to go. He said he was also going to the field army. I and Qu Qiubai, He Shuheng, Deng Zihui, and others took letters of introduction to the Fujian Provincial Soviet in Tangwu. Deng Zihui handled everything. I heard that Chairman Liao of the Provincial Soviet sent us to Yongding. The next day, Zhou Yuelin came and we went together. We were captured by the 14th Security Regiment in Shuikou. Those captured were me, Qu Qiubai, and Zhou Yuelin. Deng Zihui and another person from Yongding had escaped. He Shuheng was heard to have been killed. After arriving at the regiment headquarters, I heard the soldiers say that an old man had been shot and killed, and it could be concluded that it was He. At the regiment headquarters, I gave the name Zhou Lianyu and was sent to the county government for custody. A merchant without a son heard that I was pregnant and guaranteed me to go out to give birth. The child born would be his. I was guaranteed to stay in his store. Because Zhou Yuelin had already told the truth, we were escorted here together. As for Xiang Ying's news, I have not heard from him for a long time. I will write a letter of repentance separately, but I am not good at writing and do not know many characters, so it is difficult for me to write. Can I dictate it to be written for me?"

According to news from Ganzhou from the Longyan area, Xiang Ying was besieged by the Fourth Division in Wantianshali, Ruijin, and fled to Guantian in Xingguo, where he was captured alive by the local militia in a desperate situation. Xiang Ying successively served as the Chairman of the pseudo-Military Commission and a member of the pseudo-Central Committee. When Zhu and Mao fled westward, Xiang presided over the remaining bandits. (May 12th)

Hebei Special Police Enter the War Zone - 10,000 Troops to be Stationed in the War Zone; Liu and Zhao Security Teams to be Reorganized 79

Tianjin Dispatch: Negotiations on the rotation of security teams in the war zone have been going on for years. Only on the 10th of this month was an agreement finally reached. The newly organized First and Second Regiments of the Hebei Province Special Police began to move on the 10th. The First Regiment, led by Zhang Qingyu, marched from the Caicun defense area towards Tongxian, camping in Yanjiao that night. On the morning of the 11th, they entered the war zone, passing through Yutian, and then divided into Jixian, Shunyi, Sanhe, Huairou, and Miyun to take over defense. The regiment headquarters is located in Yutian County, with the First District Headquarters in Jixian and the Second District Headquarters in Shunyi. The First Regiment of the original security team stationed in the five counties of Ji, Huai, Zun, Mi, and Shun, led by Fan Yongxiang, will leave the war zone after handing over the defense. They will gather in Matou Village, Tongxian, and transfer to Pingnanyuan, where they will be disbanded and then head to northern Hubei, still under the command of Liu Duoquan's original division. The Third Security Regiment stationed in Yutian, led by Zhou Yuying, will move to Zunhua and Qian'an. Part of this team is also stationed in Funing, Qinhuangdao, Haiyangzhen, and Beidaihe. After the special police of Zhang Yantian's team take over the defense, they will also be transferred to Zun and Qian to be responsible for bandit suppression for a period of two months. After the banditry is eliminated, they will return to the war zone and return to their original divisions and brigades. This is the step-by-step movement of the new and old teams in the Ji-Mi area, which will take about a week to complete. The Second Regiment of the Special Police, led by Zhang Yantian, boarded the train from the Cangxian defense area at 5:00 PM on the 10th. Due to the lack of vehicles on the Tianjin-Pukou and Beining railways, only two trains were allocated, one with twenty open cars and the other with seventeen. The train carrying the first batch of troops was attached to the Tianjin-Pukou No. 402 slow train and departed at 6:30 PM. It passed through Tianjin at around 0:40 AM on the 11th, stopped briefly, and headed east, entering the war zone via Tangshan on the evening of the 11th. The second batch of troops departed at 9:00 PM on the 10th, passed through Tianjin at around 7:00 AM on the 11th, and headed east, entering the war zone that night. They got off along the designated defense area and went to Funing, Lulong, Haiyangzhen, Qinhuangdao, Fengrun, and other places to take over defense. At the same time, the Second Regiment of the old security team, led by Yang Yucheng, gathered at Liushouying, Changli, and took the vehicles transporting the special police, leaving the war zone that day and returning to their original defense area in Junliangcheng. The Second Regiment of the Special Police set up its headquarters in Liushouying, with the First District Headquarters in Qian'an and the Second District Headquarters in Funing. Changli and Leting defense areas - there was originally a proposal to have the First Regiment of the War Zone Security Force, led by Liu Zuozhou, fill the defense, but it has been decided not to station any troops there for the time being. The surplus of several hundred men from Liu Zuozhou's team will be reorganized after the new and old teams are rotated, and then a part will be sent to Changle. However, due to the difficulty in allocating vehicles, it will take more than ten days to complete the deployment of Zhang Yantian's team, which requires seven trains. The troop rotation in the Yu area is more complicated than that in the Su-Mi area. It is difficult to say whether there are still twists and turns in the middle. Da Mu, Ishii, and Douxie, staff officers of the Japanese Army Command in Tianjin, accompanied by Jiangtou, and accompanied by Yin Rugeng and Tao Shangming, went to Tongxian and Tangshan early on the 9th to take an attitude of inspecting the special police entering the war zone to ensure that the number of people and guns met the agreed number.

After the special police enter, the troops stationed in the war zone in the future will include 5,000 men from Zhang Qingyu and Zhang Yantian's teams, still called the First and Second Regiments of the Hebei Province Special Police, so as not to be limited to permanent stationing in the war zone and can be transferred to other counties at any time. Liu Zuozhou and Zhao Lei's teams each have 2,000 men, still called the First and Second Regiments of the Hebei Province War Zone Security Force, limited to stationing in the war zone to maintain local security. Li Yunsheng's team has 1,000 men, called the Hebei Province War Zone Security Supplementary Regiment, also limited to stationing in the war zone. However, the three teams of Liu, Zhao, and Li must be reorganized to meet the provincial regulations on the number of personnel. Zhou Yuying's team has 2,000 men, originally called the Third Regiment of the Hebei Province Security Force, with the same organization as the two teams of Fan Shuihe and Yang Yucheng, which were transferred out of the war zone. After Fan and Yang leave, Zhou will only temporarily remain in the war zone and will be transferred out in a short time. The actual statistics of the war zone troops total 10,000 men. As for the unification of the names and numbers of the teams, the province has no intention of doing so, because the special police under the two Zhangs are organized as one regiment, with two district teams under its jurisdiction, and three large teams under each district team. The two teams of Liu and Zhao have four large teams directly under each regiment, and Li Yunsheng's team has three large teams under one regiment. The number of people and organization are different, so it is also difficult to unify the numbers and names. (11th)

Remnant Bandits Roaming Through the Border Between Hubei and Anhui - The Main Force Has Been Pursued and Eliminated by Liang Guanying's Troops; Local Militias in Huangmei and Other Counties Blocked and Killed Bandit Leaders 80

Hankou Dispatch: The remnant bandits in the border area of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui have recently roamed through Susong and Taihu counties in Anhui, and Qichun and Huangmei counties in Hubei. They have been largely eliminated by Liang Guanying's troops. The local militias of various counties assisted in blocking and killing many bandit team leaders and followers, which was also quite effective. Previously, more than 1,000 remnant troops and guns of the pseudo-28th Army sneaked into Erlang River in Susong County, Anhui Province, in the middle of last month, with the intention of invading eastern Hubei. Huangmei County, only fifty miles away from the area, was particularly vulnerable. The people had long been disturbed by the bandits and were easily frightened, fleeing in droves. Wu Dehuai, the county magistrate of Huangmei, learned that the bandits would enter the territory and immediately mobilized the second battalion commander Chen Weizhen, the sixth company commander Cai Shie, the armed police captain Wu Huating, and the district chief Deng Fuchang to lead the local militia, police force, and volunteer team to Tingqianyi to prevent the bandits from entering. The bandits, after arriving near Tingqian, did not dare to attack lightly and detoured through Changxi Mountain in Susong into Maojiaju and Wang Yuchong in Qichun County. The third battalion commander Huang Liwu stationed in the county engaged in interception and suppression, and the troops of the 25th Route Army also followed and pursued. The bandits, with enemies on both sides, fled south to Tangjiashan and Wangjiashan at the junction of Qi and Huang, intending to continue south to Chengshengyi in northern Huangmei, or to Baiyangling via Jiandao, because the area is mountainous and suitable for occupying. At this time, the Tingqian militia stationed in Huangmei was transferred by the county magistrate's order to Chengshengyi and Baiyangling day and night to establish a strict defense. They announced that the Guangji County militia would come to support, and the people who had fled saw the arrival of the large forces and returned home one after another. The old and weak helped with guarding, and the able-bodied men participated in the blocking and suppression. The bandits, fearing being surrounded if they went deeper, changed their plan again. On the 20th, they turned northeast between Tangwang Mountain and fled back to Susong and Taihu. The three counties of Qichun, Huangmei, and Guangji in eastern Hubei were all spared from banditry. Now, the three counties of Qi, Huang, and Guang are carrying out large-scale cleanups at the same time. Except for Guangji, which has no bandits, there is a group of about 60 or 70 people hidden in Yanshouan on the border of Qi and Huang, and a group of about 50 or 60 people in Huangzhuguo. On the 21st, the county magistrate of Huangmei directed the local militia and volunteer team to search Yanshouan, killing a pseudo-team leader named Zhang Hu and more than ten bandits on the spot, and seizing a red flag, bandit hats, clothing, and other items. They then took advantage of the victory to search Huangzhuyuan, but the bandits had already fled and disappeared. At this point, there were no bandit traces in eastern Hubei. The bandits who fled back to the Anhui border were also caught up and severely damaged by Liang's army and have now been eliminated. (11th)

JINAN AREA - DISCOVERY OF IRON ARTIFACTS FROM THE ZHOU DYNASTY - THE GREATEST FIND IN ARCHAEOLOGICAL HISTORY 81

Jinan Correspondence: Ancient Chinese implements initially consisted of stone and pottery. Bronze was first used during the Shang Dynasty. As for ironware, although it initially appeared in Guanzi's "Qingzhong Pian" (Essays on Economic Policy), there were only written records, and no actual artifacts have been seen. Wu Dacheng once obtained an iron coin mold from the Zhou Dynasty, which was already considered a rare treasure. Among other ironware discoveries, the earliest was the iron voucher from the Qin Dynasty. Ironware from before the Qin Dynasty is extremely difficult to obtain. When ironware was invented remains a major question for archaeologists due to a lack of supporting evidence. Unexpectedly, recently in Xiaonanying, 80 li (about 25 miles) southeast of Jinan City, four pieces of Zhou Dynasty ironware were discovered, representing an unprecedented major harvest in Chinese archaeological history. The details are recorded as follows:

Xiaonanying, 80 li southeast of Jinan City, was formerly named Panlong Village, and is now called Xiaonanying. Four li north of the village is Danan Village. According to local legend, the Song Dynasty general Yang Ye stationed his camp here, hence the name Xiaonanying Village. Some days ago, farmers in the village discovered an ancient tomb about half a li southwest of the village. After digging two meters deep, they found many human bones, including what appeared to be skull, rib, and shin bones, as well as numerous bronze artifacts, categorized and arranged: spears were placed together, and swords were placed together. Most remarkably, there were two spear-shaped weapons, which had never been seen before. Each had a handle, all made of bronze. Northwest of the bronze artifacts, about half a meter away, three or four hoe-shaped iron tools and one guillotine-shaped iron tool were found, extremely thick and large, with holes in the handle. There was also a stone implement, shaped like a teacup. The farmers, seeing that the iron was rusty and thinking it had no value, only brought the bronze artifacts to the provincial capital for sale. Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, purchased them and recognized them as Zhou Dynasty bronze artifacts. He repeatedly inquired if there were any other items. The farmers then revealed that there were also the aforementioned iron tools. Upon hearing this, Wang was overjoyed. He inquired further and learned it was an ancient tomb, as the villagers were initially afraid of being punished for digging up a tomb and were reluctant to speak. Wang immediately instructed the farmers to send the iron tools to the library for research. The farmers, thinking that a pile of scrap iron was worthless, readily agreed. The co-location of bronze and iron artifacts has not been found in Yin Ruins (near Anyang), making this the first such find. The presence of ironware from the Zhou Dynasty can be proven by the Zhou Dynasty bronze artifacts, making this an important discovery in Chinese archaeological history.

SONGJIANG - COUNTY GOVERNMENT STRICTLY PUNISHES SOIL PEDDLERS 82

In this county, the peddling of illicit soil has always been managed by a few northerners residing in Songjiang, whether they were veterans or residents from other places. They all made a living by peddling soil. Since this province implemented the ban on opium, these guest residents engaged in illicit soil peddling have not reduced their activities in the slightest, continuing to traffic it as before, causing the official opium dens' business to plummet, making it impossible to maintain. Previously, detectives apprehended Sha Baozhong, a well-known guest resident engaged in illicit soil peddling, seizing thirteen taels of illicit soil. He was handed over by the Anti-Opium Committee to the county government for interrogation. Yesterday (the 11th), Zhu Yiyi, the section chief of the county government, sentenced Sha Baozhong to ten years of imprisonment. As for the soil trafficker Liu Shuye who was apprehended, yesterday, Yao, the secretary of the County Anti-Opium Committee, Zhou Mian, the inspection section chief, and He Runzhang, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, led a team to Liu Shuye's home and searched it again, finding another package of soil, weighing one tael. The house where the Liu family lived was originally sealed off with three seals, but after yesterday's inspection, only the main door was sealed. The county's determination to ban opium is evident from this.

WUXI - STARVING PEOPLE IN DISASTER AREAS DIG FOR SMILAX CHINA ROOT 83

Last year's severe drought caused widespread suffering. The disaster was especially severe in the Anzhen Jiaoshan area of the seventh district of this county. The terrain there is relatively high, and last summer's severe drought left the fields barren, leading to a food shortage. The farmers' livelihood was almost exhausted, and they lacked grain to eat. Since the beginning of spring, the panic has worsened. Many farmers have gone to the foot of Jiaoshan Mountain to dig for Smilax china roots (also known as Guanyin vine, yellow in color and hard in texture). They wash off the mud, soak it in clean water to remove the red color, cut it into thin slices, and dry it in the sun. After it is dried, they grind it into powder, remove the rough outer skin, and make cakes to fill their stomachs. In the Dongfeng Huadafang Village area of the third district, farmers are also suffering from food shortages. Since the beginning of spring, they have eaten almost half of the rice seeds they had stored from last year for spring planting. Others grind soybean cakes and corn into flour and cook it to eat. The poorest people have to divide one soybean cake to eat over five or six days.

HURRICANE STRIKES WUXI AND CHANGSHU AREAS 84

Yesterday morning (the 12th) at 1:15 AM, the southeast corner of the city was suddenly covered in dense black clouds and faint lightning, as if a thunderstorm was about to descend. Before long, a hurricane struck, flying sand and stones, like ten thousand horses galloping. Pedestrians on the road were nearly knocked over, many glass windows were shattered, streetlights were all extinguished, trees were broken and uprooted, creating extremely dangerous conditions. Electrical wires were broken, houses collapsed, and people were injured, causing very serious losses. Around 2:00 AM, the wind began to subside. The various situations are recorded below:

Outside the Guangfu Gate, at the Zikang Silk Factory at the base of the city wall, a large iron chimney, over ten zhang (about 100 feet) long, was suddenly blown down by the hurricane at 2:05 AM. The upper section fell inside the city, smashing through the roof beam of Xu Shunchang Coal Store at No. 25 Hongqiao Bridge. Xu Guiquan, the store owner, his wife, and their children all escaped in their sleep, but Xu's adopted daughter-in-law, Chen Cuie, who was sleeping in the attic, did not have time to escape and was crushed to death. The chimney is very heavy and cannot be removed immediately, so the body is still trapped in the house. Fresh blood can be seen dripping down from the attic, a truly tragic sight.

The intensity of this hurricane has not been seen in decades. Many houses in the city and countryside were blown down. Hundreds of telephone lines in the city were cut off. In the rural areas of Tangkou, Oudang Bridge, and Yanqiao, telephone service was also disrupted. Repairs are currently underway. Many power lines were also blown down, and in Lishe, two utility poles were toppled. At the Yuanhe Teahouse in Shitangwan, a chimney was blown down. Many trees were uprooted in Huishan and other places. The bean and wheat crops in the countryside were blown over. Fortunately, it did not rain, otherwise the losses would have been even greater. Many mulberry trees were also broken, and roofs were blown off. The wooden sign of the Provincial Education Institute on Tonghui Road and many advertisement boards at the railway station were blown down. Over a dozen cattle sheds were blown away at Xueyan Bridge. Some boats in the outer river capsized. All night boats in the villages stopped halfway to avoid danger.

At Qishuyan Station on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, an empty car, parked on a siding, was secured with an iron crowbar to prevent movement. Unexpectedly, the car was hit by the wind and began to move forward, causing the iron crowbar to break under the weight. The car derailed and overturned beside the track. At Lucheng Station, an empty car was blown all the way to near Benniu Station. The stations in Wuxi, Shitanwan, etc., did not suffer any losses; only various advertising signs, etc., near the stations were blown to the ground. In addition, the newly built awning of the Jiangnan Motor Company, valued at over 500 yuan, was also blown down. Fortunately, the twenty new cars inside the awning were not damaged. Furthermore, the long-distance telephone line from Zhenjiang to Nanjing was completely cut off, making it impossible to talk. Repairs are currently underway. That night, there was also intense lightning in the city, like a searchlight, which those who saw it called a wonder.

ZHENJIANG - HURRICANE STRIKES ZHENJIANG 85

For several days, the temperature in this city has reached as high as 96 degrees, like the heat of summer. Yesterday at 11:30 PM, the weather suddenly changed, with flashes of lightning and distant loud noises coming from the northwest, like the clamor of thousands of troops. About five minutes later, the hurricane struck, with the force of overturning mountains and overturning seas. All things cried out together, and glass windows and roof tiles flew like paper scraps into the sky. The city's streetlights were immediately extinguished, and telephone and telegraph services were also cut off. Fires broke out in several places. The fire brigade, threatened by the wind, dispatched very few people. Countless boats along the riverfront lost their moorings and disappeared. Near the station, trees were uprooted and houses collapsed. Advertisement boards along the road to the station were all blown down onto the road, cutting off traffic. Night trains arriving at the station were delayed by two hours. Huts near the flour mill were all burned down. At 10:00 PM, thunder and lightning were intense, and heavy rain poured down. By 3:00 AM this morning, the wind and rain gradually subsided. Afterwards, in the dim night, the reporter took an electric torch and personally went to investigate the area along the riverfront. Along the way, collapsed walls and uprooted houses were seen everywhere. Countless utility poles and trees were broken by the wind. Electrical wires were strewn all over the ground. Countless boats, estimated to be over 170, sank from North Zhoushan to Xiaomatou River. Near the Pingzheng Bridge, piles of broken boat planks and wood were stacked almost like a small hill. At that time, the Tongyi Steamer, which was docked at the Hexing Wharf, was also sunk by the wind and waves. The anchor chain of the British inland river gunboat Sandpiper, which was docked in the center of the river, was also broken and ran aground on the riverbank. Other losses in various places are difficult to estimate at this time. A detailed report will be provided after further investigation.
