LOCAL NEWS

CITY PARTY HEADQUARTERS AND SOCIAL BUREAU ISSUE REGULATIONS FOR ESTABLISHING LITERACY SCHOOLS BY SOCIETIES - SCHOOLS MUST OPEN BEFORE JUNE 20TH 86

The Shanghai City Party Headquarters believes that it is responsible for assisting in the progress of the municipal government's literacy education campaign. Therefore, it has organized a Literacy Education Promotion Association, appointing Tong Xingbai as the executive director and Wang Yansong, Lin Meiyan, Lu Jingshi, and Li Suixian as directors to actively carry out the project. The public's enthusiasm has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Now, the City Party Headquarters believes that there are many societies in the city, and since these societies have the nature of serving society, they should bear the obligation of supporting public welfare. Therefore, it has specifically formulated regulations for establishing literacy schools by societies and implementation measures. Together with the City Social Bureau, these have been issued to various societies in the city, with a deadline of June 20th for opening the schools. The regulations for establishing schools have already been reported in this newspaper, so there is no need to repeat them. The instructions and implementation measures are recorded below:

JOINT INSTRUCTIONS

"Regarding the matter of joint instructions, literacy education is the most fundamental and essential method for promoting popular intelligence and cultural revitalization. All Chinese people should exhaust their resources and abilities to accomplish this great task. Now, when the government is actively promoting it, it is difficult to achieve the effect of joint and simultaneous prosperity without mobilizing the entire strength of society. Moreover, various societies have the nature of serving society and should bear the obligation of supporting public welfare. In view of this, the committee and bureau have jointly formulated two types of regulations: 'Regulations for Establishing Literacy Schools by Societies' and 'Implementation Measures.' In addition to issuing a general order to all subordinate societies to abide by them, attachments are being printed and issued to the association for compliance. Starting from the date of receipt of this document, preparations must be made within two weeks and reported at any time. The schools must open before June 20th, and a responsible representative must be dispatched to Shangwen Elementary School on Penglai Road at 2:00 PM on the 15th of this month to listen to the report. This is essential. A copy of the 'Regulations for Establishing Literacy Schools by Societies' and a copy of the 'Implementation Measures' are enclosed."

IMPLEMENTATION MEASURES

"Implementation Measures for Establishing Literacy Schools by Societies" (Article 1) In addition to complying with the 'Regulations for Establishing Literacy Schools by Societies,' all societies establishing literacy schools shall implement this method (Article 2). Each society should establish at least one literacy school; more are better (Article 3). School sites shall be limited to the society's premises. Temples, shrines, residences, parlors, village teahouses, and ordinary school buildings may all be borrowed and used as annexes (Article 4). Students shall be limited to people in the same trade, regardless of gender or age. No tuition fees shall be charged. Two classes shall be established each day, one in the morning and one in the afternoon. Each class must have at least 30 people; the more, the better (Article 5). The scale may be simple; it does not have to be in the form of a school. Ordinary household furniture may be used. However, a large blackboard must be provided for teaching (Article 6). Teaching time shall be determined according to the convenience of the students, and may be set in the morning, evening, or daytime. However, once it is set, it may not be changed. The teaching method may be determined at discretion, but the ultimate goal is to enable those who do not know how to read to learn to read (Article 7). In addition to teaching literacy, literacy schools must also provide common knowledge guidance and civic training, so that in addition to literacy, students can also receive intellectual enlightenment in thought and knowledge (Article 8). The teachers of literacy schools established by various societies must meet one of the following requirements: (1) Graduates of junior normal schools or junior middle schools with certificates to prove it; (2) those who have served as teachers in municipal or registered primary schools for more than one year with proof; (3) those who have been registered or tested and qualified by the Shanghai Literacy Education Association or the Literacy Education Committee; (4) those with teaching experience and approved by the Shanghai Literacy Education Association (Article 9). In addition to managing the literacy schools established by the various societies completely on their own, those who entrust the City Party Headquarters Literacy Education Promotion Association to handle them on their behalf shall pay the expenses to the City Party Headquarters Literacy Education Promotion Association at one time in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the 'Regulations for Literacy Schools of Various Groups' (Article 10). The City Party Headquarters shall send personnel to examine the performance of the literacy schools established by the various societies at any time. All schools that arrive shall be subject to the guidance of the visiting staff (Article 11). The rewards for those who have established literacy schools with excellent results are as follows: (1) Those who can establish two literacy schools, or hold two consecutive sessions, and have achieved results, will be given royal jelly (2) Those who can establish three or more literacy schools, or hold three or more consecutive sessions, and have achieved results, will be given a certificate in addition to a medal (Article 12). If the various societies are able to hold literacy schools, and the extension is still being established, the punitive measures are as follows: (1) From the date of the notice from the City Party Headquarters, two weeks later, if preparations have not yet been made, and reasons have not yet been presented, a warning shall be given (2) From the date of the warning, two weeks later, if there is still no indication of establishment, and they have not come to apply, they shall be dissolved (Article 13). This method shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the City Party Headquarters (Article 14). Matters not covered in this method shall be revised by the City Party Headquarters at any time.

CITY CHAMBER OF COMMERCE SENDS OPINIONS ON THE BANKRUPTCY LAW - PRESENTS FOUR POINTS AND REQUESTS AN EXTENSION OF THE DEADLINE - PUBLISHES THE ORIGINAL DRAFT IN THE "COMMERCIAL MONTHLY" 87

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Civil Law Committee of the Legislative Yuan, inquiring about opinions on the draft Bankruptcy Law. The Chamber's Industrial and Commercial Law Research Committee and Standing Committee discussed it in detail and decided to first present four points of opinion and request an extension of the deadline for soliciting opinions, which was originally set for the 10th of this month. This case is of great importance, and the deadline is too short. The Chamber requested that the deadline be extended and that the original text of the draft be published in the Chamber's "Commercial Monthly" to allow various industries to explore it. The letter of opinion is recorded below: (1) It is proposed to change "suspension of payment" in Article 1 to "total suspension of payment." (Reason) It is difficult to escape the responsibility of a debtor who is untrustworthy, delays payment, and disregards debts. However, the sequestration of assets affects all the debtor's abilities and actions. The extent to which bankruptcy should be declared should be carefully considered. This law takes the inability to pay as the cause of bankruptcy and the suspension of payment as the presumed cause of bankruptcy. From a legal point of view, a debtor's credit, property, and collateral must be lost before bankruptcy can be declared. The reason for setting the presumed cause in the law is to facilitate the determination of facts. However, the meaning of suspension of payment is too broad. It is proposed to add the two words "total" above suspension of payment to facilitate explanation and show restriction. (2) In the last two sentences of Article 2, "The court that can exercise jurisdiction in accordance with the preceding paragraph shall be the local court where the debtor or bankrupt's property is located," it is proposed to add the two words "main" before "property." (Reason) The debtor or bankrupt's property is often scattered in various places. If there is no residence or place of business, limiting the jurisdiction to the location of the main property can reduce difficulties in management. (3) It is proposed to delete the four words "unlimited liability" in Article 3, Paragraph 4. (Reason) The shareholders who execute the business of a limited partnership company are naturally unlimited liability shareholders, and this is consistent with the meaning of Paragraph 2 of the same article. (4) It is proposed to change Article 2, Paragraph 6 to "the legal representative, manager, or liquidator of the debtor or bankrupt." (Reason) According to the Company Law, the rights and obligations of the liquidator of a limited company are the same as those of the director and can naturally be regarded as the legal representative of the company. However, the law does not explicitly stipulate that the liquidator of a partnership or other type of company is the legal representative. Therefore, it is better to add the term "liquidator" to make it clearer. (5) According to the above provisions of Article 4, "For those established abroad or declared bankrupt abroad, it shall not be effective for the debtor's or bankrupt's property in China." If a Chinese merchant in Hong Kong has branches in both Guangdong and Shanghai, and the Hong Kong head office is unable to pay its debts, the Hong Kong Overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce may negotiate a settlement. However, because of the above restrictions, it will not be possible to dispose of the property in Guangdong and Shanghai. To protect their rights, creditors in Guangdong and Shanghai will inevitably seek reconciliation from the courts or chambers of commerce in the location. Therefore, one case is handled in several places, which is costly and does not benefit either creditors or debtors. It is proposed to set an exception clause in this article as follows: "However, if the location of the main business is abroad, and the local chamber of commerce has completed the reconciliation procedures, creditors in the Mainland may apply for a merged reconciliation (explanation)." The proviso shall also include court conciliation and bankruptcy declaration to prevent foreign courts from interfering with the property in the Mainland for enforcement issues. In addition, the Chamber still has something to contribute: This law does not list the order of priority for bankruptcy claims, except for setting separate provisions for secured claims and co-ownership rights and recognizing the existence of priority rights. For example, in the old draft Article 28, the medical expenses of physicians, pharmacists, midwives, and nurses used by the bankrupt within one year before the bankruptcy declaration, and the wages of workers and servants employed by the bankrupt within one year before the bankruptcy declaration, were listed prior to all other claims. From the perspective of social interest, should this law adopt this provision? Please consider this carefully by the legislative authorities.

FUJIAN CONSTRUCTION DEPARTMENT BORROWS 210,000 YUAN FROM THE BANK OF COMMUNICATIONS - TO FUND THE REPAIR OF THE LUOXINGTA PAGODA WHARF - FUJIAN PROVINCE PUBLIC DEBT SYNDICATE AGREES TO UNDERWRITE 88

The Provincial Department of Construction has borrowed 210,000 yuan from the Bank of Communications to fund the repairs. RICE MERCHANTS RESIST SIAMESE RICE 89

According to the Shenshi News Agency, since the incident of Siamese discrimination and mistreatment of overseas Chinese occurred, all sectors of the country have expressed indignation. Rice merchants have taken action to resist Siamese rice. According to a source in the rice industry in this city, the Mixed Grain Industry Association has announced its decision to resist Siamese rice and has telegraphed the central government to negotiate. Rice merchants deeply sympathize with this and will immediately implement a boycott of Siamese rice. Siam has a large trade surplus with China, with rice and grains accounting for the majority of its exports to China. A boycott of Siamese rice will be very effective. Due to last year's drought, rice merchants in this city ordered a large quantity of foreign rice, but it was all from Saigon and Xiaojiao. They then ordered over 700,000 bags of Siamese rice. Siamese rice is of superior quality but expensive, so its sales are not as smooth as Saigon and Xiaojiao rice. Recently, a batch of Dajiao rice arrived, and because of its low price, it met the needs of the time and was sold out in an instant. Siamese rice, on the other hand, is more sluggish. Therefore, rice merchants have no problem resisting Siamese rice. Now that the Mixed Grain Guild has made a decision, rice merchants will stop ordering Siamese rice from today. As for the over 700,000 bags of Siamese rice that were previously ordered, only over 400,000 bags have arrived in China. There is no plan yet for the 300,000 bags that are still arriving in China.

JIANGSU PROVINCIAL GOVERNMENT PROCLAIMS - STRICTLY PROHIBITS FISHING BOATS FROM SMUGGLING - WU SONGKOU AND OTHER PLACES ARE THE INSPECTION LOCATIONS - LIU HE QI YA KOU AND OTHERS ARE THE RE-INSPECTION LOCATIONS 92

The Jiangsu Provincial Government issued a proclamation, stating: "According to the Ministry of Finance, Supervision No. 10073, the Supervisory Office submitted a report stating that from Qingming onwards each year, it is the time to handle the yellow croaker fishing season. In previous years, it was ordered that Xiangjiang Port, Qigang Yu, Qidong's Yongchang Town, and Wusongkou be used as inspection locations, while Liuhe, Luyuan, Jiangyin, Fushan, Hupu, Fuqiao, and Liuhe's Qiyakou were used as re-inspection locations. The Tax Police Bureau should be instructed to follow the previous year's precedent and order each district team to comply with the new regulations and handle the matter carefully. At the same time, the Songjiang Branch shall select fishing gear inspectors to be stationed in various places to conduct strict inspections and strive for thoroughness. However, coastal fishing boats often smuggle contraband under the guise of salting, and some even collude with large groups of smugglers, relying on their numbers to resist inspection, causing trouble. This not only affects tax revenue but also hinders public security. If preventive measures are not taken in advance, applying for a proclamation following the case is insufficient to deter them. In addition to ordering the Tax Police Bureau to supervise the district team and fully take responsibility for handling the matter, we should prepare a document and request the Supervisory Office to follow the precedent and reissue the proclamation for posting to strictly prohibit smuggling, etc. Accordingly, a notice is hereby issued to all fishing boat personnel to be informed and comply with the regulations, wear the monitoring badge, and wait for inspection. Do not take the opportunity to smuggle or rely on the crowd to break through. If the aforementioned circumstances occur, strict investigation will be conducted according to the law, and there will be no leniency. Anti-smuggling officers and soldiers must also not take the opportunity to harass. They must all be respectful and not reach this point. This is essential."

The City Social Affairs Bureau Formulates a Plan for Agricultural Cooperative Experimentation, Which Has Been Approved by the Municipal Government, Significantly Aiding Rural Revitalization 100

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau noted that last year's drought caused agricultural disasters and poor harvests. However, the agricultural cooperative experiment zones in the city maintained their production performance. Records show that the production volume in these zones was higher than that of ordinary cultivation methods. If this can be promoted citywide, allowing all farmers to imitate the methods of the agricultural cooperative experiment zones, selecting improved varieties, and improving techniques, then the agricultural production in this city will certainly see remarkable progress. This will significantly aid rural revitalization. With the current spring plowing season, the agricultural cooperative experimentation should be carried out to achieve the full success of agricultural improvement. The bureau has formulated a plan for the agricultural cooperative experiment zones in the 24th year, following established precedents, and it has been approved by the municipal government. The plan and an overview of last year's agricultural cooperative experiment zones are recorded below:

Formulated Plan

(1) Locations: In addition to the ten districts of Lihang, Yangsi, Tangqiao, Caojing, Yinhang, Gaohang, Zhenru, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Fahua, Yangjing, Wusong, and Pusong, which should continue to be operated to achieve results, Gaohang and Yinxiang districts will also be added to expand coverage. (2) Organization: The bureau will entrust municipal committee members and agricultural associations in each district to select excellent local farmers and establish zones in suitable locations, with farmers responsible for management and subject to the guidance and supervision of the bureau, municipal committee members, and agricultural associations. A non-salaried instructor may be hired as needed. (3) Facilities: This year will still focus on cotton experimentation. Twelve zones will be set up in Lihang, Yinhang, Yangsi, Tangqiao, and Caojing, divided into two districts each, while the remaining ten districts will each have six zones, totaling one hundred and twenty zones. (4) Subsidies: Each zone will have a designated area of five mu (Chinese acres), with a subsidy of three yuan per mu for experimentation costs. Each district will receive 45 yuan for instructor travel expenses and 15 yuan for seed costs.

Last Year's Overview

Last year, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau designated thirteen districts, including Yangsi, Lihang, Yinhang, Fahua, Pusong, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Tangqiao, Zhenru, Gaohang, Yangjing, Caojing, and Wusong, as agricultural cooperative experiment zones. It ordered municipal committee members and agricultural associations in each district to select excellent farmers and instructors and proceed according to the agricultural cooperative plan set by the bureau. It also formulated a chart of cotton cultivation procedures and diary forms, which were issued to each district for compliance. The bureau sent personnel from time to time to inspect and urge the instructors and cooperative farmers in each district to carry out the plan diligently. After each district reported the experimental situation to the bureau, it was found that several zones were severely affected by drought due to the terrain, and the production results were slightly lower. However, the rest were diligent in irrigation, cultivated properly, and had abundant harvests, which were higher than those of ordinary cultivation methods, so they were deeply trusted by the farmers. The bureau selected and rewarded those with excellent results to show encouragement. The overview of the city's agricultural cooperative experiment zones in the 23rd year is excerpted below:

Production Situation

1. Yangsi District: A total of 18 zones, covering 90 mu, planted Jiangyin White Seed Cotton and harvested 9,660 jin. 2. Lihang District: A total of 18 zones, covering 90 mu, planted Jiangyin White Seed Cotton and harvested 15,293 jin. 3. Yinhang District: A total of 12 zones, covering 60 mu, planted Baoshan White Seed Cotton and harvested 8,485 jin. 4. Fahua District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, with 4 zones planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton and 2 zones planting local cotton, harvested 2,805 jin. 5. Jiangwan District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, with 3 zones planting local cotton and 3 zones planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 3,300 jin. 6. Pengpu District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, with 4 zones planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton and 2 zones planting local cotton, harvested 1,711 jin. 7. Tangqiao District: A total of 12 zones, covering 60 mu, all planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 6,050 jin. 8. Zhenru District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, with 2 zones planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton and 4 zones planting local cotton, harvested 2,060 jin. 9. Yangjing District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, all planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 2,405 jin. 10. Caojing District: A total of 12 zones, covering 60 mu, all planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 5,520 jin. 11. Wusong District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, all planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 2,075 jin. 12. Pusong District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, all planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 2,150 jin. 13. Gaohang District: A total of 6 zones, covering 30 mu, all planting Jiangyin White Seed Cotton, harvested 2,515 jin. The total is 120 zones, covering 600 mu, with a harvest of 64,029 jin, averaging 106 jin per mu.

Division of Municipal and County Public Property; Objections Arise Regarding Part of the Tianhou Palace; Evaluation Meeting Scheduled for May 16 105

The case of dividing the accumulated grain funds, properties, and original public suspected public properties between the Shanghai Municipality and Shanghai County has been submitted by both parties to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Jiangsu Provincial Government for review based on the public property division method proposed by the Second Evaluation Committee (the division method was previously reported). The Municipal Finance Bureau has now received instructions from the Municipal Government, stating that the submitted reports and diagrams have been reviewed. The Tianhou Palace building base (i.e., the Municipal Shuji Elementary School) to be divided to the Municipal side was already handled in November of the 21st year by the Municipal Education Bureau and the Shanghai County Government based on the provisions regarding education in the fifth case of the meeting record of the Provincial and Municipal Division of Governing Authority Conference. A method was formulated, stating that it had been included in the previously established method. The first item stated that the County Education Bureau should transfer it to the Municipal Education Bureau along with the deed. When the County Education Bureau transferred the education properties in February of the 22nd year, it was also included in the transfer list (the list referred to it as a deedless base and a copy of the list was sent to the Finance Bureau for the record). Therefore, the property rights had long been determined, and it could no longer be included in the scope of the municipal and county division. The Tianhou Palace building base should be removed, and another division method should be proposed for review. The Municipal and County public property building base should be investigated for existing funds and reported accordingly. The bureau has scheduled a third evaluation committee meeting for 2:00 PM on May 16 to discuss the division plan. However, after receiving the Municipal Finance Bureau's letter, the County Government found that the former County Third Elementary School (i.e., the current Municipal Shuji Elementary School) borrowed a portion of the Tianhou Palace as a school building. The County Public Funds and Properties Management Office found that the County Education Bureau published an educational overview, stating that the Municipal and County Division of Education Properties declared that the Shanghai County Third Higher Elementary School, located at Tianhou Palace on Henan Road, covering 3.8 mu of land, had no deed and was transferred to the Municipal Education Bureau for receipt. The office believed that since the Shuji Elementary School was reorganized from the County Third Elementary School, the transfer of jurisdiction should be limited to educational administration, and the land should still belong to the original public property. The Education Bureau's transfer to the Municipal side should not be tacitly approved. In December of last year, it was found that the County Third Elementary School (i.e., the current Municipal Shuji Elementary School) borrowed the Tianhou Palace public property. The office sent a letter to the County Education Bureau to forward to the Municipal Education Bureau, stating its objection. Yesterday, letters were sent to county committee members Qin Yanqi, Wang Yunseng, Zhang Jingye, Zhu Changlin, Wang Chengyao, and Zhang Guangrong, requesting them to investigate and attend the meeting, and to unanimously advocate that the Tianhou Palace should still belong to the original public property according to the original case declared by the Funds and Properties Office last year and be divided accordingly.

Chuansha County Requests Prohibition; Foreigners in Shanghai Should Not Hunt; To Ensure Safety 109

The Jiangsu Provincial Government approved the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' response regarding Chuansha County's request to negotiate with foreign consulates in Shanghai to notify foreigners not to hunt or stay overnight in the coastal areas of the county to ensure safety. It specially instructed the administrative inspectors of each district and the county magistrates of each county, the director of the public security bureau of the provincial capital, etc., stating that the Chuansha County Magistrate Li Leng had previously requested that foreign consulates in Shanghai be negotiated with so that foreigners would not hunt or stay overnight in the coastal areas of the county to ensure safety. Because this matter concerned foreign affairs, instructions were issued and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was consulted for review. Now, the reply has been approved, stating that there are no provisions regarding hunting matters in the treaty, but hunting is not within the meaning of "travel" in the treaty. The former Prime Minister's Office had an explanation on record. Currently, foreigners hunting in China are handled according to the Hunting Law of the Third Year of the Republic and the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Hunting Law of the Tenth Year of the Republic. According to Article 8 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Hunting Law of the Tenth Year of the Republic, when issuing a Class B hunting certificate, the local government of the hunting area should be consulted first to obtain their opinion, and the government should be notified after the certificate is issued for inspection. If the Chuansha area believes that it is necessary to ban foreigners from hunting, it may, according to the provisions of Article 8 of the aforementioned Detailed Rules for Implementation, state the reasons why it is not convenient to allow foreigners to hunt when the issuing authority solicits opinions in writing. Having approved the report, in addition to the Ministry informing the Ministry of Industry to order the competent authorities in each province and city to strictly follow the provisions of the Hunting Law of the Third Year of the Republic and the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Hunting Law of the Tenth Year of the Republic when issuing hunting certificates to foreigners in the future, and to indicate the permitted hunting locations on the certificate. If the permitted location is in the interior, it should also be stated that the certificate holder must still apply for an inland travel passport when going to that location. After the reply arrives, it will be reported separately. Appropriate consultation and notification are required. This order is issued for notification.

Zhang Sumin Lectures on Modern Economic Thought 110

Yesterday, Fudan University specially invited economist Dr. Zhang Sumin to lecture on "Modern Economic Thought." Professor Li Binghuan, head of the university's economics department, gave an introduction. Dr. Zhang then began his lecture, stating that the word "modern" has two meanings. One is narrow, referring to the most recent period, roughly from 1900 to the present. Economic thought during this period is so recent and diverse that it is difficult to categorize into schools. If forced, it could be divided into as many as ninety schools, such as the Price School, Happiness School, Quantity School, Mathematical School, Legal School, Socio-economic School, Experimental Economic School, Functional Economic School, Institutional Economic School, and Controlled Economic School. However, these schools are interconnected, and many individuals belong to several schools simultaneously. Therefore, recent economic thought can only be described in terms of trends, not schools. Thus, we can say that the trends of modern economic thought emphasize quantitative methods, experimental methods, price research, people's happiness, social stance, legal institutions, and government control. The second meaning of "modern" is broad, referring to the modern era in general, starting from the publication of Adam Smith's "The Wealth of Nations" in 1776. If we consider the period from 1776 to 1900 as one era, the schools of thought during this period, besides Socialism, include the Classical School, Nationalist School, Historical School, Optimist School, Austrian School, and Neo-classical School. If we group the Classical School, Optimist School, Austrian School, and Neo-classical School into the Liberal School, then the economic thought of this period includes the Liberal School, Socialist School, Nationalist School, and Historical School. If we summarize the economic thought since 1900 into two or three schools (such as the Mathematical School, Institutional School, and Controlled School), then there are perhaps six or seven major schools of economic thought from 1776 to the present. In short, the division of schools is somewhat arbitrary. However, some believe that besides the Socialist School, there is only the Liberal School in modern economic thought, which does not align with the facts. Moreover, liberalism (i.e., laissez-faire policy) died in fact in the mid-19th century and in thought at the beginning of this century, which is something we should pay particular attention to.

Kang Yuan Canning Co., Ltd., held its second annual shareholders' meeting on the 11th of this month at its main factory on Huade Road, Shanghai. The meeting venue was arranged in a dignified and neat manner, with statistical charts and guiding slogans posted. Shareholders inspected the entire factory. The directors and supervisors have already committed to raising half of this amount, and the remaining 500,000 yuan will be offered to existing shareholders. The company distributed toys and other products as souvenirs to add to the enjoyment. The shareholders were quite excited about the company's thriving business and generous profits.

Yantai Jingyu No. 2 Winery Developing the South China Beverage Market; Eliminating Leakage and Recovering Rights 113

Gale in the City Yesterday Morning; Trees Uprooted in Zhenjiang, Delaying the Shanghai-Nanjing Train; Incoming Ships Delayed; Weather Turned Cool Yesterday 115

At 3:00 AM yesterday, when the city was still in the quiet of the night, a sudden gale swept in. People in Shanghai were sleeping soundly when their windows were blown open. The wind lasted for two hours before subsiding, causing delays for incoming ships yesterday morning. Telephone and telegraph lines were also slightly damaged. Many large trees at the Shanjingkou in Zhenjiang were uprooted and fell on the tracks, delaying the Shanghai-Nanjing train and the Shanghai-Pinghu train from Nanjing by two hours this morning. The weather also turned cooler yesterday. The details are as follows:

The Situation of the Gale Yesterday Morning

The weather had been sultry for days, reaching ninety-one degrees at noon the day before yesterday. Although it cooled down slightly at night, it was still sultry. Many residents, unable to bear it, left their windows open when they went to sleep. However, at 2:00 AM (i.e., yesterday morning), the weather suddenly turned cold, like late autumn. At 3:00 AM, a gale roared in. Most people, at this late hour, were awakened from their sound sleep and felt the discomfort of the early morning cold. The wind subsided slightly at 5:00 AM. The lowest temperature last night was about seventy degrees.

Shanghai-Nanjing Train Delayed

The gale extended to the coast and along the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. The situation was particularly severe in Zhenjiang, where many large trees at Shanjingkou were uprooted and fell on the tracks, preventing the Shanghai-Nanjing train from Nanjing and the Shanghai-Pinghu train from passing. After railway workers removed the trees, traffic could resume, but the trains were delayed by two hours. The Shanghai-Nanjing train arrived at 9:30 AM (originally scheduled for 7:15 AM), and the Shanghai-Pinghu train arrived at 10:00 AM (originally scheduled for 8:00 AM). However, the train cars and passengers were not otherwise affected.

Incoming Ships Delayed

Due to the gale yesterday morning, many ships originally scheduled to arrive were delayed by several hours. These included ships from China Merchants and Taikoo. However, ships scheduled to depart yesterday, such as the Jiangxin from China Merchants, the Dayu from Dada, and the Hongda from Dalian, departed as scheduled. In addition, many of the city's telegraph and long-distance telephone lines were damaged by the wind, but they have now been repaired.

Weather Cooler Yesterday

The weather had been quite hot recently, reaching 94.5 degrees on the 10th and 91 degrees the day before yesterday. At 9:00 AM yesterday, it was 70 degrees, and at noon it was only 77 degrees, much cooler than the previous two days. However, the weather has been alternately cold and hot recently, which can easily lead to illness.

The gale passed through yesterday morning, and the telegraph and telephone lines along the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway were also disrupted. At the Lucheng Station, a 21-ton flatcar parked on a siding was blown and moved automatically for more than one station. A locomotive was dispatched from Changzhou Station and towed the car back near the Xinzha Station. At the Qishuyan Station, a 30-ton flatcar from the Jinpu Railway parked on a siding was also blown and moved automatically, breaking the iron yoke, causing two wheels to derail. In addition, the 301 through train and the 5 night express from Nanjing the night before last were also delayed by two or three hours due to the hurricane.

Mother's Day Commemorated Yesterday; Wu Xingya Speaks at the Women's Temperance Society; the U.S. Navy YMCA Also Holds Celebrations 116

Yesterday was World Mother's Day. The Shanghai Chinese Women's Temperance Society held a commemorative meeting at its headquarters on Yuanmingyuan Road at 3:00 PM, attended by more than a hundred representatives from all walks of life, as well as mothers and children. An oath-taking ceremony was held. The U.S. Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai and the U.S. Navy YMCA also held celebrations. The details are as follows:

Participating Representatives At 3:00 PM yesterday, the Women's Temperance Society held a Mother's Day commemorative meeting. Attendees included Social Bureau Director Wu Xingya, Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, and women's leaders Wu Laowei, Liu Wang Liming, Chen Lingyi, Yang Zhihao, as well as mothers and children, totaling more than one hundred people.

Oath-Taking Ceremony After the ceremony, Ms. Wu Laowei led the representatives in taking the oath. The oath read: "I hereby solemnly swear to abide by the precepts of the Chinese Women's Temperance Society, to honor our mothers, to promote maternal love, and to strive for social service." This oath was taken on May 12, 1935. There was also a three-minute moment of silence to recall the love of our mothers from childhood to adulthood and to show respect.

Chairman's Report Chairman Wu Laowei then gave a speech, stating that World Mother's Day originated at the end of the European War and was initiated by Ms. Anna Jarvis of the United States. All countries in the world have also vigorously promoted it, and it has become Mother's Day for all nations and peoples. If people have no parents, how can they survive? Therefore, I hope you will not take it lightly. Although the site of this association is small and the ceremony is simple, its mission is extremely serious and upright. We are very honored to have you all present today. From now on, we should follow the oath we took today, promote maternal love, and strive for social service, so as not to fail the meaning of commemorating Mother's Day.

Wu Xingya's Speech Wu Xingya then gave a speech, stating that mothers are the greatest people in the world and the people who love us the most. From birth to now, I have never been separated from my mother. Mothers nurture me, guide me, and make us members of society. Therefore, we should commemorate mothers. As for making the country strong and the people healthy, we should first think about the mothers. Healthy mothers mean lively and innocent children. Therefore, mothers taking care of their bodies indirectly means taking care of their children. Now, Chinese women should first seek liberation so that the future little masters of our country can thrive day by day. Conversely, if women do not seek liberation, the children they bear will not be healthy. This point should be discussed. Furthermore, if we want to love the country, love society, and serve the people, we should first love our own mothers, because mothers can teach you to grow up, contribute to the country, serve society, and work for the people. These are all the meanings of commemorating Mother's Day. Please remember them well. Afterwards, the participating elementary school students performed songs and dances, which were quite wonderful. Finally, child representatives presented flowers and refreshments, and the meeting adjourned.

American Celebrations The U.S. Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai and the U.S. Navy YMCA held separate commemorative ceremonies. The Marine Corps and others gathered at the Grand Theatre at 10:00 AM yesterday for the ceremony. A committee headed by Mrs. Pannell presented each participating sailor with a small bouquet of flowers. The person representing the mothers to accept the flowers from the sailors was Mrs. Pannell, the wife of Marine Corps Sergeant Pannell. During the ceremony, the band played music and sang, which was very moving. Finally, Reverend Forbes gave a speech on "Mother and Child." After the ceremony, two hundred American soldiers who participated in the ceremony were invited to various homes by American expatriates in Shanghai for a meal. Catholic members invited seventy-five sailors to their homes, with each family hosting about two to ten sailors. In the evening, fifty American women jointly hosted the American soldiers at the Navy YMCA.

Grand Teaching Scene Yesterday was Sunday. The Moore Memorial Church held a Mother's Day prayer service at 10:30 AM, led by Reverend Ye Fang. Students from the Moore Memorial Girls' School sang special hymns. The church presented each male and female guest who attended the service with a bouquet of flowers. White flowers were given to those whose parents had passed away, red flowers were given to those whose parents were alive, and one red and one white flower were given to those with one parent alive and one deceased. The flowers were beautiful and touching. The church also presented two Chinese and Western Mother's Day flower baskets to show respect.

Newspaper Commemorations Because yesterday was Mother's Day, all the newspapers in the city devoted space to publish commemorative articles. The International Council of Women, organized by sixteen women's groups representing fourteen countries, has been established for several years. The council held its annual general meeting at the American Women's Association on Jingan Temple Road yesterday, and discussions will continue today. The main proposal this time is "The Establishment of Vocational Education Institutions for Young Women in Shanghai."

International Telecommunications Bureau Calibrates International Call Equipment; Tests Lines and Sounding Accuracy; First Talking to the U.S. and the Philippines, Then Gradually Developing 117

Since the Ministry of Communications' International Telecommunications Bureau began actively planning domestic and international wireless telephone services last year, the wireless telephone equipment at the radio station has been installed by the end of last month. Currently, engineers from the station are testing the lines to ensure they are correct and the sound is clear. Once the calibration is complete, test calls will first be made with various countries. If the results are good, formal calls will then begin on a regular basis with the United States and the Philippines, with whom agreements have already been reached. After telephone service with the U.S. and the Philippines is implemented, it will continue to work with Germany, France, Italy, and other countries. As for the call charges, in addition to the regulations of international call rates, connecting fees and other expenses will need to be determined separately. The Ministry of Communications is currently drafting these regulations.

Japanese Oil Dumped at Low Prices; Sales Not Strong; 2,000 Boxes Remain in Storage for Sale; Several Thousand More Boxes to Arrive in Shanghai at the End of the Month 118

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Japanese Petroleum Corporation named the oil produced in Fushun, Northeast China, "Chengmen" brand and shipped the first batch of 5,000 boxes to Shanghai for trial sales. The Shanghai agency of the Japanese Petroleum Corporation, Yinghua Foreign Firm, was responsible for promoting the sales. Because this batch of goods was less efficient than British, American, and Russian oil, sales were not strong. Yinghua then dumped the oil at low prices to compete with British, American, and Russian oil merchants. The facts over the past half month have shown that this is impossible. According to inquiries, of the 5,000 boxes, only about 3,000 boxes were purchased or retailed by Japanese residents. There are still 2,000 boxes in storage for sale. Very few Chinese people have purchased the oil. According to Yinghua, several thousand more boxes will be shipped to Shanghai later this month.

Joint Committee, etc., Requests Investigation of Telephone Company's Accounts; If Expenses Are Not Covered, Efforts Should Be Made to Economize; Why Repeatedly Raise Prices and Increase the Burden on Users? 120

Since the British and French concessions approved the Shanghai Telephone Company's illegal price increase, all sectors of industry, commerce, and education in the city have expressed dissent due to the economic depression of all industries. The Joint Committee of Machine-Made National Goods Factories yesterday specially submitted a request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for the government to thoroughly investigate the company's accounts. The original text reads: "Submitted regarding the Shanghai Telephone Company's repeated increases in telephone fees, earnestly requesting negotiations to stop the increases in order to relieve the burden on users. Shanghai is a major trading port, and its prosperity in industry and commerce is the highest in the country. However, since the Shanghai War, foreign economic aggression has crowded out domestic industries, and last year's drought caused rural bankruptcy, causing the entire Shanghai market to be depressed. Bankruptcies are frequently heard. The telephone company previously increased prices in 1932, and soon after, proposed to calculate telephone fees by the number of calls. The Board of Directors of the Public Works Department even proposed to increase prices by 12.5%. However, it is known that telephones are a public utility, and according to international practice, profits should be reduced. However, the company stubbornly insists on maintaining a certain profit, which is inappropriate. Moreover, in the two months before the price increase, according to surveys, 2,500 telephone lines had already been removed. If the fees are calculated by the number of calls, according to the statistics of a neighborhood association (published in Shen Xin and other newspapers on April 9), the charges would exceed the original charges by three to four times. How can users bear this burden? It is known that more people will remove their lines. In addition, the price of silver has risen sharply recently, and the exchange rate is low, reducing the company's import costs and invisibly increasing its profits. If expenses are not covered, efforts should be made to economize. It is not appropriate to repeatedly seek compensation from users. Otherwise, if the company disregards market conditions and insists on raising prices, the accounts of the public utility should be submitted to public examination by citizens in order to be fair. Therefore, we specially submit this request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to approve and negotiate a halt to the price increase, or send a letter to the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department to jointly investigate the accounts in order to clarify the facts and relieve the people's difficulties. This is for the public good."

Gale Strikes Shanghai; House Collapses in Pudong, Injuring People; Decayed Houses Are No Match for Storms; Eight People Injured, None Seriously 123

A house collapse occurred on Yihua Road, Lanni Ferry, Pudong at approximately 8:30 AM yesterday. Nine buildings collapsed, injuring eight people of all ages. Details are recorded as follows:

Nine Buildings Collapsed: The collapsed houses are from No. 132 Yihua Road to No. 148, all even-numbered addresses, a total of nine buildings. These were built by the foreign firm Jardine Matheson during the late Qing Dynasty. After more than thirty years, the buildings are dilapidated. Most of the tenants are from Anhui and Hubei provinces. Last summer, because the firm did not intend to manage the properties, a negotiator persuaded the Hongsheng Zhan real estate department to purchase the land and buildings. The transfer was completed in November.

Refugees Occupy: After Hongsheng acquired the property rights, seeing that the houses were in dangerous condition, it notified the tenants to stop paying rent and vacate the premises to allow for reconstruction. While the tenants had not yet completely moved out, a fence was erected. Suddenly, a large number of refugees from other provinces fleeing famine arrived in Pudong. For a time, they had nowhere to live and lodged in the empty houses. At most, there were about 200 people. During the day, they relied on begging to survive. Because the refugees were not managed, most of them privately dug up wall bricks and column foundations to build houses elsewhere, gradually moving out. Until recently, there were over twenty injured refugees in the empty houses.

Hurricane Causes Collapse: After the empty houses were excavated by refugees, they gradually became shaky and on the verge of collapse. In addition, a hurricane suddenly struck Shanghai at about 2:00 AM yesterday morning. The houses were excessively shaken and became even more difficult to support. By 8:30 AM, with a series of crashing sounds, all nine buildings completely collapsed to the west in an instant. There were loud cries and wails. Those who could escape fled, and those who were crushed were trapped. The tragic cries for help were endless.

Eight People Injured: After the tragic incident occurred, the loud noise resonated far and wide. Nearby police officers immediately blew their whistles to call for help. Zhao Longsheng, the director of the Pudong Fire Brigade, led his entire staff to rescue the victims. Zhang, the director of the Pudong Public Security Bureau, also supervised Cai and Liu, officials, and patrol officers to assist in the rescue. Fortunately, there were many people available, and the collapsed houses were completely cleared within an hour. Eight injured people of all ages were rescued. Dr. Wang Xiongfei from Peidong Hospital arrived on the scene to provide treatment. Because the rescue was relatively quick, no one lost their lives.

Alternative Arrangements for Aftermath: The names, ages, origins, and injuries of the eight rescued people are as follows: (1) Wang Ping, female, 4 years old, from Hubei, lightly injured, discharged after bandaging. (2) Wu Gen, male, 28 years old, from Ningbo, lightly injured, discharged. (3) Zhao Alou, female, 21 years old, from Hubei, seriously injured in the left thigh, abdomen, and corner of the eye, unable to move. (4) Mrs. Chen Tong, 40 years old, from Liyang, injured in the right elbow. (5) Chen Ruiying, female, 8 years old, from Liyang, injured in the face, swollen back of the head. (6) Chen Xiaomao, male, 1 year old, from Liyang, seriously injured in the right face and internal organs, unable to breastfeed, in critical condition. (7) Mrs. Wang Peng, female, 44 years old, from Hubei, unable to move her right leg, multiple skin injuries, serious internal injuries. (8) Wang Xingzi, male, 11 years old, from Hubei, a large laceration on the right thigh, about the size of a palm, also injured in the right shoulder. Director Zhang reported the details of the tragic incident to the General Bureau for review. At the same time, alternative arrangements were made for the injured refugees to provide relief.

Balcony on Avenue Joffre Collapses, Injuring People; One Girl and One Western Woman Dead; Two Other Children Injured, Condition Still Critical 124

The balcony in front of the building at No. 749 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession suddenly collapsed at around 3:00 PM on the 10th. It happened that two girls and one boy, three children of Yu Azhang, owner of the Aikeli leather shoe store at No. 723 on the same street, were passing by while out buying food. A Westerner was also injured. They were sent to the hospital for treatment in critical condition. Details have been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the two buildings, No. 749 and No. 751, belong to an old local woman, Zhu Gao. They are rented by a local man, Zhang Shaoquan. He lives on the upper floors and rents out parts of the building. He operates Yongtai Cigarette Shop on the ground floor of No. 751. The shop front at No. 749 is sublet to Zhou Ada (43 years old), who runs Fat Tai Fruit and Beef Shop. The building was originally a *shikumen*-style building without a balcony. It was installed by the second landlord, Zhang Shaoquan (46 years old), for temporary storage of goods. After many years, it had rotted from wind and rain and had become shaky. However, Zhang was stingy and did not hire workers to repair it. At 3:05 PM on the 10th, Fu Sheng (16 years old, from Shaoxing), an apprentice at Yongtai Cigarette Shop, went to the balcony at No. 749 to fetch a kerosene can. Due to the movement, the corroded balcony could not bear the weight and suddenly collapsed, causing a great disaster. The apprentice, Lu Fusheng, lost his balance and fell, but was not injured. However, the children, two girls and one boy, and a Westerner who were passing by were affected. After the incident, the French police were notified and immediately sent detectives to the scene. They first sent the injured to Guangci Hospital for treatment and took the accountant of Yongtai Cigarette Shop, Zhang Puru (28 years old, from Nanxiang), and the apprentice, Lu Fusheng, as well as Zhou Ada, the owner of Fat Tai Fruit and Beef Shop, to the police station for investigation. Zhang Shaoquan, the owner of Yongtai Cigarette Shop, had fled. Detectives supervised the shop assistants of both stores to remove the fallen balcony wood and debris to clear the way for pedestrians. The six-year-old girl, Yu Sanbao, was the most seriously injured, with head injuries. She died at 5:53 PM that evening. The hospital notified the police to transport the body to the Tongren Fu Yuan autopsy center. The next day, the Second Special Court was notified. The chief prosecutor, Chen Beisan, along with forensic doctor Jiang and secretary Peng, arrived at the center at noon to verify that the deceased had died from head injuries caused by being crushed. He took the case and questioned the defendant Zhang Puru, Lu Fusheng, and witnesses Zhu Gao and Zhou Ada. He then ordered that the body be released to the family for burial after they had signed a statement, pending an investigation by the police department in accordance with the law. The Westerner, a Portuguese woman (name unknown), also died in the hospital at around 10:00 AM the next day due to her injuries. The condition of the other two injured children, Yu Sanbao's sister, Abao, 10 years old, and brother, Yinsong, 8 years old, is still critical. It is heard that the police will transfer the defendants to the Second Special Court today for questioning.

Colleagues and Friends Commemorate Tie Lisheng Yesterday; Minister Kong and His Wife Attend in Person; Funeral Procession Was Extremely Solemn and Mournful 125

Tie Lisheng, a secretary in several departments, recently died in a horse riding accident. This was reported in a previous newspaper. The Ministry of Finance, the Central Bank, Mingbao School, and friends from various quarters held a memorial service at the Shanghai Funeral Home on Xujiahui Road, Fenglin Bridge, at 10:00 AM yesterday (the 12th) to express their condolences. Over five to six hundred people attended. Executive Yuan Vice President Kong Xiangxi and his wife, their sons and daughters, and Zheng Hongnian, Wu Jisun, and others attended. The details are recorded as follows:

Arrangement of the Venue

A simple colored archway was erected at the entrance of the funeral home auditorium. The archway was surrounded by elegiac couplets, memorial banners, and fresh flower wreaths. The hall was decorated very solemnly. Simple candlesticks were placed on the spirit altar, with Tie's portrait in the middle. Incense smoke wafted, creating a solemn atmosphere. The four walls of the auditorium were also filled with elegiac couplets.

Funeral Procession

1. Playing of funeral music. 2. Singing hymns. 3. Prayers. 4. Reading the Bible. 5. Report on Tie's deeds. 6. Singing hymns. 7. Reading the eulogy. 8. Singing hymns. 9. Family thanks. 10. Blessings. 11. Playing of funeral music. After a classmate of Tie's reported on his deeds, Minister Kong stood up and briefly stated that Lisheng's character could be summarized in the four words "loyal, righteous, and courageous." He recounted Tie's time studying at Mingxian School and his service in various fields. His words and gestures moved everyone present. Finally, he encouraged alumni of Mingxian School in Shanghai to prioritize the welfare of the country and society in their work so that they would not be ashamed to have lived in this world. Next, Li Qingxuan delivered a eulogy, with tears in his voice, moving the entire assembly. In particular, the eulogy personally written by Tie's wife, Wang Qiwen, was the most sincere and touching. It was exceptionally mournful.

Eulogy

On the 12th day of May, the 24th year of the Republic of China, Li Yumei and others from the funeral committee, colleagues from the Ministry of Finance and the Central Bank, classmates from Mingxian School, and friends from various quarters, respectfully open this memorial service for our deceased friend Tie Lisheng and announce it with this text. Alas, Lisheng, did you really die? Did you really meet such a tragic end by falling from a horse? I have shared feelings with you for over ten years, knowing you well. I heard your classmates say that when you studied at Mingxian, your excellent reputation spread, and everyone respected and loved you. After graduating from the Northwest Army Cadre School, you joined the military and were valued by Zhang Gongzi, being promoted as an outstanding rising military talent. Kong Gong recruited you as an assistant, managing affairs in an orderly manner. I thought that you not only had the talent to manage the army but also had ample ability to govern. I hoped that your future would be unlimited, but who knew that you would encounter this sudden change? I and other colleagues often only met once every few days, but I would talk and laugh with you morning and evening when working with Kong Gong. On the day of the accident, I was having dinner with you, but who knew that in half a day, we would be separated by life and death? Your straightforward and talented nature, your steadfast and simple demeanor, seemed to indicate that you could achieve great things and live a long life. But who knew that you would suddenly die in your prime? I know that the length of life is predetermined, but after ten years of sharing similar interests, someone with whom I have laughed and talked with suddenly passes away. How can I not feel pain in my heart? And you left behind your widowed wife and no hope for an orphan. Does this not make people feel even more disappointed and sigh without end? Regarding the matters after your death, Kong Gong paid close attention, entrusting me and your old friends to handle them in a proper and appropriate manner, hoping to comfort you in the afterlife. But the sorrow in my heart cannot be fully expressed. I hope you will appreciate this humble sentiment.

Wife's Eulogy

On the 12th day of May, the 24th year of the Republic of China, your wife, Wang Qiwen, cries and tells your spirit, my husband Lisheng: Alas, Lisheng, why did you leave me behind? The initial news brought hope that we would meet the next morning, but who would have thought that it would become a stream that would never return? Heartbreaking and soul-shattering, there is nothing comparable. Crying and wailing, I call out without knowing when to stop. I will no longer be with people in this world. Lying still in death, sleeping soundly, I want to follow you, but my heart and soul cannot reach you. The sky is dark, and I almost cannot distinguish the truth from falsehood in the world. Sometimes I believe it, sometimes I doubt it. Is it a dream? Have you really left me? I used to never let you leave my side, sharing every moment, every meal. But from now on, I will never have you again. How heartbreaking, how tragic! The so-called heaven is unpredictable, and the gods are incomprehensible. Even gods and humans cannot understand. Recalling the time from our marriage to today, it has only been six years, and half of that time was spent apart. How pitiful and sad! Could there be anything longer and more unbearable than this? Alas, I will no longer have you. The world will no longer see you. I used to not believe in the existence of gods, but today I must consult a sorcerer. Although, you have gone first and are not alone. My spirit will follow you. The reason why my body remains is that you were loyal and filial. I have an elderly grandmother of seventy and an old father of sixty. Can I not be filial? But the pain in my heart will never be erased. You have been gone for nine days. Do you know? Have you seen the sorrow and mourning of your superiors and friends, their busy and troubled minds? They dress you in brocade clothes, place you in a coffin, and bury you in a good place. Soon, I will see you again, leaving this evil world, escaping the vast sea of suffering. Blessed, blessed, why don't you take me with you quickly? Two months ago, you said that if I died, you would erect a monument to commemorate me. Unexpectedly, today I am here to cry for you, prepare you, and bury you. I can only disfigure my face, wear humble clothes, and long for a piece of land in Shanghai. How sad, how sad! I can no longer speak. If your spirit knows, please understand.

Summary of Elegiac Couplets

There were many elegiac couplets displayed at yesterday's meeting, too many to record individually. Here are some of the most notable ones: Kong Xiangxi: "We followed each other in our youth, originally hoping to spread our wings and fly, working together to serve the country. Our ambitions were not fulfilled. Who would have thought that you would die while riding a horse, causing your peers to lose a talent?" Zhang Zhijiang: "We were comrades-in-arms for a long time, recalling the revitalization of national arts. You helped me with numerous plans. Unexpected events arise. Those who are good riders often fall. I will no longer see you wielding your whip." Zheng Hongnian: "I remember working with you in the Ministry of Works. Your free spirit and heroic posture were something I always appreciated. The news of your fall from a horse was shocking. The sound of the carriage and your words still echo in my ears." Li Qingxuan: "Looking back on your life, you were especially heroic among our few friends. Recently, we traveled to Shanghai together, spending time together day and night. Who would have expected such grief to come so suddenly? The news of your fall from a horse arrived. On that day, the 5/3 National Humiliation Day, heaven was full of sorrow. How could I bear to lose another good friend? The sounds of music have disappeared. From now on, I can only increase my commemoration, learning from Hong Luyu's cries." Zou Lin: "Sighing that you fell halfway, I now know that the path of the world lacks strength and robustness." Li Tang: "Your extraordinary spirit suppressed Chen Lou. We both promoted the bearded Shen Can. You deserved to be chosen for your talent. A sad wind rises from the Huangpu River. Who would have thought that your travels south and north would end in a loss of control, causing the death of a hero?" Mingxian School Alumni Association: "Scratching our heads, we ask heaven, why do good people not live long? Grieving in the sunlight, our great ambitions have never been easily realized." Tie's wife: "After six years of marriage, you left behind a widowed swan and a solitary gull. I will live a peaceful life. How could your heart bear it? We will follow you to the nine heavens, only to support our parents and guard our ambitions. I will temporarily remain in this world. You know my intentions." Chen Xing: "I often sighed with you, allowing you to test your skills with the reins. Why did you die so quickly? I feel even more saddened by the loss of talent." Fan Guang and Fan Songfu: "You stirred the reins, determined to clarify the situation. Your swift feet once pierced Hebei. You wielded your whip bravely. A literary star fell in Jiangnan overnight." Zeng Kezhuan: "With great ambition, you awaited a swift steed, hoping to soar in the wind and clouds. It is painful that you fell and died in your prime. It is difficult to make a living with dew and lightning." Chen Duan: "Your talent surpassed others. I have long been ashamed of my own literary skills. Death is predetermined. I only lament that you fell from your horse and rode a whale." Yang Hu: "With the external threat of killing the enemy, it is a pity that we have lost a pillar of talent."

Fellow Townsmen from Lishui Protest the Death of Zhou Jiuyuan; What is Zhang Binnan's Responsibility? 127

The Shanghai Lishui Fellow Townsmen Association in South Shanghai reported that member Zhou Jiufu claimed that his brother, Zhou Jiuyuan, had been working at the North Piao Coal Mine Wharf in South Huangpu. On the 6th, he boarded a coal truck driven by Zhang Binnan, a driver for the North China Coal Mine Company, to go to the North City. While driving past No. 341 Xujiahui Road in the French Concession, he lost his balance due to the swaying of the vehicle, fell, and injured his head. He immediately lost consciousness. At the time, the other workers on the truck, Li Xinxiang and Zhang Fuge, ordered Zhang Binnan to stop the vehicle to rescue him, but Zhang ignored them and continued to drive quickly. As a result, Jiuyuan did not receive medical treatment in time and died from his injuries. The body was transported by the car to the Tongren Fu Yuan autopsy center. Later, the French police summoned and questioned those involved. Zhang Binnan admitted in court that Jiuyuan died from falling off his swaying vehicle and volunteered to compensate for the costs of clothing and coffin. He then informed Jiufu to sign a statement to claim the body. However, after Zhang Binnan arrived in court, he shirks his responsibility and denied his previous statement. The deceased has a seventy-year-old mother and a wife and children. Their future livelihoods are in dire straits. Therefore, assistance is requested. Hearing this, all the fellow townsmen in the association felt indignant. They convened an emergency meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday to send personnel to investigate. They also sent a letter to the director of the French Police Station in Chu Jia Wan, French Concession, and letters to various organizations requesting assistance.

Dispute Arises Over Pig Transportation in Wusong; Almost Leads to a Strike 128

Most of the fresh pork needed daily in Shanghai is supplied by pig farms in Wusong. Therefore, thousands of pigs are transported from Wusong to Shanghai every day. The Songhu United Transportation Company and other companies are contracted to handle the loading and transportation. Recently, the company's trucks were suddenly fined and suspended from operation for one day by the Wusong Office of the Municipal Health Bureau on some pretext. The company was very dissatisfied with the penalty because the Health Bureau has no direct authority to punish vehicle violations. Therefore, it filed an appeal, requesting an investigation. This was heard by Yu Dongmo, the director of the Wusong Office of the Health Bureau, who yesterday coerced various pig farms to provide written proof that the aforementioned situation had not occurred. The pig farms refused to comply. The director then refused to issue inspection slips, preventing the pigs from being transported, as a threat. As a result, pig trucks completely accumulated on the roads outside the port, causing traffic congestion. Hearing this, the pig farms were greatly angered and collectively went on strike. Fu Zhenbei, the director of the Wusong Police Station, learned of the situation and, fearing that the incident would escalate, immediately went to persuade them. The pig farms then convened an emergency meeting and decided to appoint several representatives to go to the municipal government on the 13th (today) to thoroughly investigate the matter.

Jingjiang Fellow Townsmen Association Supports *Jingjiang Daily*; Telegrams Monitoring Yuan and Jiangsu Provincial Government to Investigate Magistrate 129

Li Jinfang, the magistrate of Jingjiang County, because *Jingjiang Daily* published an article on May 1 entitled "Injection Novel," considered it to be referring to his ambiguous relationship with a certain woman. In a fit of rage, he arrested Liu Jianfan, the editor of the newspaper, and armed the order for the newspaper to cease publication. The Jingjiang Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai learned of the incident and considered Magistrate Li's actions to be a destruction of public opinion and a trampling of human rights. They convened an emergency meeting at their association at 1:00 PM on the 12th and unanimously decided to send telegrams to the Monitoring Yuan, the Jiangsu Provincial Chairman, the Department of Civil Affairs, and the High Court, requesting a thorough investigation. They also sent letters to fellow townsmen associations in Jiangyin, Wujin, Wuxi, Suzhou, and other places, calling for united support. The association will serve as the plaintiff and file a petition with the High Court, requesting the designation of jurisdiction in order to prosecute Li for abusing his power. The telegram to the Monitoring Yuan reads: "To the Monitoring Yuan in Nanjing, transferred to Inspector Ding, Chairman Chen of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, Director Yu of the Department of Civil Affairs, Chief Hu of the Suzhou High Court. It is reported that Jingjiang County Magistrate Li Jinfang, harboring his private grudge, sealed up the *Jingjiang Daily* office and arrested editor Liu Jianfan, destroying public opinion and trampling on human rights. This is the worst example of such behavior. This meeting has decided to provide support. Please conduct a thorough investigation. The Jingjiang Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai."

City Public Works Bureau Yesterday Held an Examination for Trainees, Results to be Announced on June 2nd 130

To relieve unemployment among young people in Shanghai, the City Public Works Bureau held an examination for trainees. Only fourteen positions were available, but over four thousand people applied, demonstrating the poor economic conditions and widespread unemployment. To assist young applicants and reduce travel costs, the bureau pre-selected 160 applicants based on their clear and coherent writing, neat handwriting, and good understanding of general knowledge. These applicants were notified to take a written exam yesterday morning at 9:00 AM at the Wan Zhu Elementary School on Xiang Yuan Road, near the Xiao Bei Men. The exam was conducted in four classrooms, with the Chinese composition topic being "Everyone is Responsible for the Rise and Fall of the Nation." Five questions each were given for general knowledge and arithmetic, and examinees were given two hours to complete the test. The applicants submitted their papers at 11:00 AM. The names of those who passed will be announced on June 2nd.

Grand Opening of "Journey to the West" at the Grand Theater: Exquisite Scenery and Mechanisms: Audience Welcomes: A Sea of People 134

The new Lu Kangji Grand Theater on Er Ma Road in the Public Concession is the latest architectural addition to Shanghai. With its grand scale, it is said to be extremely popular among audiences. The reporter eagerly sought to experience it firsthand. Last night, upon receiving an invitation and reserved seating from a friend, I made my way there before 8:00 PM. At that time, the stage was presenting Sun Wukong's birth. The entire theater was filled with people, a sea of faces and fragrant clothing. The stage machinery and scenery were exquisitely chosen, and the casting was excellent. The entire play was full of highlights, especially Zhang Yipeng's performance in the Dragon Palace, where he wielded the whip with skill and ease, truly a unique talent. According to the playwright, the play, although based on the novel "Journey to the West," meticulously removed the dross and simplified the complexities. The scene where Sun Wukong avenges the snow and rescues the monkey tribe embodies the spirit of the nation, with profound implications. Other characters, such as Wu Zhongye's loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, and kindness, the Little Dragon Girl's gratitude for kindness, and the King Yama's impartiality in enforcing the law, are all essential for criticizing society and promoting morality.

Common Stage Rehearsing the Complete "Legend of the White Snake" 135

The "Legend of the White Snake" is a popular folk tale, and stage performances have become commonplace, often done carelessly and unremarkably. The Common Stage is re-arranging the play, sparing no expense, creating brand new, specially-made scenery, racking their brains to invent several scientific mechanisms, and hiring actors who fit the roles to give full performances. The magnificent scenery includes the birth of the White Snake, with lights that do not go out, transforming into human form on the spot. Also, the White and Green Snakes, each three or four zhang long, fight with magic in a room, and people are suspended in mid-air without the use of lead wires or ropes, hanging high in the air. Other scenes, such as the real scenery of West Lake, the Immortal Dao Gate, and the Kunlun Wonderland, change four times in quick succession, unexpected and surprising. It is currently being rushed day and night and will be ready for opening soon, especially suitable for responding to the capital during the Dragon Boat Festival.
