Free Talk

German Romanticism 138

— Meng Jia

Romanticism varies in its emergence due to the differing political, economic, and literary conditions of individual countries. There are also clear or subtle differences in its progressive nature. On the other hand, it stems from the differences in the societies to which various writers belong. In essence, it manifests in two styles: progressive (consistent with the laws of historical development) and degenerate (contrary to the laws of historical development).

Degenerate aristocratic Romanticism is characterized by an avoidance of reality and an immersion in irrational fantasies. This includes a retrospective tendency—such as drawing images and themes exclusively from the declining world of the feudal aristocracy, avoiding the modernity of England and tending toward Byron (Byron), who still retained natural, economic organizations, and Scott (Scott), whose themes were based on medieval life; and a flight to the countryside—taking a negative attitude toward the city, viewing it as a dirty source of all evil, and seeing the morally healthiest people in independent farmers, as exemplified by Wordsworth (Wordsworth). Similarly, in Germany during the two or three decades before and after the eighteenth century, Romanticist literature also exhibited two distinct postures. Although during this period, the color of such retrospective fantasy was intensely dyed onto both different Romanticist poems because, on the one hand, the aristocracy was forming and the serf system was collapsing, and on the other hand, the emerging citizens had not yet grasped the power to guide politics and economy, we can still see the differences even in this aspect: The retrospective fantasy nature of degenerate Romanticism is mainly because this group has already completed its historical mission and task, has lost the ability to dominate the existing society, and this realization in rapid transition makes it feel a sense of decline, so it dares not face reality, avoids it, and indulges in the memories of its young and prosperous era, using this memory to fill its own life, comfort itself, and at the same time decorate reality with it, idealize and beautify it. Examples include Friedrich Fouque and Archim Von Arnim as representatives of this art.

As one of the forward-looking Romanticists of this period, Amadeus Hoffmann, although sometimes expressing a retrospective fantasy nature in his works, his fantasy grew out of the reality of the daily life he described. What he looked back on was not the pastoral feudal era of knights, but the cities of Germany at the end of the Middle Ages (such as his description of the life of craftsmen in German cities at the end of the Middle Ages and their relationships with each other in "Barrel Master Martin and His Apprentices"). This fantasy is healthy. It is a longing for a broader world, feeling the narrowness of early bourgeois society. It is "the literature that describes a more meaningful future life in the form of an ideal poetic country." His fantasy can be said to have come from a fervent hope and prayer for the future of the new society. Such fantasy is realistic, is the image of necessity contained in reality itself, and therefore has gained the highest evaluation.

In Germany during the 1840s, due to changes in the socio-economic forms, the collapse of small industry, and the rise of the mechanical age and the commercialization of all life, brilliant new ideas suddenly emerged in the intellectual world.

At this time, Germany began to liberate itself from semi-aristocratic police supervision, from Romantic dreams, from pastoral sleep, and from the atmosphere of theological metaphysics. Therefore, the face of Romanticist literature became more diverse and complex. The new style of lyric poetry—political lyric poetry—was the product of this period. The greatest completer of political lyric poetry was Heine (Heine). The entire life of the poet Heine, a radical democrat, straddled the collapse of feudal society and the establishment of capitalist society. His life breathed in a changing society. From this came his conviction of future victory, and also his conviction of the necessity of religion; a fierce attacker of monks and emperors, and on the other hand, a lyric poet who praised love, lilies, and nightingales: a prophet with abundant eyes, and also a petty vulgar person. This instability of the intellectual in the transitional period was expressed in Heine's creation in a very clear way.

What gave Heine's current affairs and political lyric poetry a distinctive feature was Heine's unique method in creation, a special kind of Romanticism. He did not express the reality as an object in its original form, but rather transformed reality into an object of fantasy and constructed a world of fantasy. Brandes (Brandes) called this method a means of the Romantic transformation of reality. Therefore, the "interweaving of reality and shadow" in most of Heine's poems (such as "Germany: A Winter's Tale"), just as he himself called his poems "political Romanticism," is unique to Heine's poetry.

Heine wove into his lyric poetry a warm emotion and a calm wit, and gave Prussian princes, monks, and especially "papists" scolding and ridicule. His thorn-like satire and the sharp sound of ridicule gave these figures a powerful blow.

Although Heine never obtained a fixed and completely unified worldview, which caused him to show considerable confusion in his understanding of reality; however, this suffering was the suffering of all his people in that era, the suffering of the era.

In addition, Immermann, who was the same type as Heine, can only be briefly mentioned here.

Spring Outing People in Painting Cattle Bank 139

— TK

The Writer's Conscience 140

— Zuo Mu

The concept of "conscience" is usually abstracted and mystified; there is probably no absolute, general conscience in fact. Usually, people say "discovery of conscience," which, if explored using Freud's method of "psychoanalysis," seems to correspond to the human "unconscious." However, this explanation ultimately delves into the "dead end," because even the human "unconscious" has the cornerstone rooted in human social circumstances rather than Freud's libido. Different social circumstances of course cannot produce a general, universal "conscience."

This only means that human "conscience" is different, not that humans have no conscience at all. No, people with a "conscience" exist at all times and in all places.

When we look at Andre Gide's life, it is truly a great tragedy of conscience. At first, like the blind girl Gertrude in "Pastoral Symphony," he was full of yearning for the truth: "Are the birds on the earth as beautiful as they say? Why don't people tell me this at all?" The distress and cruelty that reality gave him became the fuel for his quest for truth. People say that his life changed due to the influence of Bergson's philosophy; however, in fact, it was the various conditions of reality that caused the touch of a writer with a "conscience." The words spoken by the blind girl Gertrude when her eyes were opened again seem to be Gide unburdening himself for the present: "My eyes have been opened, to a world more beautiful than I imagined. Yes, I really didn't think the sun was so bright, the air was so brilliant, the sky was so vast!"

In the furnace of reality, the waste of the writer's old consciousness will sometimes be burned off. At this time, his "conscience" is refined more and more precisely and firmly. It constantly interacts and fluctuates with the torrent of reality.

Sending A-Bao Out of the Golden Age 141

— Zikai

A-Bao, you and I have been together in this world for fourteen years now. In these more than five thousand days, we have been together almost every day, with rarely a day of separation. I watched you come into the world with a cry, and learn to speak with your first words. I watched you change from breastfeeding to eating, from crawling to learning to walk. Your demeanor gradually changed, little by little, without any trace, so that I was completely unaware and thought that you were always a child of my family, always a kind of embellishment in our family, and always a consoler of the lives of me and your mother. However, in recent years, the changes in your attitude and behavior have gradually proved that this is not the case. You have grown into a young girl without our realizing it, and are about to become an adult. The ancients said, "The age of one's parents must be known; one is happy, and the other is fearful." Now I have gone against the words of the ancients, and when I send you out of the golden age, I also feel both sad and happy.

What is happy is that the changes in your attitude and behavior in recent years are all signs that you are about to change from a child to an adult. My hard work and my mother's labor seem to have been successful, and I am secretly gratified. What is sad is that your golden age is about to end, reality is gradually being exposed, you will stop your beautiful dreams and start the struggle of life. At the same time, in us, it is as if we have lost a child who has been snuggling by our side since childhood, and gained a new friend instead. "There is no joy greater than new acquaintances": But the innocent and carefree A-Bin of the past will never be seen again?

I remember one day last spring, I took your hand and walked on the road. The falling flowers and the wind blew a flurry of willow catkins onto your hair, face, and lips, making you look like you were covered in snow and had a white beard. I smiled, held your shoulder, and wiped it off for you with a handkerchief. You also smiled, raised your head and leaned against me. This was originally a very ordinary thing for us: Before, I used to wash your face for you every day after you ate. However, the people on the road were staring at us, even laughing at us. The meaning seemed to be saying: "Such a big girl," hugging her father on the road to wipe her face! I suddenly saw that your body seemed to be taller, fully developed, and had completely changed from a neutral child to a full-fledged woman. I suddenly felt that a very high, very firm, and very thick invisible wall seemed to have been built between you and me. You grew up in my arms, and grew up in my care: But from now on, you and I will forever live in two different worlds. In an instant, I felt a deep sadness in my heart. I blamed you for not wanting to grow up forever, I blamed myself for wanting to be a child and for wanting to grow up, and I blamed mankind for having a distinction between men and women. However, after blaming, I immediately turned grief into laughter. Our A-Bin is about to grow into a big girl, isn't that a happy thing?

I remember one day when I came back from Shanghai. Your brothers and sisters, as usual, crowded around me, waiting for me to take out the "goodies" from my suitcase to share. I gladly took out a bunch of chocolates and gave each of you a pack. Your younger siblings, upon receiving these colorful gold and silver chocolates, were as happy as usual, making a big fuss and joyfully taking them to enjoy. You accepted the gift and also expressed your joy, following your younger siblings. However, a few days later, I happened to look down from the upstairs window and saw you by the flower stand, holding a newly opened pack of chocolates and dividing them among your two younger siblings. They were arguing over who got more and who got less, and you were busy dividing them equally for them. On a piece of chocolate with a missing corner, you added a piece of colorful gold and silver wrapping paper and gave it to your younger sister, so that it was fair on all three sides. They were happy to eat the candy, and you were happy to watch them eat. This surprised me. Eating chocolate has always been a great pleasure for the children in my family. Because in the countryside, there are only candies wrapped in reed leaves and cakes wrapped in straw paper, and there are no such colorful gold and silver candies; there are only extremely sweet candied dates and extremely sweet preserved green fruits, and there are no such candies with exotic aromas and flavors. (To be continued)

Leisure 142

— Feng Zi

Farmers' most common leisure place is the teahouse.

The teahouses in the countryside are very simple, so there is no need to spend much money. Just four or five copper coins will allow you to sit there for half a day. And that place is really suitable for sharing feelings and finding out news.

There are more than a hundred families in our village, but only three or four small shops. There is no teahouse. To share feelings or find out news, you have to walk more than three miles, which is not surprising for farm laborers. They have no idea that there are cars, trams, and rickshaws in the world.

When I was young, I often went to those places to sit and listen to the news. I knew most of the people who came and went to the teahouse. The news singer was called Jin Chang, and he was blind. Whatever new things happened in the various villages, as long as it was ten days later, you could hear the details from beginning to end in Jin Chang's mouth, with songs, dialogues, and jokes.

This blind man often gave people laughter, sighs, and tears.

I have been away from my hometown for ten years. And in these ten years, I have also had laughter, sighs, and tears. However, there are mostly sighs than laughter. Whenever I was sad and indignant, there was not a single pleasant joke to make me happy. Therefore, I often think of Jin Chang, the blind man. He knew how to insert jokes into tragedies to prevent everyone from being depressed; but I am always depressed, and my tragedies have never had any laughter inserted.

Maybe it's because I wanted to find laughter! This time, when I returned home, I brought with me a feeling of visiting old friends and returned to that teahouse.

The entrance was still so dim and dilapidated, not eye-catching at all: The white sign with red characters, after being beaten by wind and eroded by rain, had already lost the "spring" character from "De Chun Teahouse." Coming into the door, there was a middle-aged woman sitting on the counter, holding a child to breastfeed. In the dark house, there were seven or eight square tables, with ten or so people sitting, either chatting, dozing, or holding teapots in a daze. But I didn't recognize any of them.

I sat down at a table on the left, and a teenager poured me a pot of green tea. The eyes of the whole room were directed at me. I called to the boy who was about to turn away and asked:

"What time does the blind man Jin Chang come?"

"What blind man Jin Chang?"

"The one who sings the news."

"There's no one here who sings the news."

I felt it was pointless and didn't ask any further. But the one who was dozing across from me raised his head and looked at me.

"You look familiar!"

"Really? Old man, what's your name?"

"I'm Sanbao, the tofu seller. I haven't had a surname since I was a child."

I suddenly remembered that that person was exactly Sanbao, who shouted and sold tofu along the village every morning. He was great at talking, and we all called him San Huotou, who knew…

"Your husband is…"

"I'm the XX from the Erfang of Gutang Village."

"Ah! I recognize you. No wonder, you just asked about the blind man Jin Chang. You've been used to listening to him sing the news since you were a child."

"Yes, it's because I've been used to listening to him since I was a child. I don't know why he doesn't come now?"

"He died five or six years ago."

I wanted to ask more, but in the end I didn't open my mouth.

"It's not as lively as it used to be now. There are a lot of people, but business is slow." He said, turning his head, "We still can't make two thousand a day, can we, Sister Asheng!"

"Yes! Da Mao Ye said last night that if we continue like this, we'll have to close up." The woman upstairs replied.

"Hongtai Company has already closed its doors today." The two people who were chatting suddenly raised their voices, but then lowered them again and sighed.

Immediately, like a contagious disease, the whole room sighed.

"We can't harvest even half a grain of rice from the fields, who has spare money to sell things?" Sanbao said, shaking his head, and then turned to me: "We used to hate being busy with work and wanted to steal a little leisure and come here for a cup of tea; now we're idle all day long, where do we spend it? We drink tea until our tongues are thick."

"Eighty coins, can I get it on credit?" A tea customer ran out of the teahouse.

"Pay half, Uncle Wu!, we…" The woman upstairs said.

"I didn't bring any money today." That person ran away.

"When will you bring money!" the woman grumbled.

Sanbao was still shaking his head.

The interesting jokes were all taken away by Jin Chang. What's left here is also a tragedy without laughter inserted.

Rain (Two) 143

— By What

He paced back and forth, his mind fixed on the village at the foot of the ridge, for Juanzi lived in that village.

It was a cluster of white houses, all old and sturdy, intertwined like fortresses. Juanzi's house, where she lived with her grandmother, was near the ridge corner, appearing particularly gray and gloomy.

The pavilion was dark and dilapidated, like a broken ferry. Not only were both front and back sides open, exposing it to fierce wind and rain, but the ground was also covered with filthy puddles. When one was tired of standing, even finding a relatively dry spot to squat was impossible.

Tianli waited for them. He wondered how Juanzi, whom he hadn't seen in so long, had grown. He imagined she must be much more beautiful now. The thought of her eyes and lips made his whole body seethe with an uncontrollable, fervent passion. From the pavilion, he could see the gate of Juanzi's house. He remembered how, in their innocent youth, before the old woman had come to dislike Tianli, they had jumped on those stone steps by the entrance countless times. In a cemetery behind the village was the grave of her deceased mother. He couldn't count how many firecrackers they had set off there and how much incense they had burned during the spring and autumn festivals. And, even more unforgettable for him, was the stone bridge on the left side of the village. The memory of them lying together on the stone railing, teasing the washing women, was so sweet it felt as if it were happening right now!

Time passed slowly, but his heart was beating so fast. He felt restless. Sometimes he would glance at the "cartoons" on the pavilion walls and the small characters on the plaques, but most of the time he stared blankly at Juanzi's house. The scenery was beautiful, and the wind and rain were full of poetic charm, but none of it could touch Tianli's heart. In his mind, there was only Juanzi. He stared intently, listening as if he could faintly hear Juanzi's laughter.

The surroundings were silent, without a single movement. There were a few pine trees on the hillside, but he couldn't hear any sound, only see them swaying in the wind. All he could see was gray and white clouds and mist. Occasionally, a few people hurried past, but as the hurried sounds faded away, the "empty valley" seemed even emptier and more desolate.

The rain fell sadly and incessantly.

Page 12

Educational News

Absurd Statement Issued by Siamese Ministry of Education: Overseas Chinese in Siam Refute with Reason; Interference in Overseas Chinese Education Violates International Norms; Closure of Chinese Schools under Pretext Is Especially Arrogant 144

Since the Siamese Minister of Education, Mr. Paksan Sarapahuwa, issued his absurd statement about restricting Chinese schools, overseas Chinese in Siam and people from all walks of life in our country have been extremely indignant. The overseas Chinese education community in Siam recently refuted it point by point with reasons to awaken the Siamese authorities. Our reporter from the Industrial and Commercial News Agency obtained the original text of the rebuttal and transcribed it below:

Forcing Siamese Schools Violates International Law

(1) Although independent countries have autonomy over their own education, international practice holds that foreign nationals enjoy the right to education within the confines of the laws of their place of residence. These nationals may establish schools in their place of residence to teach their children their native language, script, and civic knowledge. For example, China has established overseas Chinese primary schools in Europe, America, Japan, and even the islands of Southeast Asia, where instruction is given in Chinese language and script. Even the curriculum is designed to meet the needs of the Chinese national situation and has been implemented for many years. It has never been heard of that any government in the place of residence has forced Chinese children to attend schools established by that country under the enforcement of compulsory education. Even in China, although the recovery of educational rights has been underway in recent years, it only applies to joint foreign and Chinese education schools and schools attended by overseas Chinese children. It is not appropriate to interfere with schools established by foreigners for their own nationals. The scope of sovereignty is, in fact, to despise international norms. (2) The Siamese Civil School Ordinance of 2461 B.E. and the Compulsory Education Ordinance of 2464 B.E. only apply to schools established for the people of Siam. There are no explicit provisions for overseas Chinese, which is also inconsistent with international practice.

Prohibition of Party Doctrine: How Can it Be Considered Lenient?

(3) Since Chinese schools and Siamese schools are different, the Siamese government should not treat them the same way or impose measures on them. Therefore, the previous methods permitted by your office, with frequent interference, are still far from the original purpose of establishing Chinese schools. How can this be considered giving special privileges to Chinese schools? (4) Based on the above, it is very clear that the Siamese government should not force Chinese schools to be uniformly restricted by these regulations. Now, even the compulsory classes established by Chinese schools are being canceled uniformly. How can one even speak of leniency in the curriculum? (5) Most of the Chinese schools are primary schools, with only two or three junior high schools. Their curriculum follows the standards set by the Chinese Ministry of Education, with only civic knowledge and no so-called political books. To adapt to the environment, Chinese schools also teach the Siamese language, literature, history, and geography. These arrangements should not hinder Siamese laws or security. Now, the Siamese government sometimes finds one or two books on the Three Principles of the People in schools and uses this as a pretext to close schools for teaching political doctrines. Is this reasonable?

Disparate Treatment of Chinese and Siamese People

(6) On the Chinese school side, the Progressive Association understands the Siamese government's intentions and勉力 proceeds, and the Siamese government prepares two kinds of democratic education regulations and hires Siamese people as principals, following the key points of teaching Siamese. The difficulties and obstacles are already difficult to describe. But now, schools are being closed on the grounds of violating laws and regulations, and the right to education that Chinese schools should have is being completely canceled. This is especially arrogant. (7) As mentioned above, the purpose of establishing Chinese schools is only to teach the motherland's language, script, life skills, and civic knowledge. There is no need to suspect the so-called teaching of political doctrines. The right to attend Chinese schools is also only for schools run by Siamese people that also teach Chinese as a subject, and also to assist Chinese people, whether newly arrived or long-term residents in Siam, to enjoy the same treatment as Siamese people, which is not entirely true. The differences are as follows: (A) Chinese people are subject to immigration laws and must pay residence taxes, while Siamese people do not. (B) Chinese people must pay for passports when leaving the country and are required to return to Siam within a limited period, while Siamese people do not. (C) In the Siamese election law, Siamese people have the right to vote, while Chinese people do not. (D) The recently promulgated fisheries regulations limit fishermen to obtaining licenses, with Siamese people accounting for 75% and Chinese people only 25%. Other unequal treatment in industrial and commercial operations is too numerous to mention. If we apply the principle that there should be rights where there are obligations, then nothing is more unequal than this.

Insulting Overseas Chinese Is Evident

(8) The Siamese Ministry of Education denies the right to establish Chinese schools and violates the purpose of overseas Chinese educating their children. It wants to force overseas Chinese to fulfill obligations they should not have to fulfill, just like fishermen use cormorants to catch fish and put a ring around their necks. In other words, it treats overseas Chinese as slaves. Its contempt for our country and insult to our compatriots is evident. Sophistry cannot cover the eyes and ears of the world.

Recent News from Zhejiang Provincial Library: Compiling and Printing General Catalog of Books... Open Day and Night Throughout the Year... Promoting Correspondence Lending... Holding Reading Campaigns 148

Since Zhejiang Provincial Library opened the University Road branch in September of the 21st year and established the original location as a branch, library affairs have been developing daily. Educational groups from Shanghai and other places who travel to Hangzhou to visit often go to see its facilities. The situation is gradually attracting attention from people at home and abroad. Recent news is as follows: (1) Promoting Reading and Borrowing: Since September of last year, the library has implemented a year-round day and night opening system, canceling the previous Monday holiday. Except for New Year's and commemorative holidays, the library is open every day from 9:00 AM to 9:00 PM, with no interruption during meal times. All sectors feel it is convenient. This year, the library is further promoting group borrowing services. By April, reading and borrowing had reached 27,750 people, an average of 975 people per day. The average number of books borrowed daily was 226. Recently, the library, in view of the small scale of libraries in various counties of the province, will formulate a correspondence lending method within the province, which will be implemented from May 1st. (2) Compiling and Printing a General Catalog of Books: The library's previous compilation and publication of the catalog was ten years ago, with incomplete content, no classification code, and unsuitable for current use. Therefore, since last year, the library has been compiling a book-style catalog that combines the old and new books that have been sorted out. The catalog contains about 100,000 books, listing the book name, author, and edition, using a self-ordered thousand-classification table. It is bound in two volumes using a five-six binding method. The first volume was published at the end of April. This is a necessity for the above two lending methods. In addition to exchanging with major libraries, the library sells pre-orders (the list price is six yuan, and the pre-order price is three yuan and six jiao). In addition, the catalog of rare books has also been compiled and is awaiting printing, and the catalog of Western books is still being compiled. (3) Holding Reading Campaigns: The library, in view of the failure to popularize the reading atmosphere, has long had the intention of holding reading campaigns. This time, the Zhejiang branch of the China Cultural Construction Association held a reading campaign at the end of April, and the library actively participated.

China-Portugal Football Cup Final: China Wins Again Against the Portuguese Team; 5-2 The Cup Has Been Permanently Preserved by China; Xu Jingcheng Was the Most Outstanding Player in Yesterday's Game 157

After winning the standard with one win and one draw in the China-Portugal Football Cup, China has shown its prominence and high morale. Yesterday, they met for the last time and gave Portugal a very fierce display of power. As a result, China won again by five to one. China's Xu Jingcheng is young and strong, good at running and grabbing. He is the real hero of China's victory. The situation of yesterday's game is briefly described below:

Portugal Takes the Lead

At the start of the game, the Portuguese team's forwards made a probing attack, which was rejected and retreated. China counterattacked with both sound and appearance. However, the enemy's defense was strict, and there was no opportunity to take advantage of it. After five minutes, China's offensive gradually weakened, and the Portuguese team attacked decisively. Colasa dribbled past people, and Gu Shangdong could not stop him. Zhang Rongcai jumped up to grab the ball and grabbed an empty space, so Luo Zican attacked and scored.

China Takes the Lead in the First Half

After losing a goal, China used its life and launched a major counterattack. Xu Juecheng ran around the field, which was quite laborious. When Li Yichen brought the ball forward, the enemy's defense committed a handball foul outside the penalty area line. Xu Jingcheng kicked hard, and it happened to hit C Huang Shanfu's hand, and a penalty was awarded. Sun Jinshun kicked it in. Five minutes later, Li Yichen cleverly scored a goal with the assistance of Liang Shutang. China's football luck turned for the better from then on. Zhong Jia contacted and advanced and passed the ball to the center from afar. Qian Jingyong saw the opportunity and rushed up, dodged the entanglement of Remidi, and was actually rushed in. In the first half, China took the lead with three to one.

Fafan Shoots Cleverly in the Gap

Changing sides and fighting again, China's offensive was still very strong. Li Yichen had a chance in front of the goal but failed to kick it in. After the enemy escaped danger, they suddenly came to the fore. Colasa came from the middle, and Li Mi stopped him. The ball fell to the right, and Fafan waited early in the gap. Taking advantage of the situation, he lifted his foot and swept low, and goalkeeper Zhang Rongcai was caught off guard and lost the goal.

Youliang and Yongsheng Both Score

After the Portuguese team scored two to two, they frequently thought of winning by surprise. Colasa and Fafan repeatedly led troops deep into the area, pressing aggressively. Fortunately, China's defense was too tight to avoid difficulty. At the bottom, Xu Jingcheng sent out a ball, Yichen's feet shuttled, and Zhong Yongsheng rushed into China from the right corner, so China won by five to.

Page 13

Economic Supplement

Silver Problem 171

— Pan Mingshan

The United States' silver policy, with the current value of the Treasury's silver holdings at $8.6 billion, while the silver reserves are only $915 million, requires the continued purchase of $1.95 billion in silver to meet the gold-to-silver ratio of 3:1. Such a large amount of silver exceeds the current total global supply. Consequently, silver outflow from our country is no accident. As of now, China's existing silver reserves amount to 1.5 billion yuan, significantly impacting our national economy. In light of this, the government, unable to declare a ban on silver exports, ordered the collection of silver export duties and equalization taxes by the Ministry of Finance on October 15th of last year. On the 19th of the same month, the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee was established. However, driven by profit, many people resort to smuggling and tax evasion. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance ordered all provinces and cities to combat smuggling in order to prevent this. Moreover, the re-export duty on silver was waived to encourage silver repatriation. The government's palliative policies have achieved considerable results.

The U.S. Treasury Secretary has repeatedly stated that the United States will continue to purchase silver until the price reaches $1.29 or the Treasury's silver reserves reach the gold-to-silver ratio of 3:1. Currently, the U.S. Treasury's fixed purchase price for silver is still 77 and 57/100 cents per ounce. The U.S.'s silver policy is relentless and will not change its established course due to the protests of one or two countries. Examining the U.S.'s vigorous implementation of the silver policy and its collection of global silver reserves, it is nothing more than a response to the global economic downturn. Countries have erected strict tariff barriers, and domestic unemployment is severe, with industry and commerce declining. To alleviate the domestic economic downturn and promote domestic industry and commerce, the rise in silver prices would increase the cost of goods in silver-using countries like China and Mexico, making it difficult to transport and sell them to the U.S. Even Japan, due to its purchase of Chinese raw materials, has seen its costs increase invisibly, indirectly affecting its exports to the U.S. This allows the United States to improve its international trade, and citizens who rely on foreign goods will switch to domestic products. Conversely, the cost of U.S. domestic goods will decrease, making exports more prosperous. The United States can then reap the benefits and complete its industrial and commercial revitalization plan. This is one reason. The global situation is precarious. Since Germany disregarded the Treaty of Versailles and expanded its military, the situation has become increasingly urgent, with a palpable sense of imminent conflict. The next world war seems unavoidable, and the country with the strongest financial resources will have an advantage, as evidenced by the First World War. The United States is storing large quantities of gold and silver with a far-reaching plan in mind. During wartime, economic hardship is inevitable, and silver is easier to distribute. Its turnover rate will be higher than gold. Therefore, the U.S. is raising silver prices at all costs, implementing its silver policy to attempt to control the world's economy. To cope with this complex situation, we can only find our own path. At the very least, we must first understand the impact of the silver policy on our country. A brief overview is as follows:

(1) Financial Market: China uses silver as its standard currency, and fluctuations in international silver prices affect the value of our currency. A sudden rise in silver prices leads to an outflow of silver, a shortage of funds in the market, monetary tightening, credit contraction, and increased interest rates. The financial sector adopts a cautious attitude towards lending to industry and commerce, leading to instability in the industrial and commercial sectors. The financial market is thus unable to stabilize, as evidenced by the financial panic in China last year and the crisis before the end of April this year.

(2) International Trade: Since countries on the gold standard abandoned it and devalued their currencies, the exchange rate of foreign currencies has fallen, making imported foreign goods expensive and difficult to sell. At the same time, the prices of our country's exports have fallen, reducing exports. To pay for this international trade deficit, a large amount of silver flows out. On the one hand, our country's export trade must calculate the value of foreign currencies based on their high or low exchange rates. If the value of foreign currencies falls, our country's exchange rate rises, and our country's exporters suffer losses due to the low exchange rate when foreign currencies are converted back home. Exports become increasingly sluggish. Therefore, silver outflow is conditioned on a trade deficit, and a trade deficit inevitably leads to silver outflow. The two are interlinked. China's trade deficit over the years has caused silver to flow out uncontrollably.

(3) Central Finance: The largest source of central government revenue is customs duties, which are levied based on the gold standard. If silver prices rise sharply, the amount of gold coins converted into silver coins will inevitably decrease significantly. This will undoubtedly cause difficulties in repaying domestic debt and raising military and administrative expenses. Moreover, import taxes based on quantity are only subject to losses from the gold and silver conversion rate, while import taxes based on value are subject to both declining prices and conversion losses. The central government's losses are substantial.

(4) Manufacturing Industry: China's industry is still in its infancy. This blow makes it difficult to gain a foothold. Emerging industries such as rubber, matches, and cigarettes have reduced production or even stopped production altogether. Large-scale silk and textile industries are facing a bleak situation, with production reductions and shutdowns occurring across the board. In the past, foreign merchants relied on their strong capital, making it difficult for Chinese manufacturers to resist. Now, with rising silver prices and cheap foreign goods, aggressive dumping is destroying China's industry as expected.

Regarding countermeasures, we should start by preventing silver outflow, reducing trade deficits, promoting domestic goods, and boosting production. A detailed description is as follows:

A. Preventing Silver Outflow: The U.S.'s silver purchase plan has repeatedly intensified, increasing the price from every ounce to 77.57 cents, and there is still a trend to continue raising it to $1.29. According to statements by powerful members of the silver faction in Congress, they will make further efforts to raise the silver price to $2.18. If their attempt succeeds, the disruption to the world's financial market will be unimaginable. As a silver-using country, China is no exception. To complete their plan, the silver faction will continue to raise silver prices to actively purchase silver abroad. China's silver is flowing out like water downhill, which is an inevitable trend. The government has taken precautions, but to thoroughly prevent silver outflow, the government should set a price to purchase it. Around January of this year, the Central Bank of China, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications released more than 20,000 bars of pure gold and purchased 20 million yuan of silver from Hong Kong. In February, the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee purchased 3 million yuan of silver from the London market. How this silver purchase policy should continue relentlessly should also be an effective way to prevent silver outflow.

B. Reducing Trade Deficits: Last year, the declared exports of silver totaled 260 million yuan, of which more than 90% was flowed out by foreign merchants and banks. The outflow of large amounts of silver by foreign merchants and banks is to pay for the international trade deficit over the years. Therefore, seeking a balance in international trade is the most effective way to prevent silver outflow. As for how to seek stable international trade and reduce trade deficits, the Ministries of Industry, Diplomacy, and Finance met on May 6th to discuss it. The fundamental solution is to maintain domestic industry so that production can be self-sufficient, and to pay attention to overseas markets to expand sales channels. An international trade committee should be organized by relevant ministries and commissions to study solutions. The government is actively taking steps to reduce the trade deficit. China's trade deficit over the years is due to the excessively low import tax rates on foreign goods, allowing them to be dumped at low prices. Conversely, the exports of domestic goods have decreased. Furthermore, due to China's backward production, it has failed to satisfy people's desire to purchase, so foreign goods are imported endlessly. To reduce the trade deficit, domestic industry should be encouraged and export taxes should be reduced. The Ministry of Finance is drafting measures to reduce export taxes and is preparing to implement them, which will be realized soon. To encourage domestic industry, import tax rates should be increased for foreign goods that can be replaced by domestic goods to resist their import. On the other hand, dumping taxes should be implemented to prevent the dumping of foreign goods, which would be very effective.

C. Promoting Domestic Goods: Rural bankruptcy, capital concentration in cities, huge trade deficits, and massive silver outflow—in the final analysis, the failure to purchase domestic goods is the root cause. Decades ago, the amount of the trade deficit was only several million, then tens of millions, and now tens of billions. If a rescue is not sought urgently, then China, with its vast territory and abundant resources, will inevitably see its national economy collapse and move towards ultimate demise. Some may believe that China's trade deficit has existed for a long time, while rural bankruptcy and industrial and commercial decline are recent conditions, assuming that the two are not related. But in previous years, the assets that flowed out mostly remained in China, created by loans from foreign merchants and banks or investments from foreign merchants. Thus, the wounds could be concealed. Now, with the U.S. raising silver prices and the pursuit of profit, silver is flowing out in large quantities. The so-called accumulated illness of several years has erupted in one day. If domestic goods could be promoted early on and waste reduced, then how could rural areas go bankrupt, and how could capital be concentrated in cities, or even if it were concentrated in cities, it would not flow overseas. China is an agricultural country, but the annual import of foreign rice has become a major import. Other foreign textiles have penetrated rural areas, and the sales channels for domestic textiles have become sluggish. China has merely become the end of the line for the promotion of rice and foreign textiles. This phenomenon is extremely dangerous. To save the situation, domestic goods should be promoted. If the government promotes domestic goods from above and the people implement them from below, why is there still little effect to this day? In short, it is because there is a lack of perseverance. We must be determined to persistently refuse to use foreign goods and not purchase them in large quantities simply because they are cheap. If there are domestic goods that can replace foreign goods, then we should try to improve their technology and vigorously promote their sales. For those without substitutes, experts should carefully study them to imitate them, working hard and diligently over time. Then, the foundation of domestic goods will be solid. How can there be dumping due to silver prices rising and foreign goods becoming cheaper? D. Promoting Production: To develop a country's economy, it must first increase its citizens' purchasing power. The U.S.'s silver policy also uses raising the purchasing power of the East as its slogan. Therefore, the fundamental method for dealing with rising silver prices is to effectively increase the purchasing power of the Chinese people. The method is to promote production. To promote production: (1) Revitalize rural areas. 80% of China's population is farmers, and the raw materials imported from abroad over the years are mostly agricultural products. Rice, wheat, and cotton textiles account for the majority. The capital currently concentrated in cities should be distributed to rural areas to revitalize them, thereby increasing their purchasing power and promoting the development of domestic goods manufacturers. (2) Develop transportation to facilitate the promotion of domestic products and adjust their surpluses and deficits. The development of highways has been rapid in recent years, allowing goods to flow smoothly and stabilizing prices, which indirectly promotes the development of industry and thereby prevents the outflow of silver.

To What Extent Will the United States Raise Silver Prices? 172

— Tan Bingwen

In the past two years, the most active endeavor of the United States in monetary policy has probably been raising silver prices. Clearly, the motivation for raising silver prices has economic and political effects, although in justice, it is rather unfair to countries like China and South America, intensifying their suffering. "But to what extent will the United States raise silver prices?" Everyone is concerned about this question. This article aims to find an answer, even if it is not an absolutely correct one—perhaps it will not be a futile attempt!

"Remembering the past is a guide to the future." Let us look back at the history of the United States raising silver prices. The beginning of raising silver prices was the Thomas Amendment in the Agricultural Relief Act. It stipulated that the United States could accept silver as repayment of war debts, but the amount was limited to $200 million, with each ounce valued at 50 cents. European debtor nations originally produced very little silver, and their silver reserves were also very limited, so although the United States had this permission, it had little practical effect. The next was the London Silver Agreement, which stipulated that the United States should purchase 24.4 million ounces of silver annually, but there was no provision for the purchase price (the original intention of the agreement was to have the United States purchase at the then-current market price, not to raise the purchase price). When the United States passed the bill on December 21, 1933, it decided that the purchase price of silver would be 64.25 cents per ounce. From this time on, the price of silver gradually increased. Later, the Silver Purchase Act of June 19, 1934, stipulated that the Treasury's gold and silver holdings should constitute a ratio of 75% to 25%. At that time, if calculated at 50 cents per ounce (because the market price had not yet risen to 64.25 cents at the time), then the United States would still need to purchase 1.3 billion ounces. This was followed by the Silver Nationalization Act of August 9, which stipulated the purchase of domestic silver at 50.01 cents. Under these two measures, the price of silver skyrocketed; the outflow of silver from China was also most intense at this time.

The White House authorities have expended great effort to implement the aforementioned steps. However, the increase in silver prices, in the eyes of the silver faction in Congress, was like a snail's pace—too slow and circuitous. Therefore, Pittman, Wheeler, Thomas, White, and others often made speeches criticizing the government, saying that "the purchase of silver has not fulfilled its duty." Until the end of last year, if the United States wanted to increase its silver holdings to constitute a ratio of 25% to 75% with gold, it would still need to purchase 1.1 billion ounces. Assuming that the average annual silver production is 180 million ounces (according to Edward Kann's estimate, see Finance and Commerce I May, 1935), and assuming that other supplies are absorbed by industrial use, then the United States would have to spend seven years to complete this task. The criticism from the silver faction in Congress, which represents the interests of mine owners, is also quite reasonable. To make them wait seven long years—not seven months! What is even more disheartening is that next year is the period for the presidential election, and no one dares to guarantee that "Franklin" will be re-elected. The former President Hoover, who is in opposition, is often complaining and declaring that the United States should best restore the gold standard. Once Hoover takes the stage again, will the seven-year long-term silver purchase plan not be overturned? No one knows if the price of $1.2919 will ever be realized. Therefore, the silver faction in Congress made every effort to demand that the government take a stronger attitude towards the silver policy, and the government was forced to raise the silver purchase price to 71.11 cents on April 10, 1935, and again to 77.57 cents on April 24. For a time, the world silver market was stirred by it. The governments of Mexico and Peru successively banned silver exports, and the suffering of China was even deeper, needless to say. It is said that in the near future (tomorrow or the day after tomorrow, it may be said), the silver purchase price will be raised again, which is very likely. The United States has long arranged the procedure for raising the silver purchase price, and the unit of increase is 5%. Observe the table on the left:

Coinage Profit　Silver Purchase Price (Unit: Cents)

45%　77.11

40%　77.57

35%　84.03

30%　90.50

25%　96.96

20%　103.43

15%　116.36

5%　122.82

0　129.29

This procedure of gradually reducing coinage profit (Seigniorage Profit), which is the procedure for raising silver prices, has already been implemented to the second step. The remaining steps will eventually be put into practice sooner or later. The focus of the debate now is: should the price be gradually raised step by step according to the original plan, or should it be raised to $1.2929 in one fell swoop? Only the silver faction in Congress knows about this, and the author does not dare to guess blindly. However, we can predict that if the price of silver really rises to $1.2929, the mine owners, who never dislike making money, will definitely have demands for even higher prices. According to recent telegrams, some members of Congress even proposed that the price of silver should be raised to $2.18 per ounce. Their reasoning is: "The Treasury's existing silver holdings, calculated at $1.29 per ounce, are worth approximately $1.45 billion. If calculated at $2.18, it would be $2.45 billion. At that point, the Treasury would only need to purchase $415 million worth of silver to establish a ratio of 3:1.—Shen Bao, 3rd of this month. This proposal also has the possibility of being passed, because on the one hand, the mine owners do not have to wait for a long seven years and can immediately enjoy the high price of $2.18; on the other hand, the duplicate standard of "two drunkards walking close together"—to use W. Kammerer's words—can descend upon Uncle Sam's house. From this point of view, the silver faction in Congress is like a black whirlwind, wishing that the price of silver would immediately rise to $1.19, then to $2.18, and then to...

However, we must doubt that raising silver prices in such an artificial way will naturally allow mine owners and speculators to obtain considerable benefits, but it is not necessarily of much benefit to the entire U.S. national economy. As a certain U.S. monetary expert said, the actual price of silver is only 25 cents, and excessive increases will inevitably lead to a reaction and a fall. Isn't the recent decline in the silver markets in New York, London, and Bombay a good example? The higher the price of silver rises, the more severe the reaction will be, which only benefits speculators. We do not understand why the silver faction in Congress and the White House authorities are doing such a stupid thing.

Furthermore, the United States' gold is also increasing day by day (this is due to the Favorable Balance of Trade and debt repayments, etc.), and silver is difficult to catch up with it. At the end of February, the Treasury's gold holdings were $7,593,721,000. In mid-March, they increased to $7,600,010,000. At the end of March, they increased further to $7,654,034,000 (according to the Federal Reserve Bulletin, Apr. 1935). Furthermore, according to the Shen Bao's Washington dispatch on May 9: "On May 6, the U.S. Treasury's gold holdings actually increased to $8,725,313,788, while silver holdings were only $1,500,000,000." Perhaps the United States will increase the price of silver to around $3 because the increase in silver is too slow—this is also very possible!

Under the threat of another sharp rise in silver prices, China suffers the most, followed by Mexico and Peru. At the end of last month, the Mexican government implemented a new monetary system policy, banning the export of silver coins and replacing various silver coins with paper money. All banks have been ordered to suspend business for a week. On the other hand, they have nationalized existing silver and will set a new exchange rate of three yuan and five jiao for one U.S. dollar. The Mexican authorities' flexibility in handling affairs is truly admirable. Regarding the situation in Peru, the Shanghai Daily News on May 5 had the following record: "The Peruvian government, in order to prevent the melting of silver coins, has banned exports this month. The government has ordered the nationalization of domestic silver production and has adopted a silver export license system." It seems that even small countries are unwilling to lag behind in dealing with currency wars.

What about our China? We originally had a good weapon—the equalization tax—but we have not been able to make good use of it. The difference between the London silver price and the Shanghai silver price these days is about 36%, but the equalization tax is always lazy and does not move—6.75%! Short-sighted financiers and theorists believe that besides extending foreign exchange, there is no possibility of silver export. The "Gentlemen's Agreement" between Chinese and foreign banks on the 16th of last month was really because foreign banks had no silver, so they had to flirt with each other. Honestly speaking, there will not be any changes in the short term. At the same time, the Shanghai Daily News also said on May 7. "Silver flowing out of Manchuria via the Korean Railway has reached a large sum of 35,000,000 yuan in the past week. The puppet government of Manchukuo has also adopted a passport system." It can be said that it is completely thanks to the United States for this increase in silver prices. Continuing to follow the old path without making progress is not a solution!

Prospects for Overseas Silk Markets 173

— Ling Yun

Our country has always been known throughout the world for its silk production. Unfortunately, there has been no attempt at improvement. For decades, silk-making machinery has stubbornly adhered to old methods. As a result, this only export capable of offsetting huge import surpluses has been seized by the Japanese and abandoned by the United States, a major user of silk. Isn't this a lamentable situation? Now, this great dream is beginning to awaken, and efforts are being made to revive the industry. It may not be too late to mend the fold after the sheep are lost. However, given the increasingly fierce competition in international industrial economics, the future still feels chilling. Last year, the consumption of raw silk in the United States saw an increase. On the surface, it seems that silk-producing countries in the East have a chance of recovery. However, a closer examination of the details may not warrant optimism.

U.S. Raw Silk Consumption Statistics for 1934 (Unit: bales)

Japanese Silk European Silk Chinese Silk Total

January 39,296 330 1,316 40,942

February 37,991 98 932 39,021

March 41,815 615 650 44,080

April 36,324 434 634 37,392

May 37,919 352 469 38,740

June 32,162 395 512 32,079

July 29,418 1,063 1,540 32,021

October 47,687 625 794 49,106

November 36,528 367 653 37,548

December 39,558 450 933 40,941

Total 446,004 5,386 10,316 461,706

According to the above statistics, the consumption of raw silk in the United States is on the path to progress. Compared to December of the previous year, with 26,959 bales consumed, last year's consumption has indeed increased significantly. However, the price of silk in New York often fluctuates between $1.10 and $1.20 USD. It was not until mid-November that it showed a brief surge, followed by a decline, and it remains around $1.20. The mystery behind this lies in the manipulation by American and Japanese silk merchants, which is not difficult to investigate. The reason why the consumption of raw silk in the United States gradually turned around last year is due to silk merchants spending huge sums of money on various promotions, showcasing the features of pure silk products, and emphasizing the economic benefits of buying genuine silk products, which aroused public attention and boosted sales. Lower prices were also a contributing factor. However, the main reason is the sudden decrease in the production of rayon. In 1934, the total production of rayon in the United States was 190,000,000 pounds, compared to 207,580,000 pounds in 1933, a decrease of 17,580,000 pounds, which translates to approximately 130,000 bales of raw silk. The sales of silk fabrics in the United States can be said to be increasing daily. If not for the major threat of rayon, the production of raw silk could have unlimited development. The reason for the short production of rayon in other countries is neither a shortage of raw materials nor other significant obstacles. So, what is the reason? Modern commercial competition has very clever tricks. Would rayon merchants sit idly by and do nothing in the face of actions detrimental to them by silk merchants? Talented people versed in the mechanics are setting up new machinery for their capitalists, so that the products are improved, the cost is reduced, and some have invented wood pulp raw materials, which can save 50% of the original cost, and so on. Therefore, whether the United States will be able to continue to consume large amounts of raw silk in the future is still worth studying.

Japanese silk prices are expected to rise due to reduced autumn cocoon harvests and bullish sentiment in Yokohama. If it were before last year, Japanese silk could have sailed smoothly last year and obtained satisfactory returns. However, due to the relationship with rayon, they have to obey the trend of the New York market and dare not raise their prices too high. They truly deserve to be called experts in observing the situation in the world market.

Japanese cocoons and silk are so cheap that farmers are complaining endlessly. Although they receive various subsidies from the government, it is still of no avail. Last year, the total income of silkworm farmers was 197,290,000 Japanese yen, only one-third of the previous year's income, and the lowest new record in the past ten years since farmers engaged in silkworm farming.

The United States consumes 96.6% of Japan's total silk production, but Japan's silk production is still excessive. Therefore, all silk-consuming countries in the world have traces of dumping. Even India and Australia, which have backward production, have now successfully entered their markets. The following is a list of their export quantities last year for reference:

Japanese Silk Export Quantity Statistics for 1934

Unit: bales Value (Japanese Yen)

Exports to the US 433,437 244,379,365

Exports to France 36,574 20,333,890

Exports to the UK 23,878 14,237,056

Total 505,998 286,793,875

Last year, the selling price of Japanese silk was very low. The highest price in the Yokohama market (based on the B grade standard) was 675 yen in mid-February, and the lowest was 437.5 yen in September. Compared with the previous year's highest price of 1,090 yen and the lowest price of 520 yen, the difference is indeed alarming. Fortunately, its exchange rate with the United States is controlled by the government and is often between 28.3 and 28.55, so its silk-making business, although in great difficulty, has not been particularly affected, which is also a good phenomenon in misfortune.

Japanese merchants began to hope for a rise in silk prices at the beginning of December last year, but they have not yet achieved their wishes. However, they have never forgotten this. Therefore, in the three months since spring, the United States has consumed more than 44,000 bales per month, while Japan's monthly shipments to the United States are only more than 30,000 bales. It can be seen that the Japanese intend to reduce New York's inventory and use the air of insufficient domestic supply as a smokescreen to compensate for their long-cherished wish. This is also the reason for the sudden activity in overseas markets recently.

Securities: Except for 96 Bonds, Public Bonds Were Stagnant Last Week 175

Last week, from May 6th to May 11th, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange only conducted five days of trading, excluding the May 9th Memorial Day market closure. The market conditions were generally lackluster. The stagnation of market prices and the light trading volume were unprecedented in recent years. Although the depressed environment was one reason for this situation, the lack of loans, the financial crisis, and the commercial depression did not reduce public anxiety. Many asset holders, given the volatility of the financial sector and the unpredictable changes in the future, are now shifting to purchasing public bonds. However, most investments are not enthusiastic due to the limited interest earned on holdings. Speculators also refrained from action due to the lack of opportunity. Under these market conditions, prices naturally tended towards stagnation, with no changes. As a result, trading volume also decreased sharply. Last week, only the 96 Public Bonds were relatively active, and trading volume was also higher. In addition, various bonds were almost completely stagnant. Cotton Yarn: American Cotton Fell, Then Rebounded at Closing 177

Yesterday, American cotton opened lower due to selling by foreign merchants, especially those from Mainland China and Bombay. Bulls took profits, and prices for all months fell by 5 to 7 points. Subsequently, due to good local demand and government purchases of futures cotton to offset sales of stockpiled cotton, prices rebounded. The number of sellers gradually increased as prices approached 12 cents. At the same time, buyers were hesitant, fearing increased movements in the interior. Closing prices were firm. Spot prices fell by 5 points, and futures prices fell by 1 to 5 points. English cotton spot prices rose by 4 points, and futures prices rose by 5 to 6 points. Oil Market: White Tung Oil Market Stable 179

The outflow of white tung oil from Hankou foreign firms continues unabated, and the market fluctuates constantly. This is because foreign firms' purchases fluctuate daily, causing prices to rise and fall frequently. At the end of last week, the situation looked weak, but after entering this week, it suddenly increased to over 40 yuan per dan, and the day before yesterday it fell back to 39 yuan 4 jiao, but last night's telegram showed it rising again to 40 yuan. Foreign trade is prone to rise and fall, so a fluctuation of one or two yuan is not surprising. As for the source of supply, foreign firms also purchase in the producing areas, and Sichuan tung oil is shipped directly from Wanxian to Shanghai for transshipment, bypassing Hankou for a long time. Therefore, most of the tung oil arriving in Hankou is inferior tung oil. Xiang tung oil from Changde also has foreign firms purchasing, and the prosperity of Hankou is no longer what it used to be. Even though the quantity of tung oil produced in various producing areas increases annually, Hankou's volume decreases year by year. This is because transportation has gradually reached the interior, and foreign merchants' purchases have also penetrated into the producing areas. Although Hankou is a native product market in our country, holding the north-south hub, with the rapid progress of transportation, the market is becoming increasingly scattered. It can be seen that market changes are rapid and change with transportation. In the future, it may transfer to Shanghai, which is also unknown. According to details in recent letters from Hankou, the opening price for Xiang tung oil from brokers is 23 taels to 23 taels 12 qian, and the quantity is also small. The tung oil exported from this port mainly comes from Zhejiang province. The quantity has increased sharply in the past two years, mainly due to sluggish domestic sales, forcing sales to foreign countries. However, the quality of the products produced last winter is insufficient, so selecting goods for export inevitably requires careful consideration.

North-South Goods: Raw Peanuts Market Weakens in Qingdao 180

Due to the softening of prices in Qingdao, buyers here are waiting and watching, hoping for a further decline. However, sellers, facing gradually declining inventories, insist on not lowering prices. Therefore, quoted prices are high, resulting in no transactions. According to insiders, all existing inventory may be difficult to replenish in the future.

Metals: Limited Progress in Lead Market 181

The quantity of lead purchased by tea shops recently has not been large, so there have not been many transactions in the market. Paint companies and yellow dan factories have also reduced purchases due to sluggish sales. There were few transactions in the city, but more goods arrived from overseas, resulting in an increasingly saturated market. Standards therefore have no new developments, and the price remains around 14 yuan per dan for cash. For bulk transactions, the price may be cheaper by one or two jiao. It is said that only one or two hundred bars were sold in the market yesterday, all of which were purchased by small customers. Manufacturers only inquired about prices.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 182

— (Xu Jie)

A person born into this world cannot be thorough in everything. To be thorough is to be unable to live as a person.

In water and air, there are countless microorganisms that can transmit diseases and kill people. If a person is thoroughly fastidious about hygiene, they would not dare to drink water or breathe air. How could they live as a person?

People from birth to youth, to adulthood, to old age, eventually die. Through decades of hot and cold, joys and sorrows, partings and reunions, birth, aging, sickness and death, it is truly like a dream. If you think about it thoroughly, would you still be willing to live as a person?

As the saying goes, "Clear water has no fish." To hate evil like an enemy, to be the only one sober in a drunken crowd, to seek perfection in everything in the current era, to be thorough in everything, will inevitably lead to running into walls everywhere. How could you live as a person?

Sugar tastes sweet, but saccharin becomes bitter. People should be "good," but "too good" people turn into "bad" people. Therefore, in life, one cannot be too thorough. Always go with the flow, and it is good to be "rarely confused"!

The Cherries Are Red 183

— One Heart

— Written for Mother's Day, May 12th —

I happened to take a copy of Bai Xiangshan's Ci Poetry from the bookshelf and turned to a poem by Jiang Jie, "A piece of spring sorrow is poured with wine. The boat rocks on the river. The curtain招招 on the building. Qiu Niang is graceful and Tai Niang is charming. The wind is blowing, the rain is pouring. When will the cloud sail be unloaded at Pu Bridge? The silver-character zheng is tuned. The heart-character incense burns. Time easily throws people away. The cherries are red. The bananas are green." I couldn't help but feel a little gloomy.

It was in the late spring three years ago when I was eating the first red cherry that the news of my mother's serious illness came to me. But when I rushed home, my mother was already lying quietly on the wooden board. Besides her last crystal tear, which was still hanging in her sunken eye socket, as if to replace comfort, I could no longer hear her say, "Zhen'er, you're back. Are you hungry?"

My mother was indeed a typical virtuous mother. She had the willpower of a shrewd and capable person. On her thin face, there was always an expression of love. Although my father abandoned us for a mistress when we were young, my mother still harmoniously raised us and prevented our fragile and innocent childhood from being covered with some sorrowful tunes.

I still remember very clearly that every night before going to bed, we always tugged at my mother's skirt, asking her to tell us an anecdote about an ancient filial son or hero. Of course, she never refused, and she would tell us with such spirit, making us forget all our pain and fatigue.

Sometimes my sister and I would fall asleep in my mother's tragic singing. Undoubtedly, countless tears were hidden in this forced laughter.

"Time easily throws people away." The season of sending spring has come again. When the first cherry of the market reflects in my eyes, I think of my only dear mother again. She has been dead for three years. In these short two years, who knew that your unprogressive son has been driven by life into a wreck full of wounds? Alas, mother!

Star Shift Field 184

— Ziwei

"Star Shift Field" is a common saying in Suzhou. On a clear summer night, we cool off in the courtyard and look up at the bright Milky Way, with its many stars scattered here and there. The light is bright and beautiful. Suddenly, a line of light flashes past like lightning. Looking closely, it turns out that a star has moved its position. According to ancient legend, this is the so-called "Star Shift Field."

What I am talking about now is not the "Star Shift Field" in the sky, but the migration of the Shanghai Star Film Company's factory site. The lease of the old site of the Star Company on Pushi Road has expired. They wanted to relocate to a better place. After a long search, they found a piece of land near Xujiahui Road near Fenglin Bridge in western Shanghai. It just so happened that it was next to the former municipal government. There are secluded trees and green grass, as well as three tall foreign-style houses, covering an area of ​​more than 30 acres. The two planned photography fields are about to start construction.

Half a month ago, the workers had already moved many props by truckload. The day before yesterday, although a housewarming ceremony was held, the office had not yet moved.

On the afternoon of the housewarming day, more than 300 male and female stars and all employees took a car in a line to reach the gate of the new company. Ten thousand firecrackers and Gaosheng fireworks went off, and the sound almost deafened everyone. After the colleagues entered the ceremony hall to participate in the ceremony, they also inspected the area for a week and felt that the place was three times larger than the old site. Everyone enjoyed some refreshments and dispersed in the misty evening.
