— Yue

Little Western Heaven 186

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Episode Thirteen: Yesterday's Marriage Made Selling Oneself Difficult; Merchandise as Slaves Also Enjoy Bankruptcy to Speak of Farmers

This isn't because the local authorities don't scrutinize teachers; fundamentally, it's because the inland areas lack such talent. If we don't use these people who remember old books, I'm afraid there will be no one to teach. Therefore, some young people in the area, planning for their own future and the literacy of the locals, don't make any grand plans. They run to the county elementary school, muddle through for two or three years, learn some geography, history, arithmetic, and writing, and then they can go to the countryside to lead those who are illiterate. This is unavoidable. I ask you, who, truly trained as an elementary school teacher, would be willing to go to the countryside to earn two dollars a month? So the difficulty of teacher resources is definitely not just a problem of one county. It depends on how the provincial education authorities come up with a complete plan to revitalize it, so that there is hope of getting on the right track.

In Xi'an city, they have already set up an elementary school teacher "training center." Perhaps in a year or two, these difficult situations can be gradually reduced. After listening, Zhiqian stood up and slapped himself on the head a couple of times, laughing: "Should be hit, should be hit! I've been a county magistrate in Shaanxi for half a year, but I didn't realize that lower-level education had such difficulties. This county magistrate of mine should have taken off his black gauze hat long ago, why wait until today to get a reprimand and resign?" Zhiqian laughed: "Let's not talk about it anymore, talking back and forth will only arouse County Magistrate Zhou's complaints again. Probably that Miss Zhu has changed into her fanciest clothes and left long ago. The door isn't locked, I should go back and take a look. Beihai, why don't you come to my room? Let me give you extra lessons." When Beihai heard this, he picked up his schoolbag and stood up. Zhou Yourong was talking with great enthusiasm, and their sudden departure was quite disappointing, but it was not appropriate to force them to stay and chat. (202)

Records of Lingering Fragrance from the Imperial Court 187

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Because these dogs are all very small in size, they definitely cannot guard at night or do other work. They can only be cuddled in the arms or held in the hands as a small toy to play with. Later, after we entered the Pass, almost all Manchurian families kept this kind of dog, and we all lived in the capital. Therefore, when outsiders saw this kind of dog, they all called it the Pekingese. Now it is called by its name. 1

What was this imperial dog house like? Of course, it was not some deep palace hall—but its scale was vastly different from ordinary people's dog houses. Its format also imitated the palace, but was only a few times smaller. Its building materials were not wood or stone, but all made of bamboo heads. There were also four eunuchs managing these dogs, one was considered the leading chief, and the other three were his assistants. They also stayed in the palace all year round, not asking about other matters, only accompanying those puppies. Although they were ordered to manage these dogs, they could not really be said to "manage" them, but only to "serve" them. How dare they easily beat or scold them, they could only serve them carefully.

When our group was about to approach the dog house, an eunuch tending the dogs saw us and shouted loudly:

"The Empress Dowager has arrived!" He shouted very loudly and slowly, almost one word at a time. (312)

Leftovers 188

— Nineteen

Whether in the afternoon or evening, after the meal bell rings every day, there are always many people waiting at the gate of the neighboring school. Among those people, there are men, there are women, there are old, and there are young. They either carry broken baskets, or hold tile bowls, or take teacups, mostly dressed in incomplete coarse clothes, with sallow complexions and thin bodies; they are poor people living near that school.

After a while, a person from the school came out carrying a shoulder pole; behind him, there was another person following. The noisy situation began like this. When the shoulder pole carrier rested at the school gate, those people with dripping saliva swarmed forward. Some contribute one copper coin, some contribute three copper coins, some even contribute as much as six copper coins—this is probably the largest number. Then one person collects the money, announcing the numbers aloud; another person bends down, holding an iron scoop in hand, like Chen Ping dividing meat, distributing the leftovers in the pole to those poor people according to the amount of copper coins. Those who complain about too little, stretch out their dirty hands, and take one or two handfuls from the pole; the person guarding the pole does not stop them. There are also those who come late, carrying disappointed emotions, and returning empty-handed.

So what are those leftovers? There are meat bones, there are fish bones, there are vegetables, there is tofu. In short, they are leftover things; to put it nicely, you can call it a big mix. However, those who buy leftovers truly treat it as a big mix: if they occasionally get a piece of fish tail, they are very happy, saying that it can be used to cook noodles. After the leftovers are all bought up, the cook counts the copper coins, and sometimes frowns and says: "The capital for buying Chao cigarettes is not enough!"

After that time, what is parked at the door is a chartered car.

Places Visited

A Brief Account of the Historical Sites of the Confucius Temple in Qufu 189

— Nanggongsheng

Qufu in Shandong is the hometown of the Most Sage Teacher Confucius. Confucius is the master of literature in our country, that is, the most sacred person who promotes our culture. His hometown, the cultural memorial sites about him, are naturally countless. Therefore, people who go to Qufu must go to admire the relics of this eternal master of literature to broaden their knowledge. From Qufu Station to Qufu City, there is a distance of eighteen li. This is because Confucius' tomb, the Confucius Forest, is three li away from the city. If the station were too close, it would shake the Confucius Forest. This is also an expression of respect for the sage. From Qufu Station to the "Dacheng Hall" in the city, the historical sites I heard about at the Confucius Temple can be briefly recorded as follows:

Queli... Queli is where Confucius lived in Qufu City. Everyone who has read the Four Books knows that it is a short alley on the right side of the current Confucius Temple gate. There is a wooden archway across the street with the two large characters "Queli" written on it, so that people can know that they have arrived at Confucius' former residence at first glance.

Apricot Altar... Confucius taught at the Apricot Altar, with a thousand disciples, which is a famous story throughout the ages. Entering the gate of the Confucius Temple, the first thing you see is the Apricot Altar, about five or six zhang in size. It is a pavilion-like house, but the front is open and there are no windows. It is only a little over a chi high, reached by stone steps. In the center of the top is a golden "Apricot Altar" horizontal plaque. Two stone tablets are erected in the altar. This Apricot Altar is said to be where Confucius taught.

Confucius' Hand-Planted Cypress... It is a cypress tree that Confucius himself planted with his own eyes when he was alive, but now, only a section of dead wood, a relic, remains.

Dacheng Hall... The Dacheng Hall is the main hall of the Confucius Temple, the main hall for worshiping Confucius. Outside the hall are stone pillars with dragons coiled around them, very solemn. In the center of the hall is a statue of Confucius, about two zhang in height. Standing on both sides are the statues of Yanzi, Zisi, Mencius, and Zengzi, which are the four sages who are paired for worship. On both sides of the four sages are the statues of disciples such as Zilu and Zigong, all gilded and dazzling, making people feel respectful. On the top of the hall are plaques bestowed by emperors of past dynasties. The height of the hall is as much as seven or eight zhang. Looking at the plaque above, the hat on your head has to fall to the ground, which shows how high the hall is.

Hall of Grandmother Kong... The Hall of Grandmother Kong is the hall for worshiping Confucius' wife. The buildings and facilities are all secondary to the Dacheng Hall. Only the stone pillars outside the hall are also coiled with golden dragons. Inside the hall is a statue of Confucius' wife.

Hall of Sacred Traces... The last hall is called the Hall of Sacred Traces. Inside are seventy-two famous paintings, all stories of Confucius, from Confucius' birth to his death. These famous stories of his life are all inside. After seeing them, you can know a brief history of Confucius' life. The sacred traces pictures are sold in complete sets in Qufu. In addition to the seventy-two sacred traces pictures, there is also a stone carving of Confucius, which can also be bought in Qufu city.

Zhang Menglong Stele... Many people who write the characters of the Northern Wei Dynasty take the Zhang Menglong Stele as a model. The original Zhang Menglong Stele is also in the Confucius Temple, sealed with vermilion railings. Once a year, the person in charge of the Confucius Temple opens the seal and orders people to take the stele down and sell it to the outside world. Therefore, rubbings of the Zhang Menglong Stele in Qufu can be seen and bought everywhere, and are not very rare.

The above records are just a glimpse of the historical sites of the Confucius Temple. The rest, such as the Qisheng Hall, which enshrines the spirit tablets of Confucius' five generations of ancestors, and the two corridors, which also enshrine the spirit tablets of the seventy-two sages, along with the two-zhang-high stone steles everywhere in the temple, can all be seen. Only the musical instruments in the Confucius Temple and the various objects used for worshiping Confucius occupy a very important position in our country's culture, but they are rarely seen when celebrating Confucius.

Shen Bao Medicine Weekly

The Current Situation and Areas for Improvement in Health Education in Nanjing 190

— Yunshi

Education in Nanjing is very developed. People who run education generally know that in addition to the intellectual development of children, they also know that physical health and education are equally important. Therefore, the participation of health education in children's lives, affecting the physical and mental health of children in the future, is indeed very meaningful.

The establishment of the Municipal Health Education Committee is tasked with the mission of ensuring the physical health of students. This kind of work is welcomed by society. Therefore, when health education was first started in Nanjing, there were 21 schools. In three or four years, it has gradually increased to more than 120 schools. Now Nanjing has divided these 110+ schools into five districts, one of which is called the School Health Experiment Department, which uses experimental methods to study school health work in order to quickly promote the mission of physical health.

Currently, there are more than 120 schools under the management of the Health Education Committee in Nanjing, with a student population of more than 35,000. Therefore, due to the zonal nature of the work, a new plan has been re-established from the 23rd to the 24th year. His work roughly includes the following five items:

(1) Health Care Work—New student health checkups. Follow-up checks of deficiencies. Correction of deficiencies. Training of hygiene teams. Cleanliness inspections, etc.

(2) Environmental Hygiene—Inspection, reporting, and improvement of two items.

(3) Preparation Work—Vaccination and experimental vaccine injections, etc.

(4) Treatment Work—Diagnosis of minor illnesses and referral of infectious diseases.

(5) Special Work—Such as school health training courses, student family liaison, student family hygiene improvement, etc. (This kind of work is mostly during winter or summer vacation)

The above five work items and periods are generally carried out in accordance with the school student implementation plan stipulated by the Department of Health. The general situation of the doctor's work: the director of the Health Education Committee is directly under the School Health Department of the Department of Health. Most of his work is in administrative aspects. The remaining doctors are probably doing health checkups and treating diseases.

School Health Nurse Work: Every week, nurses take turns going to schools to correct deficiencies (such as trachoma, skin diseases, etc.), give hygiene lectures, do health care work, inspect student cleanliness issues, and improve environmental hygiene.

Student Activities: Morning cleanliness inspection, assisting in correcting deficiencies, first aid work, etc.

Administrative Aspects:

Municipal Government - Health Education Committee (Social Bureau) - Health Office - Education Bureau - School District - School

Economic Sources:

Health Office: 7,200 yuan, Municipal Government: 4,200 yuan, School health expenses: 8,600 yuan, four jiao per person

Equipment Aspects:

Now the schools in Nanjing generally have a health room. Unfortunately, some schools have few houses, so they have a medicine cabinet. The medicine cabinet is very simple, and what is stored inside are some first aid and disinfectant medicines. Hanging on the wall are educational picture books published by the Department of Health, and sometimes there are a few educational photos. The second thing is various records.

The above is a general overview of the current situation of school health in Nanjing.

Below are the two points I hope to improve:

(1) Even Distribution of Economy: Even distribution of economy is the most important thing. I see that the allocation of funds for health education in Nanjing is too uneven. Looking at one item stipulated in the implementation plan, for example, travel expenses should not exceed 10% at most, but now health education has exceeded 20%. According to the above economic sources, the Health Education Committee's annual income is 20,000 yuan, and in the new plan for the 24th year, 3,270 yuan is prepared for travel expenses. Moreover, most of this money is used for nurses. When nurses travel for a long time, their working hours are reduced. Therefore, I personally hope to increase the number of nurses and replace travel expenses. Why? Suppose the Health Education Association hires six nurses, it will only cost 2,880 yuan (calculated at 40 yuan per person per month), and the remaining 400 yuan will be used for the doctor's travel expenses. I think this will reduce their working range and increase the number of staff, and increasing the time can increase work efficiency. So I always feel that this is better.

(2) Cooperation with Schools: Cooperation between schools in Nanjing and the Health Education Association is a very important issue. I hope that this matter will not cause difficulties for schools and the Health Education Association. Although sometimes, because the Health Education Association's work is not allocated properly, often a school does not have a deficiency correction or other work even once a week, which sometimes can make the school regret it and cause problems of disagreement. Therefore, I personally like to use the method of teaching more, and get close to the principal and students, because with more closeness, there will naturally be opportunities for cooperation. Therefore, many people think that this kind of advocacy is difficult, but in fact, two schools only need to pay 41 yuan, saving two kinds of health education fees; it is still worthwhile. Even the even distribution of economic expenses has a great relationship with cooperation issues.

I have only written out these few points for the plan for improvement, and I hope that the school health teachers will correct me.

A Brief History of School Oral Hygiene in Various Countries (V) 191

— Situ Xue

School Oral Hygiene in Japan

Since the Meiji Restoration in Japan, science has prospered, and all industries have advanced rapidly. The development of dental medicine is not only the best in East Asia, but also comparable to Europe and the United States. Therefore, special attention is paid to the oral hygiene movement, especially the oral hygiene of the army and navy, which is more advanced than that of European and American countries. At the time of the Russo-Japanese War, there was already the appointment of dental military doctors. As for school dentistry, in the 35th year of Meiji, the Kojimachi district of Tokyo City had already appointed four dentists to conduct oral examinations of elementary school children. This can be said to be the earliest start.

By the second year of Taisho, the school oral hygiene movement became more vigorous. The following year, the 26th Newspaper Company opened a popular hygiene exposition at Shinobazu Pond in Ueno, Tokyo. The products related to dental applications were also extremely rich, which aroused public interest. In April of the same year, a school dental treatment center was established in the Third Higher Girls' School of Tokyo Prefecture. This was probably the first dental treatment center in a secondary school in Tokyo City.

In the ninth year of Taisho, the equipment of the treatment center was further improved and greatly renovated. It is still very active today. This is probably the most historical school dental treatment center in Tokyo City.

In April of the sixth year of Taisho, Hiroshima City appointed six dentists from the city authorities to conduct oral examinations of schoolchildren in the city. In June of the seventh year, the Osaka City Dental Association issued special treatment coupons for the purpose of rescuing the poor. In August of the same year, the Lion summer "oral hygiene lecture" gathered about 200 school teachers from all over the country and held the first meeting in Tokyo to promote oral hygiene. Since then, it has been continuing every year. By March of the eighth year, a proposal on "oral hygiene for elementary school children" was submitted to the parliament, and the government committee approved it. In April of the ninth year, the Japan United Dental Association held an oral hygiene lecture to promote it. In October, the Ministry of Internal Affairs opened a children's hygiene exhibition at the Education Museum. Taking this opportunity, they held a "Tooth Prevention Day" to awaken public attention to oral hygiene. In May of the tenth year, people of insight in Tokyo established the Oral Hygiene Research Association. In August, the Hongo District Dental School Doctors Association was established. In September, Mr. Kobayashi opened a Children's Dental Hospital. And other cities such as Chiba, Okayama, and Osaka were also very enthusiastic about the school dental hygiene movement. From this, we can know how much attention was paid to children's oral hygiene at that time.

In the twelfth year of Taisho, the Japan United Dental Association published "Oral Hygiene Materials" in two volumes. (Volume 1 was written by Mr. Endo, and Volume 2 by Mr. Kawakami). Since this year, elementary schools in Tokyo City have been vigorously promoting dental examinations, which has developed greatly. In September of the same year, the Kanto Great Earthquake was encountered. The dental medical group ignored their own safety and organized a dental rescue team to serve the society. In November, Lion Company and Club Company organized a mobile dental clinic team and began to treat children in various elementary schools in the city.

In March of the 14th year of Taisho, Aomori Prefecture took the lead in the country and promulgated regulations for the appointment of school dental doctors by prefectural decree. After that, various prefectures also promulgated regulations. By the fourth year of Showa, two prefectures and twenty-five counties had followed the regulations of the prefectural decree, gradually forming a very organized oral hygiene movement. Each prefecture has a school dental doctor association, and the number of school dental treatment centers is also increasing year by year. Taking Tokyo City as an example, there are about fifty, and nearly two hundred throughout the country. However, there are fewer municipal ones, only a few cities such as Kanazawa, Otaru, Hakodate, and Asahikawa.

Since the third year of Showa, the Japan Dental Medical Association, with the support of the Ministry of Internal Affairs and the Ministry of Education, has stipulated that June 4th every year is "Tooth Prevention Day." On this day, the whole country is enthusiastic, taking schools, students, factories, and the army as the center, carrying out extensive publicity. The whole country speaks with one voice and carries out regular oral hygiene movements. Countries around the world are probably not comparable.

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases 192

— Cheng Hanzhang

(57) Osteomalacia (continued)

Q: What are the changes in the muscles?

A: The muscles are mostly weak, especially the iliopsoas muscle is more obvious, and the movement of ascending the stairs is very difficult. In addition, the adductor muscles of the thigh spasm, making it difficult to extend the legs.

Q: What other symptoms are there?

A: Others include mild fever, secondary anemia, abnormal menstruation, and proteinuria.

Q: How long does this osteomalacia last?

A: It usually lasts two to three years to five years, and sometimes ten years. Sometimes the disease stagnates temporarily, but it worsens during pregnancy and childbirth in early spring.

Q: What is the prognosis of this disease, good or bad?

A: If appropriate treatment is not given, death will result from high-grade weakness, cachexia, pneumonia, sepsis, etc.

Q: How to diagnose osteomalacia?

A: In women, attention should be paid to previous pregnancy and childbirth disorders. In men, pay attention to deformities of the chest and spine. If X-rays are used to diagnose bone shadows, it can be more accurate.

Q: What diseases should be differentiated?

A: It should be differentiated from bone cancer, war osteomalacia, and multiple myeloma.

Q: What is the treatment method for osteomalacia?

A: There are dietary therapy, physical therapy, and drug therapy.

Page 16

Q: What is dietary therapy?

A: Patients should eat fresh fruits and vegetables, milk, cream, eggs, rice, vitamin D, fish liver oil, etc.

Q: What is physical therapy?

A: Patients should breathe fresh air, be exposed to sunlight, and be irradiated with artificial sun lamps. Take water baths every day, especially carbonic acid baths and mineral spring baths.

Q: What is drug therapy?

A: Take preparations containing phosphorus, calcium preparations, fish liver oil, adrenal cortex extract, etc.

Q: What other methods are there for treatment?

A: Perform castration, radiate the ovaries with X-rays, and perform artificial abortion during pregnancy. (End)

The Medicine of Pain Relief (14) 193

— Li Xing

Neuralgia

Neuralgia is a type of pain caused by irritation or inflammation of nerve fibers. The most common neuralgia affects the trigeminal nerve in the face, followed by the nerves in the lower posterior part of the head where it connects to the neck, the intercostal nerves, the lower cervical nerves near the neck, and the nerves in the upper thigh joint and the back of the thigh.

Trigeminal Neuralgia The trigeminal nerve is the fifth cranial nerve that originates in the brain. Each of these paired nerves divides into three major branches. The first branch is distributed above the eye and in the forehead, extending to the top of the scalp. If this part of the nerve is stimulated, this area will experience pain. The second branch is distributed in the upper jaw and the front part of the face, next to the nose. If this branch of the nerve is stimulated, this area will experience pain. The third branch is distributed in the lower jaw, chin, and side of the face. If this part of the nerve is stimulated, this area will also experience pain.

There are several causes of trigeminal neuralgia: (1) Tertiary syphilis (not every case of tertiary syphilis causes trigeminal neuralgia). (2) Malaria. (3) Anemia. (4) Chronic poisoning, such as diabetes, gout, lead poisoning, and excessive drinking. (5) Overexertion. (6) Prolonged breastfeeding by women. (7) Nerve irritation, such as from teeth, impacted wisdom teeth, or inflammation in the nasal cavity. In addition to any of the above causes, exposure to cold, sudden changes in atmospheric pressure (such as ascending or descending in altitude), nerve stimulation, excessive fatigue, or slight irritation of the area where the nerve is distributed, such as chewing food, talking, yawning, brushing teeth, or washing the face, can easily trigger the nerve pain, or cause an old pain to recur.

The pain comes in waves and is extremely severe. Patients often describe the pain as stabbing, cutting, tearing, or burning. Each episode involves multiple waves of pain. The duration of the episodes can vary from several minutes to several hours, or even several days. After the pain subsides, the patient returns to normal. The longer this condition lasts, the more frequent and intense the pain episodes become.

The best approach to treating this type of pain is to eliminate the underlying cause. For example, treating late-stage syphilis, curing rhinitis, fixing decayed teeth, or extracting impacted wisdom teeth can often provide a permanent solution.

When the pain occurs, the palliative treatment methods are roughly as follows: Internally administered analgesics such as acetanilide, antipyrine, phenacetin, or similar drugs have comparable value. Note that these medications should not be taken for too long, as their effectiveness gradually diminishes and they can harm the body. Avoid using narcotics, as they are highly addictive. Hydrotherapy can be very beneficial. Additionally, nerve-calming medications can also provide some relief.

Arthralgia

Arthralgia is a complex condition. Some cases involve acute inflammatory pain, while others involve chronic inflammatory pain. Chronic cases often linger for years. Most Chinese people with this condition only know to apply plasters to the painful area, without ever inquiring about the cause of the pain. If we understand the cause of arthralgia, we can see that plasters have limited value and are not the proper course of treatment. I will briefly describe the causes of arthralgia below for readers' reference: The main causes of acute arthritis are: (1) Rheumatism, where bacteria multiply in the endocardium and enter the bloodstream, invading the joints and causing arthritis. (2) Gonorrhea (related to leucorrhea in women), where gonococci invade the joints via the blood. (3) Inflammation caused by pneumococci. (4) Pus formation within the joint. (5) Secondary to acute infectious diseases, such as scarlet fever arthritis, endocarditis arthritis, typhoid arthritis, dysentery arthritis, etc. (To be continued)

Common Knowledge on Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Hygiene 194

— Tang Renjin

(47) Acute Otitis Media

Acute otitis media mostly occurs during acute febrile infectious diseases (such as measles, scarlet fever, diphtheria, typhoid fever, influenza, whooping cough, smallpox, pneumonia, erysipelas, etc.) and acute or chronic inflammation of the nasal cavity, paranasal sinuses, nasopharynx, etc. Furthermore, swimming, nasal lavage, intranasal surgery, tympanic membrane injury, etc., can sometimes also cause acute otitis media. The most common bacteria that cause acute otitis media are Streptococcus, Pneumococcus, and Staphylococcus. Sometimes, it is caused by Pseudomonas aeruginosa, Escherichia coli, Diphtheria bacillus, influenza bacillus, typhoid bacillus, and tubercle bacillus, etc. The easiest route of infection is through the Eustachian tube. Clinically, acute otitis media can be divided into two types: acute simple otitis media and acute perforating otitis media. Although these two types have different conditions, their causes are the same. I will now describe their conditions separately as follows:

1. Acute Simple Otitis Media

The main symptom of acute simple otitis media is pain inside the ear. The pain is stabbing and tearing. Mostly intermittent. The ear pain can worsen at night, during coughing, sneezing, swallowing movements, etc. Hearing loss is also a common symptom. At the same time, one often feels fullness in the ear, headache, and pulsating tinnitus. Fever is only more severe in children. Often exceeding 40 degrees Celsius. Sometimes vomiting, dizziness, delirium, stupor, and spasms, etc., similar to the symptoms of meningitis, occur. Sometimes facial nerve palsy and taste disorders occur. If we use an otoscope to examine the tympanic membrane, we will see that the tympanic membrane is congested and swollen.

When this disease goes well, the ear pain can be relieved after about two or three days. At the same time, the exudate accumulated in the tympanic cavity will also gradually be absorbed. After about two weeks, the congestion and swelling of the tympanic membrane can subside and return to normal. However, if encountered with improper treatment, weakness, anemia, adenoid disease, tuberculosis, diabetes, and patients with chronic nasopharyngeal disease, the course of the disease will be prolonged. Even turning into acute perforating otitis media, or chronic catarrhal otitis media. Or secondary mastoiditis with pus. Sometimes it can even lead to meningitis, brain abscess, sepsis, etc., leading to fatal results.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (51) 195

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 11: Complications of Pulmonary Tuberculosis

Section 1: Tuberculous Meningitis (Continued)

How is tuberculous meningitis formed? First, it is due to the invasion of the vascular system, which has been mentioned in the section on acute miliary tuberculosis! The progression through the lymphatic system is also possible: like tuberculous otitis media, which is a good route. In addition, whether the cervical lymph nodes and tonsils are possible is still undecided. In terms of the time of occurrence, it mostly occurs after the initial aggregation of lesions. It is relatively rare in later complete forms. The fact that adults rarely suffer from this disease can be considered as circumstantial evidence!

In Chapter 9, it was mentioned that acute miliary tuberculosis has a meningitic type, and tubercle bacilli can also be detected in the spinal fluid. Then, readers may ask: Is there any difference between them? Or are they completely the same? This cannot be determined solely based on clinical symptoms. We must know that acute miliary tuberculosis is a systemic disease, hence the name "systemic miliary tuberculosis." Unlike tuberculous meningitis, which is a completely localized disease, only the clinical symptoms may sometimes be more pronounced locally! Secondly, acute miliary tuberculosis is entirely formed by the invasion of the vascular system, while tuberculous meningitis is not necessarily. Thirdly, acute miliary tuberculosis has extremely high temperature; temperature rise in tuberculous meningitis is not very high, close to 40 degrees is rarely seen. These are just examples. As to whether they are one disease with two names, I think readers will definitely understand.

Section 2: Pleurisy

Pleurisy, based on its causes, used to be classified into primary and secondary types. Primary pleurisy arises directly from the body itself. Secondary pleurisy is caused by invasion from nearby areas or by the internal transfer of other infectious lesions. However, according to recent studies, this classification is not very appropriate because most cases of primary pleurisy are associated with tuberculous causes. In fact, it tells us that most people who have had pleurisy once will develop tuberculosis later. In addition, in exudative pleurisy, tubercle bacilli can be found in 50% of the exudate. Even the initial tuberculous lesions and infiltrations can have a close relationship with the pleura. Especially in exudative pleurisy, it accounts for almost 95% of cases with tuberculous causes. Based on these facts, so-called primary pleurisy hardly exists. As for the inseparable relationship between tuberculosis and pleurisy, it is even more obvious.

Why does pleurisy occur so easily in patients with pulmonary tuberculosis? We must know that the visceral pleura covers the surface of the lungs. If there is tuberculous infiltration on the lung surface, it can directly invade the pleura. This is the case not only for tuberculosis, but also for pneumonia, pulmonary gangrene, lung abscess, etc. However, it is not as common as in tuberculosis!

Essays

League of Nations Discusses Relief for Russian Women in Shanghai 196

— Xing An

The League of Nations is not only an international political organization, but also seems to be an international charity. In addition to resolving international disputes, it also does some charitable work. A Reuters dispatch from Geneva on the 29th: The League of Nations is now paying attention to the problem of Russian émigrés in Shanghai. According to a report from the Committee on the Traffic in Women and Children, among the 10,000 Russian women in Shanghai, those between the ages of 16 and 45 account for 7,200, of which 22.5% rely on prostitution for a living. The League of Nations is now considering establishing special vocational training centers, affordable restaurants, and hostels to accommodate these helpless women.

Since the success of the Russian Revolution and the establishment of the communist state, a group of White Russians, left over from the imperial era, were unwilling to live under the rule of the Red Army leaders due to differences in ideology. They were forced to leave their homeland and wander around the world, living a stateless existence. Especially for women, their situation is even more miserable and pitiful. According to the League of Nations' investigation, there are as many as 10,000 Russian women drifting in Shanghai. These helpless women, living in a foreign land, with no family property and no occupation, their situation is bound to deteriorate day by day. Among them, 22.5% of young or middle-aged women, driven by this dire life, have to sacrifice their bodies and resort to prostitution to make a living. This is indeed very worthy of our sympathy.

But on second thought, weren't some of these White Russian women drifting abroad enjoying a very leisurely life before the overthrow of imperial Russia, enjoying all the happiness in the world? Their tragic plight today may very well be the result of their past extravagance and licentiousness. This is not an overstatement. However, that is the past. We feel that these White Russian women who were abandoned by their homeland and drifting in a foreign land, living a wandering life, are indeed worthy of people's sympathy. Therefore, we believe that it is a very pleasing thing that the League of Nations is now paying attention to these 10,000 helpless Russian women in Shanghai and is trying to find ways to provide relief to alleviate their plight. Its value is no less than solving an international problem.

White Girls and Others 197

— Li Yi

At the beginning of 1935, the atmosphere of the drama movement was quite strong, but recently, this drama movement, which was once lively, has become silent again. It was not until now that the John Drama Society broke this silent atmosphere.

The plays performed this time were three in total: "The Thief" (one-act play), "White Girl" (two-act play), and "Freedom" (one-act play); in addition, there were some songs and dances and music from the National Conservatory of Music.

When I went, because it was a little late, the "songs and dances" and the one-act play "The Thief" watched by the Nanyang overseas Chinese had already been performed, so I only saw the two plays "White Girl" and "Freedom". Now, let me write down some of my impressions of these two plays below:

It is said that the script of "White Girl" is the work of Mr. Ouyang Yuqian. It has not been performed in Shanghai before, and it was jointly directed by Mr. Ying Yunwei and Mr. Tang Na.

What does "White Girl" tell us? It says that there are two "clowns" who simultaneously fall in love with the "white girl". So they bet, whoever can't tell who is disguised, whoever wins the "white girl", let the winner "have a happy ending". But what is the result? Although the senior brother wins, he sees that the white girl loves his junior brother more than she loves him, so he ends it all with one stroke.

This is a "comedy", a comedy that makes people laugh, but after laughing, we can't find any more significant meaning. If we must find its meaning, it is probably as written in the instructions, let "people who are going to swirl in a love triangle" learn his "admirable spirit" to avoid "suffering losses". If you want to find meaning beyond that, you really can't find it.

In terms of performance, what is admirable is the earnestness and effort of the staff, the kind of persistent and meticulous spirit. In terms of the actors, although there are exaggerated movements or shortcomings, that is because of the lack of stage experience. We can still see their earnest and hardworking spirit.

The original author of the script "Freedom" is John Reed of the United States. It was translated into Chinese by Mr. Qiu Bo and published in the special issue of the sixth volume of "Modern". But unfortunately, until now, I have not read that script.

The play tells the story of four prisoners who want to break out of prison. Among these four prisoners, one is an ironworker, one is a poet, one is a "romantic"—to be more precise, we might as well say he is a mental patient—and the other is a minor offender with great religious faith.

When these four prisoners are planning to escape from prison, the poet is in high poetic spirits. He plans to immediately write a poem praising freedom. The minor offender, because he is old, perhaps because his crime is minor, or because he is anesthetized by religion, does not plan to escape halfway. And that neurotic so-called "romantic," when he discovers that the file and rope ladder made with three years of effort are useless, he also does not escape because it is too easy. As a result, only the worker who yearns for freedom wants to escape, but he is immediately held back by the three "gentlemen," because his escape will harm them?

According to the author's original intention, perhaps it is to satirize the gentlemen. He knows that "it is the worker who roars, and it is only the worker who wants to go out." However, using the prison as a background and writing these four different characters together, it is inevitable to make people feel a sense of fantasy. You think, an action that has been going on for three years, wouldn't you understand the opponent's character beforehand? How can there be a sudden change when the opportunity comes?

In terms of the development of the plot, it also makes people feel that it is too "ideal".

I don't know what the prisons in the United States are like, but after watching "The Fugitive" some time ago, my impression seems to be that it is not much different from China. In this way, I have several questions in this play: (1) In today's prisons, there seem to be no more kerosene lamps and tap lights, especially tap lights. It is said that they are prohibited to prevent prisoners from committing suicide. Although this is supposed to be a light prison cell. (2) Where did the prisoner's pistol come from? (3) Why is that iron-grille window suddenly unlatched? Since you don't need a rope ladder to grab the wall, and there are no sentries, are you really not afraid of the prisoners escaping?

Therefore, even if the author's original intention is not bad, in the development of the plot and things, it is ultimately too "ideal".

In terms of performance, the spirit of hard work and earnestness is worthy of our admiration, but because the progress of the play is too flat and the climax has no power, it cannot grasp the audience's emotions.

The Taste of Life 198

— Simon

He was also stirred by the strangeness to generate inexplicable anger. Since that was the case, he was himself, and his uncle was his uncle. What else was there to say? So he suddenly gathered great courage, opened his eyes, looked at his uncle, and said angrily:

"Whatever, consider it over like this. I will never set foot in your threshold again."

Saying this, he gritted his teeth and rushed out of the door.

On the way, the coffin containing his father's shell might not even have been painted with black ink, but the surrounding environment had rapidly collapsed, and even his uncle, who was so close like family, had become a stranger.

Whenever he thought of this, recalled the situation when he ran to his uncle's house that day, his uncle's iron-faced, gloomy face would suddenly appear in his mind's eye, and the fire of anger would immediately pierce through his brain, and his teeth would grind with a rustling sound. He shook his fist as if he wanted to grab someone.

Then he would say to himself: Hmph, just look down on me. Don't be so smug. Even if I'm so poor that I have to beg for food, I will never ask for your help. Just wait and see, someday.

Then he would mutter to himself like a neurological error.

So his mother would quietly stand in front of him, encouraging and comforting her son:

—There's no need to get angry about these things. People are always like this. It's okay not to rely on others. Just do your own thing and show people what you're capable of.

What his mother said was exactly what he was thinking.

But he always wanted to remember all the glorious scenes of his family in earlier days: At that time, whether it was night or day, guests would come and go like a stream from early in the morning? Every guest had different but the same expectations for the host, so every face was smiling and unusually kind, babbling about this and that. The mouths were unusually sweet and smooth. If they happened to meet the father not at home, or not up yet, he, the young master, would take the place of his father to greet the guests, and all the guests would chat and laugh with him with the same strong interest. The whole house would be constantly noisy with laughter from morning to night, but where have the guests and laughter gone now?

They disappeared at the same time as his father.

The two door knockers that had been heavily and lightly knocked by many people's hands, now can't hear the slightest sound, and are so idle that they almost start to rust. The guests have suddenly become so lonely, letting the boundless emptiness lock them up, as cold and quiet as an ancient temple. Except for himself occasionally coming back from outside, there have been one or two sporadic knocks on the door, otherwise, there is no movement at all.

People have all gone far away from him, including his uncle.

Passing in front of that guest's door, and knowing the past of this family, you will deeply evoke a kind of distant memory and sigh:

"Now it's too lonely!"

Small Pieces of Apartment Life 199

— Xia Yin

(I)

Like a fledgling bird without a nest, flying out of the old nest of freedom, the power of life is constantly and everywhere forcing me into a state of dilapidation and hardship. On a day when the snow melted not far behind the order of the seasons, the storm of life broke my dreams again; so I picked up a small travel bag and a heart full of worldly dust, and the night's speeding train took me to this corner of the building—relying on the warmth of friends, and now it is the season of falling flowers again.

The atmosphere overflowing around here is always so peaceful and quiet, like a blue pool in autumn, proud of the peace of its own life in a satisfied smile. Every morning, a cockcrow awakens the faint dream, facing the light and shadow of the morning sun, the sky is a clear blue, all the fields and vegetables are green, the smoke from the kitchen is faint in the willow forest, with the laughter of birds, and the roses on the bamboo fence are just beginning to bloom. At this time, I usually sit facing the window, squeezing a little bit of the source of life from the tip of the white gold pen. When I am tired of writing, I drink a glass of plain water, and look up at the morning sun, which has risen into the air majestically at some unknown time. I will leisurely yearn for it, celebrating the greatness and arrival of the light, and the reflection makes me feel heartbroken about the terrible state of depression. I will throw away the fountain pen, get up suddenly, and stretch out my arms to shout at the rising sun.

"I want a bright and vigorous future!"

Yes, this apartment life has become so quiet that it has become a state of depression. Living like this, for one's young life, is simply an incurable waste. One must be like the eagle described by Gorky in The Song of the Falcon, yearning for the light, fighting for the light to the point of death. This is ultimately a praiseworthy warrior's behavior.

(II)

It is the season of falling flowers again.

The passage of time cannot help but make people regret the passing of youth.

—Flowers fall and water flows, red, a thousand kinds of idle sorrows. Although these sentimental sentences of ancient poets and lyricists will not slip from my own pen, when the roses on the trellis are removed, and the purple petals are one by one, it also makes me feel that such a young force is dormant in a corner of the building, and another spring has silently disappeared. The hidden pain and anxiety in the center are enough for a sleepless night.

—What are you waiting for?

Although the cuckoo can't stop the spring that is about to return, spring will come again next year; but the gone years will never come back!

The atmosphere of the plum rain season will be even more dull and suffocating. After this, it will be the scorching summer.

Page 19

Life 200

— Hua Mu

Life is a stone, heavy with a thousand pounds weighing on your shoulders; life is also a rugged narrow road, stretching endlessly under your feet, unless you swallow your last breath and fall, this endless narrow road will never be finished. Originally, a person's life is so fragile, it is not difficult to cut off a breath in a snap with a convenient and tragic method. However, God's bestowal of intelligence to mankind is very stingy; foolishness ultimately weaves the brains of most people, and although the current life is heavy and difficult, one cannot easily fall: even at the last moment when the vigor of life is exhausted to the point of inevitable collapse, there is still a final struggle of fading glory, filled with helpless resentment and lingering affection for the world. This is the extreme peak of human sorrow, and also the strong endowment of human beings' desire for life.

If this statement is the explanation of life, then Hou Awang is a pitiful person who uses this foolish brain to bear a heavy and difficult life.

Hou Awang is no different from ordinary people, he needs to eat and wear clothes; it's just that he was born a bit short, and it seems because of this shortness, he can only be a petty tailor in his life. His father was originally a farmer, but because he didn't want his son to endure this hard life, he sent him to a tailor shop in the city as an apprentice when his son was twelve years old. The father had great hopes for his son. From apprentice to master, from master to boss, after that he could put down the hoe, hold his dry tobacco pipe and enjoy life in the shop. Unfortunately, the year his son finished his apprenticeship, his old man passed away with regret, leaving Hou Awang to become a helpless outcast.

At that time, Awang had just turned twenty. Although eight years of apprenticeship had worn away his youthful vigor, he always showed a shy and humble appearance in front of people, but beautiful dreams of the future were still woven in his heart, constantly encouraging him and guiding him, so that he could still believe that his youth could easily create a good future; he understood that the Hou family's ancestral line had to rely entirely on him to continue, so, in the pile of needles and threads, he buried his head, silently anticipating the unfolding of the future, crawling like a snail on the line of life.

Endless years passed like lightning, wrinkles had ruthlessly smeared the corners of his eyes and forehead, a pair of reading glasses was perched on the bridge of his nose, and two meager whiskers grew on his mouth, the disillusionment of hope made him more silent, humble, and awkward, he was already a forty-five-year-old man. However, it was also in the spring of that year, perhaps his peach blossom luck had arrived, that after three nights of hesitation, he unconditionally adopted a pregnant woman who was both mute and had a kicking leg, the light of hope flickered in his heart again, he seemed to become more alive, he had a wife.

Half a year passed, and this mute wife did indeed give him a monkey-like little thing. At that time, he could truly taste the joy of life, and that day he devoutly kowtowed nine times in the ancestral hall, and tears flowed down uncontrollably.

However, his physical strength was ultimately insufficient, his old-fashioned tailoring was no longer appreciated, and people gradually forgot about him. Because he couldn't find work, the burden on his shoulders became heavier than before, besides his own mouth, there were two more hungry bellies to feed, and he suddenly fell into a mud pit.

Therefore, after the news of "Hou Awang stealing sweet potatoes" spread throughout the village one night, people would never forget to snort behind his back, mocking him.

——He doesn't even have the ability to support himself, yet he wants to support a wife and have a son? Hmph, he'd be better off dying early, why live and suffer?

News 202

Since the old machine of Huaxing Radio Station stopped broadcasting, listeners have been calling day and night to request a way to restore broadcasting. The new machine has now been modified and completed. After inspection by the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, the results were deemed excellent, and it has officially started broadcasting on the 11th. The Chinese Harmonica World, published by the Chinese Harmonica Music Weekly, has been striving for innovation since its publication. The content and layout have been fully in Chinese characters from the third issue onwards. This issue is a special issue dedicated to sending off the Dahua Harmonica Quintet to the Soviet Union. The content includes a short history of the quintet members, changes in the Suzhou harmonica community, a detailed program list of the Dahua concert, the music score of the "Wedding March" played at the conference, and practical harmonica repair methods. All newspaper vendors and Shanghai Magazine Company sell it. Out-of-town readers can subscribe for the whole year for one yuan, including postage. For a trial reading, send two cents for postage to the promotion department of the Kaimei Glasses Store on the second floor of the Old North Gate in Shanghai.

Li Shude Hall pays great attention to educational programs. Textbooks have now been compiled for English, French, shorthand, and other subjects, and daily broadcasts are scheduled. English is taught from 7:00 AM to 7:45 AM, and Chinese shorthand is taught from 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM in the afternoon. The above textbooks are all practical. It is said that there will be a second and third volume of the textbooks in the future, which are currently being edited. The textbooks are all sold by Mr. Zhou Fenglin of the station.

Fengming Advertising Agency, Jingkun, the director of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration's voice station, and Mr. Yuan Fengxing, the director of the Central Research Radio Station of the Great World, recently wanted to popularize broadcasting audiences and promote the development of the broadcasting industry, so they launched Fengming Weekly. The content includes the detailed program list of this radio station, opening articles, and various essays and literary pieces, which are very exciting. A certain gentleman and others are specially invited to be assistant editors. It is said that it will be published soon. Those who want a trial reading can send a letter with postage after publication.

Movie News

Lianhua News 203

In "Four Sisters," Liang Saizhu carries a bamboo basket to buy vegetables, with a small cloth skirt tied around her waist. Han Chugen acted in the same scene, thin and wearing clothes that were too big. So someone said, "One long gown of Lao Han's can make ten cloth skirts for Saizhu."

Sun Yu adapted the famous British stage play "The Admirable Crichton" into "Go to Nature." He once declared to people a few days ago: "My 'Go to Nature' is not advocating a nude movement."

Wu Yonggang, the director of "Little Angel," instructed the props department to buy 300 pens that day. It is said that these 300 pens were all used by Ge Zuo Zhi alone.

Gu Menghu took "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp" to the prison. The prison gate was actually shot on location. After the filming of Menghu entering the prison was completed, a coffin was just transported out. The director smiled and patted Menghu on the shoulder and said, "Congratulations, old brother, you've been promoted and made a fortune."

Wang Renmei played a "good sister" in "Little Angel."

When Fei Paiqing was filming "Four Sisters," a press photographer asked him what role he played. He said, "Like Hong Shuling, I haven't played a good person in the play."

Chen Yanyan suffered a lot in her performance in "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River." Recently, she has been filming rain scenes for days, wearing soaking wet clothes every day.

Yuan Muzhi and Tan Ying in "Children of the Storm."

Mr. Wang's Chinese New Year Snippets 204

Director Tang Jie's films have always been known for their speed, but directing Mr. Wang's Chinese New Year took six months for the sake of careful consideration, so his directing skills and techniques have achieved amazing results.

Since joining the film industry, writers Cao Xuesong and Zuo Ming have written many screenplays, but "Mr. Wang's Chinese New Year" is the best. This film is truly the representative work of Cao and Zuo.

"Mr. Wang's Chinese New Year" has a serious consciousness, rich jokes, and 100% realistic themes, which is especially commendable. It exposes the darkness of society and economic oppression with laughter, anger, and revelation.

In the acting of "Mr. Wang's Chinese New Year," Tang Jie's Mr. Wang has reached the pinnacle of perfection, and Cao Xuesong's Little Chen has also made a lot of progress compared to before. Huang Naishuang and others also have extremely careful performances, coupled with the cameo appearances of Xu Zili and You Guangzhao, which makes it even more icing on the cake.

Songstress Under the Iron Heel Recorded into a Record 205

"Songstress Under the Iron Heel," sung by Wang Renmei in "Children of the Storm," the debut work directed by Xu Xingzhi of the Diantong Company, has the same artistic effect as "Fisherman's Song." The song was written by the director and composed by Mr. Nie Er. It has now been collected by Baidai Company as record number 34848 and is now on sale in the market.

The second comic masterpiece produced by New Era Company, "Mr. Wang's Chinese New Year," was officially released at the Xin Guang Grand Theater yesterday.

Cheng Bu Gao's "National Soul" group has a scene where a cannonball destroys a dance hall, which is extremely exciting.

The Cultural Film Company and the newly established Yuyi Film Company have similar arts and have interrelated relationships with Xinhua.

While the Mingxing Company is moving locations one after another, it continues filming. However, Dong Tianya is extremely busy, having to take care of moving locations and scenery, but he handles it as usual, which is admirable.

It is said that "Nostalgia," directed by Shen Xiling, has been edited and completed. The directors of Mingxing all unanimously praised it, and the audience is looking forward to the performance period.

It is said that Yucheng Film Production Company will be entirely transferred to Mingxing Company around the end of May or the beginning of June.

Introduction to the Second Issue of Silver Kingdom 207

The second issue of "Silver Kingdom" film monthly has been published. The cover is a smile of Xu Suzhi, and the back cover is Tang Jie of New Era's "Mr. Wang." The content is extremely rich, with a total of five special features. "The Works of Film People" includes Ye Qiuxin, Xu Suzhen, Yuan Meiyun, Lu Lingxia, etc. "Impressions of Artists" includes Shen Xiling, Gao Lihen, Wu Cun, Zheng Yingshi, etc. "Photo Supplement" contains 20 photos of movie stars and films. The "New Song Introduction" introduces songs such as "Sunny Day" from "Returning" and "Xiang Lei" from "Elegy of Life." "Cartoons Under Scissors" includes Li Lili, Wang Moqiu, Li Minghui, etc. The layout is also extremely novel and beautiful. The entire book is printed in fine Song typeface. Each copy retails for five cents. It is distributed by Shanghai Magazine Company, 32 Sima Road, Shanghai. The subscription for the whole year is six corners, and half a year is three corners. Subscription address: Silver Kingdom Publishing House, No. 1 Renchang Lane, Kaizi Road, Shanghai.

"Hell Divers" is a full scale authentic demonstration of all phases of latest combat tactics in the air by the U.S. Army Air Corps personnel. Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer's newest and greatest air thriller featuring Wallace Beery, Maureen O'Sullivan, Robert Young, Lewis Stone, etc. It is a work that movie fans should definitely include on their must-see film list and is now playing at the Nanjing Grand Theater.
